# PART 3: LEADS — Capturing + Warming

> **Growth OS Brain — Part 3 of 7**
> Sources: Alex Hormozi ($100M Playbooks), Jeremy Haynes (21 transcripts), Nik Setting (22 transcripts), SooWei Goh (17 transcripts), Ben Bader (21 transcripts)
> Sabbo Application: Amazon Coaching ($3K–$10K programs) + Agency ($5K–$25K/mo retainers)

---

## Overview

Leads are only valuable when they show up and are pre-sold. This section covers the full lifecycle from the moment someone raises their hand to the moment they sit across from your closer on a call: lead magnets that attract, nurture sequences that warm, setter operations that qualify and book, webinars and challenge funnels that convert at scale, and proof systems that eliminate sales resistance before the call begins.

**The core insight driving everything in Part 3:**

> "80% of the conversion needs to happen in the marketing. 20% needs to happen in the sales process. Right now, it's the opposite for most people." — Nik Setting

Every system below exists to move that ratio in the right direction.

---

## SECTION 3.1 — LEAD MAGNETS

**Root: Alex Hormozi / $100M Leads Playbook**

---

### Framework

A lead magnet is a mini offer: a complete solution to a narrow problem that simultaneously reveals the need for your core offer. The job is not to give away your best content. The job is to prove competence while creating a gap — showing the prospect what is possible while making clear they need your help to close the distance.

Hormozi identifies **three types** and **four delivery methods**.

---

### The Three Types of Lead Magnets

**Type 1: Reveal a Problem**
Show the prospect a problem they did not know they had, or a dimension of a problem they had not fully understood. This creates urgency without you having to manufacture it artificially.

- Agency example: "Free Growth Audit" — Sabbo reviews a founder's acquisition setup live. Every gap revealed is a reason to hire an operator.
- Amazon example: "Free Account Health Audit" — scan their Amazon account, show what's costing them margin, conversion, or velocity.

**Type 2: Free Trial / Sample**
Give them a taste of the actual product. The free version is genuine and valuable. Its job is to make them want more.

- Agency example: "7-Day Growth Dashboard" — Sabbo sends a founder a custom KPI tracking sheet pre-configured for their business model.
- Amazon example: "7-Day Deal Alert Trial" — send actual sourced deals for 7 days. Real deals, real data. After 7 days, the feed stops unless they enroll.

**Type 3: One Step of Many**
Give them step 1 of a multi-step system. It works. It produces a real result. But it naturally makes them want steps 2 through 10.

- Agency example: "The Traffic Audit Template" — step 1 of the 8-step Growth OS installation.
- Amazon example: "The 5-Step Sourcing Checklist" — step 1 (product criteria framework). Steps 2–5 require coaching.

---

### The Four Delivery Methods

| Method | Description | Best For |
|---|---|---|
| **Software / Tools** | Dashboards, trackers, calculators, templates | B2B (founders, operators) |
| **Information** | Guides, checklists, frameworks, video trainings | Both offers |
| **Services** | Free audit, done-for-you sample, consultation | High-ticket entry points |
| **Physical Products** | Books, printed reports, swag | Large-scale lead gen at events |

For Sabbo's offers, the primary delivery methods are **Services** (audit format) and **Information** (framework/checklist format).

---

### Naming Formulas (Critical — Test the Name More Than the Content)

Hormozi's research: the name of the lead magnet determines engagement more than its content. Split-test the headline. Use these formulas:

**Formula 1: Number + Outcome + Timeframe**
- "3 Emails That Turn Cold Leads Into Agency Clients in 24 Hours"
- "5 Amazon Deals I Found This Week with 30%+ ROI"

**Formula 2: How to [Good Thing] Without [Bad Thing] Even If [Insecurity]**
- "How to Build a Repeatable Acquisition Engine Without Hiring a Marketing Team Even If You've Never Run Paid Ads"
- "How to Find Profitable Amazon Products Without Guessing Even If You Have No Amazon Experience"

**Formula 3: Adjective + Type + Good Thing**
- "The Lazy Founder's Growth Audit That Reveals Your #1 Revenue Leak in 20 Minutes"
- "The Fast Sourcing Template That Finds Profitable Products in Under an Hour"

**Formula 4: X Mistakes Preventing [Goal]**
- "5 Acquisition Mistakes That Are Preventing Your Business From Scaling Past $1M/Month"
- "3 Amazon FBA Mistakes That Keep Beginners Under $3K/Month"

---

### Lead Magnet SOP

1. **Choose your type** — Reveal a problem (highest urgency) for cold traffic; Free trial for warm traffic; One step of many for referral or organic audiences
2. **Choose your delivery method** — Match to your ICP. Founders want services (audits). Beginners want information (guides).
3. **Name it** — Write 5 variations using the formulas above. Pick the one that would make you want to click it. That is the control. Test the rest against it.
4. **Build the gap** — At the end of every lead magnet, there must be a natural next step. Do not leave it open. The last sentence should make the gap viscerally real.
5. **Gate it properly** — Ask for first name + email at minimum. Add one qualifying question if the lead quality matters more than volume. ("What is your current monthly revenue?" for agency leads. "How much capital do you have available?" for Amazon leads.)
6. **Track it** — Every lead magnet gets its own UTM link. Know which one drives which quality of lead, not just which one drives volume.

---

> **SABBO APPLICATION — Lead Magnets**
>
> **Agency OS (Growth Agency):**
> - Primary: "Free 20-Minute Growth Audit" (service delivery, reveals problem, creates urgency)
> - Secondary: "The Growth Engine Scorecard" (information, 1-page self-assessment, shows the gap)
> - CTA: "Book your audit → Walk away with your #1 acquisition leak identified and a fix"
>
> **Amazon OS (Amazon Coaching):**
> - Primary: "7-Day Deal Alert Trial" (free trial delivery, builds dependency, filters for action-takers)
> - Secondary: "The 3-Step Product Sourcing Checklist" (information, step 1 of the 5-step system)
> - CTA: "Get 7 real sourced deals delivered to your inbox → See exactly what profitable products look like before you invest a dollar"
>
> **Pricing:** Both lead magnets are free. The agency audit requires a 20-minute call (which is also a qualification step). The Amazon trial requires an email opt-in and one qualifying question about available capital.

---

## SECTION 3.2 — LEAD NURTURE

**Root: Alex Hormozi / $100M Playbook — Lead Nurture**

---

### Framework

Lead nurture is what happens after someone raises their hand but before they show up to buy. Hormozi's ALAN software analyzed over 1 million rows of appointment data and found four drivers of whether a lead shows up. These are not best practices — they are statistically proven correlations.

**The Four Pillars of Lead Nurture:**

1. **Availability** — The more appointment slots you have, the higher the show rate
2. **Speed** — The faster you contact a lead after they opt in, the more likely they schedule and show
3. **Personalization** — The more relevant your follow-up, the more likely they show up ready to buy
4. **Volume** — The more times you reach out before giving up, the more likely they respond

**The throughput math:**
- 100 leads → 50% schedule rate → 50 scheduled → 50% show rate → 25 shows → 25% throughput
- Improve show rate by 20% → 60 shows → 60% throughput — nearly 2.5x the output from the same leads

A 20–40% increase in show rate = 2x to 3x the profit of your business in year one.

---

### Pillar 1: Availability

Make it effortless for leads to book, and make slots available within 72 hours.

**Rules:**
- Take appointments 7 days a week (40% more availability vs. 5-day schedule)
- Offer time slots every 15 minutes instead of every 30 or 60 (4x the flexibility)
- Always have same-day, next-day, and day-after slots available
- Offer inbound calling, outbound calling, AND self-scheduling (three paths to booking)

**Online scheduler must-haves:**
1. Header confirms they are in the right place ("Book Your Free Amazon Sourcing Call")
2. Available times visible immediately on page load — no scrolling required
3. Pre-fill every field that was already collected in the lead form
4. Mobile-optimized (most leads are on phones)

**Adding friction when lead quality is low:**
- Add a video they must watch before the scheduler appears
- Add a price disclosure above the scheduler
- Add qualifying questions before revealing the calendar

---

### Pillar 2: Speed to Contact

**The statistics:**
- 391% increase in conversion when leads are contacted within 60 seconds (Velocify)
- 7x more likely to qualify a lead contacted within 1 hour vs. 2 hours (HBR)
- 60x more likely to qualify vs. 24-hour response (HBR)
- 78% of customers buy from the first company to respond (Lead Connect)

**The litmus test:** If you are not hearing "wow, that was fast!" at least once per day, you are not fast enough.

**Three speed levers:**
1. Speed to first contact: Contact every lead within 5 minutes. Gold standard: 60 seconds.
2. Speed to first appointment: Book within 72 hours. Push for same-day when possible.
3. Speed of response: After they schedule, respond to their messages within minutes — not hours. Every slow response erodes confidence in your operation.

---

### Pillar 3: Personalization

**Six methods:**

**Method 1: Use their preferred communication channel**
Start everywhere (text, email, DM, call). Continue where they respond. Get them to phone, video, or in-person eventually.

**Method 2: Qualify leads through applications**
Before the call, have every lead fill out an application. Score leads 1–5 (red/yellow/green). Route best leads to best closers. Cancel appointments with clear misfits.

**Method 3: Send best leads to best closers**
The #1 timeshare sales rep convinced his CEO to give him the best leads. He 5x'd his office's production. They rolled it out nationally. Company went from $200M to $1B/year.

**Method 4: Segment messaging**
5 minutes of pre-call research before any contact. Personalize the first message. Example:
> "Hey Greg, I see that your site traffic is down 18% this quarter. We had another client in a similar situation — they're now up 100% 90 days later. I prepped a walkthrough to show how we'd apply the same principles to your business."

**Method 5: Incentivize showing up**
- Push incentive (give before the call, no strings): Gift card with text "I just sent you a $5 gift card so you're caffeinated for our call tomorrow." Works via reciprocity even when they know what you're doing.
- Pull incentive (A/B choice that assumes they'll show): "Since you're a first-time client, I'm setting aside two options for you. Would you want the campaign audit report or the conversion analysis?" They choose → they show up to get it.

**Method 6: Personalized proof**
Send testimonials and case studies that match the lead's demographics, business type, revenue level, and specific pain. Match the proof to the person, not to the offer.
> "After they ghost, every 90 days — show them results of people who signed up when they ghosted. Makes them feel left behind but gives them the option to make up for lost time." — Hormozi

---

### Pillar 4: Volume (The First-Week Cadence)

**The core truth:** 44% of salespeople stop after the first attempt. Nearly nobody follows up enough.

**Day 1 (immediately after opt-in):**
1. Call within 5 minutes of lead coming in
2. Double-dial (immediate second call if first goes to voicemail — many phones let the second call through)
3. Leave voicemail if no answer
4. Send text immediately after voicemail
5. Call and text two more times that day, spaced 3–4 hours apart

**Days 2–3:**
- Call twice per day (once earlier, once later)
- Text after the second call each day

**Days 4–7:**
- Call and text once per day

**After day 7:** Transition to long-term nurture (free value + soft CTA to re-engage every 90 days)

**Automated reminders (after appointment is booked):**
1. Immediately: Confirmation with time, date, area code you'll be calling from, person they're meeting with
2. 24 hours before: "Reply YES to confirm"
3. 12 hours before: Reminder with any pre-call homework
4. 3 hours before: Final reminder

**Manual reminders (from a real cell phone, in addition to automated):**
1. Night before (6 PM): Personal text with a probing question
2. Morning of (8 AM): Short check-in
3. 60 minutes before: Final confirmation

**Manual reminder format (Hormozi):**
Send multiple short messages in a row — how real people actually text. Open with a probing question based on what you know about them. Once they respond, compliment them, ask the next question. Use this to pull the appointment forward if possible.

**BAMFAM — Book A Meeting From A Meeting (from Sharran Srivatsaa):**
Never end a call without booking the next one. "We'll circle back" = they will never circle back. The moment they are on the phone with you is the moment booking is most likely. Pull up the calendar. Pick the time. Do it now.

---

### The Hammer Them Strategy

**Root: Jeremy Haynes — Concentrated Messaging**

The Hammer Them Strategy is the paid-ads version of lead nurture. It is deployed on people who have already booked a call (or registered for a webinar) to compress months of organic content consumption into 2–3 days through paid distribution.

**The theory (Concentrated Messaging):**
It normally takes a prospect 5 months of organic content consumption to build enough trust to buy. The Hammer Them campaign compresses that to 2–3 days by showing them a high volume of your best content, on repeat, through retargeting ads — before they ever sit across from your closer.

**The Trust Hour Rule:** You need approximately one hour of meaningful content consumption before a high-ticket purchase decision. The Hammer Them campaign accumulates those trust hours across many short touchpoints.

**Minimum content volume required:**
- 30–50 short-form content pieces (60–90 seconds each)
- 15–30 long-form content pieces (10–30 minutes each)

This is not optional. Below these volumes, the concentration effect does not take hold.

**The 4 Content Quadrants (what to create):**
1. **Common questions from sales calls** — What do leads actually ask when they get on a call?
2. **Common objections** — What stops them from saying yes?
3. **Expectations for success** — What should they expect if they enroll?
4. **Second-order questions** — Questions that arise after the first questions are answered

**Deployment triggers:**
- After someone books a sales call (standard)
- After someone registers for a webinar (pre-show warm-up)
- After someone buys a low-ticket product (pre-upsell)

**The Tornado:** When all Hammer Them campaigns are deployed simultaneously at ALL funnel stages. Maximum saturation. This is Jeremy's most aggressive deployment and is reserved for periods of heavy scaling.

**Setup:**
1. Build retargeting audience: people who booked a call but have not yet had it
2. Create a custom audience in Meta: application form completions (confirmed appointments only)
3. Assign your 30–50 short-form + 15–30 long-form pieces to this audience
4. Run at a small daily budget ($20–$50/day per audience) — the goal is frequency, not reach
5. These people should be seeing your face 3–5 times per day across multiple formats

**Why this compounds:**
Show rate improvement alone from deploying Hammer Them typically pays for the ad spend within the first week. At a 40% close rate, getting 10 extra shows per month from better pre-call warming = 4 extra deals. At $5K average deal = $20K additional revenue. Ad spend: under $500.

---

### Pixel Conditioning

**Root: Jeremy Haynes — Unique to him**

Pixel Conditioning is the deliberate process of training ad platform algorithms by controlling which conversion events fire. Most advertisers pollute their pixel with unqualified leads. Jeremy's system ensures the algorithm only sees data from qualified, financially-capable prospects — which trains it to find more people like them.

**The Four Rules:**

**Rule 1: Only pixel qualified leads**
Disqualified applicants (those who fail the application) never reach the confirmation page. The pixeled confirmation page is only accessible after passing qualification. Result: every pixel event is a qualified lead.

**Rule 2: State the price in the VSL**
People who convert after seeing the price are financially pre-qualified. The algorithm learns to find more people who are financially qualified. Never hide the price. Say it early. This is not just good sales practice — it is algorithm training.

**Rule 3: Never pixel the drop-sell page**
The drop-sell page (shown to disqualified applicants, offering a lower-priced alternative) must never fire a conversion event to the main pixel. Firing unqualified conversion events on the drop-sell page degrades the algorithm's targeting quality over time.

**Rule 4: Use IQ-based / qualifying application questions**
Questions that only genuinely qualified buyers can answer correctly serve as a pre-pixel filter. They simultaneously qualify the lead and produce higher-quality pixel events.

**Application questions that qualify by intelligence and capability (not just willingness):**

Agency:
- "What is your current monthly revenue?"
- "What percentage of revenue comes from paid acquisition?"
- "What is your current customer acquisition cost?"
- "Describe your current acquisition funnel in one sentence."

Amazon:
- "How much capital do you have available to invest in inventory?"
- "Have you already registered a Seller Central account?"
- "What is your timeline to generate your first revenue?"
- "What is the primary reason you have not scaled your Amazon business yet?"

---

> **SABBO APPLICATION — Lead Nurture**
>
> **For both offers, deploy these systems in order:**
>
> 1. **Speed system:** Automate a text and email within 60 seconds of any opt-in. Automate a booking link in that first message. Personal call within 5 minutes from a real number with a local area code.
>
> 2. **First-week cadence:** Day 1: 3 contact attempts. Days 2–3: 2/day. Days 4–7: 1/day. No exceptions. This is the system. The system is only effective when it is run exactly.
>
> 3. **Automated reminder sequence:** Configure your CRM (GoHighLevel, Close, or similar) to send: (a) booking confirmation immediately, (b) 24-hour reminder requesting a YES reply, (c) 12-hour reminder with pre-call homework, (d) 3-hour reminder.
>
> 4. **Manual reminder sequence:** Set a task in your CRM for: (a) night-before text from your personal iPhone, (b) morning-of text, (c) 60-minutes-before text. These must come from a real number, not an automated system.
>
> 5. **Hammer Them Campaign (activate once you have enough content):**
>    - Agency leads: 30 short-form pieces addressing growth systems, acquisition, and operator model
>    - Amazon leads: 30 short-form pieces addressing sourcing, profitability math, and student results
>    - Target: anyone who has booked a call in the last 14 days
>    - Budget: $30/day per audience, every day the pipeline is active
>
> 6. **Pixel conditioning:** Never let unqualified leads reach your confirmation page. Use qualifying application questions for both offers. State price ranges early in every VSL. Never run conversion ads without first ensuring your pixel is fed only qualified events.

---

## SECTION 3.3 — SETTER / DM SYSTEM

**Root: Nik Setting — 50/50/50 KPIs, opener philosophy**
**Setter Onboarding: SooWei Goh — 48-hour training + quiz gate**

---

### Framework

The setter is the bridge between a lead and a sales call. Their job is not to sell. Their job is to qualify, warm, and book. The quality of the setter operation determines the quality of the pipeline more than almost any other variable.

Nik Setting's data from Machi (his proprietary DM management software): changing a DM opener from a low-performing one to a high-performing one increased reply rates from 6% to 29.4% — effectively 5x-ing the pipeline with zero additional ad spend.

---

### The 50/50/50 KPI Framework

**Root: Nik Setting**

Every setter must hit these daily KPIs:
- **50 messages to new followers** — cold outbound to new audience members
- **50 messages to old followers** — warm outbound to existing audience who has not yet been engaged
- **50 follow-ups** — re-engagement of prior conversations that stalled

**Track daily per setter:**
- Inbound DMs received
- Outbound DMs sent (new + warm)
- Active conversations
- Calendly/booking links sent
- Calls booked

---

### Opener Philosophy

**Root: Nik Setting**

The opener's ONLY job is to get a response. Not to build trust. Not to explain the offer. Not to generate interest. Just to get the first reply.

This requires a yes/no question or a question so easy to answer that friction is near-zero.

**Bad openers (open-ended, high friction):**
- "Why do you want to start an agency? Tell me everything."
- "What are your business goals?"
- "I'd love to learn more about your situation."

**Good openers (binary, low friction, easy to answer):**
- "Is the current bottleneck in your business clarity on how to start, or lead generation?"
- "Are you selling on Amazon right now, or are you pre-launch?"
- "Quick question — are you currently happy with how your acquisition is running?"
- "Is the main challenge getting leads in, or converting the ones you're already getting?"

The binary question forces a choice. Either answer moves the conversation forward and tells you something about where they are. There is no "I don't know" or "Not sure what you mean."

**Additional opener frameworks from the source material:**

For Amazon coaching (from DM Setting Breakdown):
> "Hey, what's up. Thank you for reaching out. Just have a few quick questions to see if we can help out. Obviously, you came from the story we just posted. Looks like you want to learn how to sell on Amazon. Do you work right now or what's the main reason you're looking to do so?"

For growth/business coaching:
> "Is the current bottleneck in your business the clarity on how to start, or the lead generation?"

For warm outbound (Nik Setting):
> Pre-qualify by checking profile (has content? has a business? demographic fit?). New followers: send to YouTube video (nurture first, book second). Old followers who have seen your content: engage directly with a booking-oriented conversation.

---

### The Full DM Qualification Framework

**Root: DM Setting Breakdown (from Hormozi Docx extractions)**

The goal: qualify on commitment, urgency, and resources (money) in as few messages as possible. You need three things confirmed before sending the booking link:
1. **Commitment** — Do they actually want this?
2. **Urgency** — Is now the time?
3. **Resources** — Can they afford it?

**The Amazon coaching example (complete script):**

*Prospect DMs keyword "AMAZON"*

**Setter:** Hey, what's up — thank you for reaching out. Just a few quick questions to see if we can help out. Looks like you want to learn how to sell on Amazon — do you work right now, or what's the main reason you're looking to do this?

**[Prospect answers — working 9-5, wants to leave]**

**Setter:** Gotcha. Is the main goal to leave the 9-5? If so, how much would you need to be making to actually do that?

**[Prospect answers — needs $5K/mo]**

**Setter:** Got it. How long have you been wanting to leave? And have you tried anything to make money online yet?

**[Prospect answers — tried Amazon on own, didn't work, been wanting to leave for 2 years]**

**Setter:** Got it. If this has been a goal for 2 years, what actually makes it important now? Can I ask?

**[Prospect answers — tired of corporate world]**

**Setter:** Heard ya. Well honestly, sounds like we can help from this brief chat. Obviously this is a mentorship — and I know you don't know all the details yet — but let's say this program was exactly what you needed to leave your job. Do you have $6K–$12K USD to invest? Want to see if I can help.

**[Prospect confirms yes]**

**Setter:** Perfect. We can get you on a longer call over Zoom with one of our coaches for a deeper dive to see if we can 100% help. Here's the link to book a call if you're willing and wanting to. All I ask is that you choose a time you're 100% good for and will be in a distraction-free area. [Send link] Just drop me a quick confirmation when you book, and what time you chose.

**[Prospect books and confirms]**

**Setter:** Perfect. I'll have [closer name] reach out with the next steps and what you need to do to prepare for that call.

---

### Setting Scripts (Phone)

**Root: Setting Scripts (from Hormozi Docx extractions)**

**Script 1 — Inbound (call within 5 minutes of opt-in):**

> "Hey [NAME], how are you? It's [Setter name] from [Business name] — [Offer owner] wanted me to reach out. The reason I'm calling is I see you recently downloaded the [lead magnet name]. What was it that really stuck out and made you want to check it out?"

[Let them answer]

> "Gotcha. And what's the goal here — what were you actually looking to achieve by looking into [business model / offer]?"

[Let them answer — this is the North Star]

> "For sure. And how does that compare to where you are now? Like, where are we starting from, just so I can see how far down the track we are?"

[Let them answer — this is the Gap]

> "And is this something you're looking at doing now to get to [their goal], or is this more of a maybe, could be, would-be-down-the-line kind of thing?"

[If NOW → go to booking pitch. If LATER → do not fill the calendar with tire-kickers. Nurture and reschedule.]

**Booking pitch:**

> "It's up to you from here. What we can do — if you're willing and wanting — is book in a deeper conversation to show you exactly what we do, how we do it, and show you how we might be able to get you to [outcome] just like we do for all our other students. Is that something you'd be willing and wanting to put in the calendar over the next couple of days, or how do you feel?"

**Financial qualifying (always ask, say it with confidence):**

> "And one last thing — so we can best help you get from Point A to Point B, with Point A being where you are now at [current situation] and Point B being [their goal], we really need to know where you're at financially... so with that said, how much total capital do you have available to go all-in on this right now?"

Stay here and ask uncomfortable follow-up questions until you get the truth. Do not accept vague answers.

**Script 2 — Outbound (calling warm leads who attended webinar or filled out a form):**

> "Hey, is this [Name]? [Tone: curious but certain] This is [Setter] from [Business]. I see you [attended our webinar / filled out a form to speak with our team / booked a call]. Does that ring a bell?"

> "Cool. Do you have like 3–5 minutes to chat, just to see if we can help out?"

> "What actually caught your attention and made you want to [reach out / attend / book]?"

[If vague: "Gotcha — what specifically about it caught your attention?"]

> "And just so I'm clear — what's the long-term goal? Is it to do this on the side, transition out of your job, something else entirely?"

> "What does an average month look like financially right now?" [Say this confidently. If pushback: "Not a problem — just to see if this makes sense for you. We don't want to put you on a longer call if you can't pull the trigger yet."]

> "And how long have you wanted [their goal]?"

> "What have you tried over the past [time period] to get there?"

[If they've tried and failed: "Any reason you think it didn't work?" — this surfaces commitment level]

> "Well, what specifically makes this important now rather than pushing it off another [time period]?"

[If they give a strong enough reason: move to booking. If weak: challenge gently but do not force. Low-commitment leads waste closers' time.]

**Booking confirmation tie-down:**

> "Awesome. What time works tomorrow to chat with one of our coaches — it'll be a deeper dive into your situation to see if we can help out. Does morning or afternoon work better?"

> "And nothing will come up making you miss this, right — maybe besides Godzilla coming to town?"

> "Cool. What I'll do from here is make a group chat between you and our coach, and I'll send over a few videos and some homework before the call. Just make sure you go through them before you jump on — sound good?"

> "And I'll confirm over text tomorrow morning. Take 2 seconds to reply when I do — sound good? Great, pleasure talking to you."

---

### Setter Onboarding

**Root: SooWei Goh — 48-hour training + quiz gate**

The most expensive mistake in setter operations is deploying an undertrained setter. An undertrained setter books unqualified calls (wasting closers' time), fails to pre-warm leads (reducing show rates), and creates bad first impressions (damaging brand trust).

**SooWei's 48-hour onboarding protocol:**

**Phase 1 — Training (first 48 hours):**
1. Complete full appointment setting course (5+ hours, 14+ lessons)
2. Complete advanced DM setting module (1 hour)
3. Complete phone setting and triage module
4. Review full offer documentation (offer structure, pricing, ICP, common objections, student results)
5. Watch Loom walkthroughs of all CRM and tracking systems

**Phase 2 — Testing (end of 48 hours):**
1. Quiz on all material — must score 90%+ in maximum 2 attempts. If they fail twice, they are not ready.
2. Niche-specific mock call with the head coach or a senior team member
3. Head coach approves or rejects based on mock call quality

No setter goes live until they pass both the quiz and the mock call.

**Phase 3 — KPI alignment:**
Before their first day, show them the math explicitly:

> "Our goal is $100K/month. To do that, we need 10 closes. We close at 40%, which means 25 qualified calls. We book at 85% show rate, so we need 29 booked calls. We convert 20% of new conversations to qualified calls. So we need 147 new conversations per week. That's on you to generate — here's what 50/50/50 per day means in that context."

When the setter can see how their daily KPIs connect to the company's revenue, they internalize the importance of the numbers instead of treating them as arbitrary targets.

**Phase 4 — Ongoing management:**
- Daily KPI tracking in a shared sheet (new convos, qualified calls, follow-ups, warm outbound, booking rate, show rate)
- Weekly team call reviewing performance by setter
- Monthly anonymous MVP vote ($1K bonus + public recognition for winner)
- Setter ascension path: top performers can move to manager or closer as they prove themselves

**Key principle (SooWei):**
Setters are usually beginners. They are not fully formed salespeople. The investment you put into training them in week 1 pays dividends for months. Do not cut corners on the onboarding. A setter who is unsure of themselves will lose prospects at the first sign of friction. A setter who has been trained and tested is confident, direct, and effective.

---

### New Follower vs. Old Follower Outreach Process

**Root: Nik Setting**

**New followers:**
1. Check profile: Does this person have a business? Do they match ICP? Is their account active?
2. If yes: Send to a YouTube video or content piece first (nurture before booking). Do not pitch immediately.
3. Goal with new followers: start a conversation, establish that you noticed them and added value, build the first layer of trust.

**Old followers (have seen your content, not yet engaged):**
1. Much warmer — they know who you are.
2. Go directly to a qualifying opener.
3. These are the most efficient conversations to have. They are pre-warmed. The outreach is just activating what the content already started.

**Tracking by setter:**
- Show-up rate per setter: if one setter has 40% show-up and another has 80%, the low-performing setter is either booking too fast (not qualifying enough) or not following up properly (not re-warming after booking).
- Weekly review: show every setter their personal metrics, not team averages. Personal accountability.

---

> **SABBO APPLICATION — Setter/DM System**
>
> **Setup sequence:**
>
> 1. **Hire one setter to start.** Source from communities (info business communities, sales rep communities, people who have used your services and understand the model). Junior is fine — they will be trained.
>
> 2. **Deploy the 48-hour onboarding.** Build the training materials:
>    - Agency setter training: offer overview, ICP profile (7–8 figure founders, PMF, burning ad spend), pricing ($5K–$25K/mo), common objections ("we already have an agency," "we're not ready for paid," "we need to figure out organic first"), and the 3 qualifying questions (revenue, current acquisition process, available budget)
>    - Amazon setter training: offer overview, ICP profile (Tier A: $5K–$20K capital, Tier B: existing seller), pricing ($3K–$10K), common objections ("it's too expensive," "what if products don't sell," "I don't have time"), and the 3 qualifying questions (available capital, current Amazon experience, timeline)
>
> 3. **Build the tracking sheet.** Track daily per setter: new DMs sent, conversations opened, qualification questions asked, booking links sent, calls booked, show-up rate, close rate on their booked calls.
>
> 4. **Deploy 50/50/50 KPIs.** 50 new, 50 warm, 50 follow-ups. Every day. Non-negotiable.
>
> 5. **Use iPhones.** Per Jeremy Haynes: rich founders on the agency side will not respond to green Android texts. All setter outreach must be from iPhones.
>
> 6. **Selfie video within 1 hour of booking.** This is the single highest-impact post-booking action. The setter sends a brief iPhone selfie video: "Hey [Name], it's [Setter] from Sabbo's team. So excited you booked — [Closer name] is going to be on the call with you on [date]. Quick thing: before the call, check out [content link] — it'll make the call way more productive. See you then."
>
> **Agency setter opener (example):**
> "Quick question — is the current bottleneck in your acquisition getting qualified leads in, or converting the ones you're already getting?"
>
> **Amazon setter opener (example):**
> "Are you selling on Amazon right now, or are you still pre-launch?"

---

## SECTION 3.4 — WEBINAR FUNNEL

**Root: Jason Fladlien (One to Many) — via Ben Bader + Jeremy Haynes**
**Cadence: Jeremy Haynes — weekly cold + monthly warm**

---

### Framework

A webinar makes three sales — and all three must be made before a single dollar changes hands:

1. **Sell the vehicle** — Convince them the mechanism (growth operating / Amazon FBA) actually works
2. **Sell the authority** — Convince them that YOU are the person who can deliver it
3. **Sell the belief system** — Convince them that THEY can do it / it will work for them specifically

**The Trust Hour Rule:** You need approximately 60 minutes of genuine content consumption before a high-ticket prospect will make a purchase decision. This is why webinars work. This is why short VSLs alone are insufficient for cold audiences.

**The correlation data (from Jeremy's inner circle mastermind):** 8 out of 9 members who cracked million-dollar months were using live webinars as a primary or secondary conversion mechanism. Webinars are the single most correlated funnel type with 7-figure months.

---

### Webinar Structure (Jason Fladlien / Ben Bader)

**Phase 1 — Frame (0–15 min):**
- Open with roll call: "Comment your name and where you're joining from." This activates participation immediately.
- Frame what the next 60–90 minutes will contain. Set expectations.
- Give them an incentive to stay to the end (a resource, a template, or a live Q&A session).
- Sell them on staying: "If you stay for the full presentation, here's what you'll walk away with..."
- Micro-commitment: "Comment YES if you're ready to get started."

**Phase 2 — Training (15–60 min):**
- Three core elements. Each element should: teach a concept, demonstrate with an example or case study, end with a probing question or micro-commitment.
- Sprinkle social proof after every major point. Do not save proof for the end.
- Use curiosity loops: "In just a moment I'm going to show you exactly how [client/student] did this, but first..."
- Rehooks throughout: "If you've been wondering [common question], stay with me — I'm going to answer that in the next segment."
- Pain amplification: Jeremy's "taking them to the pit." Make them feel the cost of inaction before you offer the exit.

**Phase 3 — Pitch (60–75 min):**
- Bridge from teaching to offer: "Everything I've shown you in the last hour is what I do for [clients/students] inside [offer name]."
- Onion pitch structure — layer by layer. Each layer reveals more value. Each layer makes the next feel like an obvious addition.
  - Layer 1: The core mechanism and outcome
  - Layer 2: The support infrastructure (calls, community, accountability)
  - Layer 3: The bonuses (stacked one at a time)
  - Layer 4: The guarantee or risk reversal
  - Layer 5: The price (say it after all layers are revealed, not before)
- Price anchoring: "I could charge $10K, $20K, $50K for this..." then reveal actual price
- "Before I tell you the price, I want to be honest — it's not cheap."
- State the price clearly. Do not hedge. Do not apologize.

**Phase 4 — Q&A / Objection Handling (75–end):**
- The real selling happens in Q&A. Jeremy Haynes: "Most of my webinar revenue comes from people who stayed for Q&A."
- Every question is a publicly handled objection. When you answer one person's question about "what if I don't have enough time," you answer it for every lurker with the same concern.
- Bring on a live member or student during Q&A if possible. Live social proof at the moment of highest buying intent = maximum impact.
- "Is there anyone in the chat who has been through the program?" [If yes: "Tell them what you told me last week on our call."]
- Drive urgency: "I'm only taking [X] calls this week — here's the link in chat now."
- "If you're on the fence, book the call. The call is free. The call is the lowest-risk next step."

---

### Webinar Scheduling Cadence

**Root: Jeremy Haynes**

**Weekly cold audience webinar:**
- Exclude ALL warm audiences (email list, past buyers, social followers, anyone who has engaged with content)
- True cold traffic only
- This is harder. Mastering it makes warm webinars feel effortless.
- The analogy Jeremy uses: "A Kobe to Shaq alley-oop" — that's how easy warm webinars feel after you've mastered cold.
- Recommended day/time: Wednesday or Thursday evening (testing shows higher attendance midweek evenings)

**Monthly warm audience webinar:**
- All warm audiences combined (email list + social followers + past applicants + content engagers)
- Only once per month. If you run warm webinars more frequently than monthly, the audience fatigues and show rates collapse.
- Treat warm webinars differently: you do not need to establish credibility from scratch. They already know you. Get to the pitch faster.

**Why the cadence matters:**
- Weekly cold webinars build a sustainable, scalable lead flow independent of organic reach
- Monthly warm webinars maximize conversion from the audience you have already built
- Without the separation (cold vs. warm), you either fatigue your warm audience or never build systematic cold acquisition

**Financial endurance expectation:**
Jeremy ran 16 webinar iterations over 16 weeks and spent $400,000 before finding the winning formula. The money was not lost — it bought certainty. Expect 8–12 iterations before a webinar works consistently. Budget accordingly. Do not make strategic decisions based on fewer than 4 iterations.

---

### Pre-Webinar: Concentrated Messaging Campaign

**Root: Jeremy Haynes**

Between registration and the webinar, deploy a concentrated messaging campaign:
- Email sequence: 4–6 emails between registration and show time (not just reminders — actual content)
- SMS: 3–4 texts (day before, day of AM, 1 hour before, "live now")
- Paid content ads: Hammer them with your best content during the 48–72 hours before the webinar
- Goal: they arrive having already consumed 60+ minutes of your best content. The Trust Hour Rule is satisfied before they even log on.

**From Ben Bader:**
> "I send so many emails and so many texts leading up to every webinar to the point where you'd think it's overkill. But I've never had an experience where it doesn't help."

Better to over-remind and lose a few annoyed people than to have a 30% show rate.

---

### Webinar KPI Benchmarks

**Root: Ben Bader + Jeremy Haynes**

| Metric | Target | Acceptable Minimum |
|---|---|---|
| Registration rate (from traffic) | 40–50% | 30% |
| Show rate (cold) | 30–40% | 20% |
| Show rate (warm) | 50–70% | 40% |
| Retention to pitch | 70–80% | 60% |
| Conversion (direct sale) | 5–7.5% of opt-ins | 3% |
| Booking rate (call funnel) | 10% of opt-ins | 5% |
| Close rate (webinar-warmed leads) | 30%+ | 20% |

---

### Post-Webinar (48–72 Hour Replay Window)

- Replay available for exactly 48–72 hours after live event (not longer — creates false urgency if perpetual)
- Email sequence during replay window: 3–4 emails, urgency-driven, case study heavy
- Setter follow-up: every registrant who did not book a call gets a personal DM from the setter within 24 hours of the webinar ending
- "Hey [Name], I saw you attended the webinar yesterday. What part resonated most with you?"

---

> **SABBO APPLICATION — Webinar Funnel**
>
> **Start with Amazon Coaching** (larger addressable audience → more registrations → faster iteration)
>
> **Week 1–4 (Build):**
> - Write the webinar outline: Vehicle (Amazon FBA works, here's the data), Authority (Sabbo's own numbers + student results), Belief System (students who started with the same capital, same fears, same situation)
> - Create the registration page and follow-up email sequence
> - Record a confirmation page video: "You just signed up for [date]. Here's what you'll learn and what to do before the webinar."
>
> **Week 5+ (Run):**
> - Weekly cold webinar: Wednesday or Thursday evening, cold audiences only
> - Monthly warm webinar: first Wednesday of every month, all warm audiences
> - Track weekly: registration rate, show rate, retention to pitch, close/booking rate
>
> **Webinar financial math:**
> 50 registrants → 40% show rate → 20 attendees → 10% booking rate → 2 booked calls → 40% close rate → 0.8 enrollments at $7K avg = $5,600 per webinar
> At 4 webinars/month → $22,400 from webinars alone
> At scale (300 registrants/webinar): $134,400/month
>
> **Agency webinar:** Run quarterly (much smaller audience, higher ticket). Limit to warm audiences only until content engine is large enough to run cold.

---

## SECTION 3.5 — CHALLENGE FUNNEL

**Root: Ben Bader — 3-day event + deposit model**
**Lineage: Funnel hacked from Iman Gaji's challenge format**

---

### Framework

The challenge funnel is a 3-day live event where:
- Day 1: Break beliefs. Destroy objections to the vehicle. Make the status quo feel impossible.
- Day 2: Deep value delivery. Teach the mechanism. Build trust to maximum.
- Day 3: The pitch. With a deposit model that catches people at peak emotional buy-in.

Ben Bader's client Yahi generated $622,000 in 3 days from a single challenge funnel in the crypto coaching niche. 4,100 registrants, ~1,300 showed on Day 1, 80% close rate on depositors.

The challenge funnel is the highest-revenue-per-event format in the info business. It is also the most effort-intensive. The revenue must justify the cost of execution.

---

### The Structure

**Registration + Promotion:**
- Minimum 60-day promotional cycle. Most operators promote for 2 weeks and get mediocre attendance. 60 days of consistent content, emails, ads, and social proof = the difference between 200 registrants and 2,000.
- Ticket pricing: free (maximize registrants), paid ($47–$197 to cover ad spend and filter tire-kickers), or hybrid (free with paid VIP tier).
- Paid tickets dramatically improve show rates because people who paid have skin in the game. Ben and Yahi recommend charging for tickets.

**Day 1 — Break Beliefs:**
- Do not teach the how. Teach the why.
- Challenge every limiting belief that would prevent them from buying on Day 3:
  - "Amazon is saturated" → refute with data
  - "I need a lot of capital" → show low-capital success stories
  - "I don't have time" → show the time requirements realistically
  - "It's too competitive" → reframe competition as validation
- By end of Day 1, the belief that prevented them from buying should be neutralized or weakened
- End Day 1 with a preview of what Day 2 holds — urgency to show up

**Day 2 — Deep Value + Soft Pitch:**
- Now that beliefs are cleared, teach the actual mechanism
- Give genuine, implementable value. If they can take what you taught and make progress without you, you have done it right. Their success is proof the vehicle works.
- Sprinkle social proof throughout (live testimonials, results screenshots, case studies)
- Soft pitch at end of Day 2: introduce the offer, give the price range, say "tomorrow I'll show you exactly how to get started"
- Micro-commitments: "Comment YES if you're committed to being here tomorrow."

**Day 3 — The Pitch + Deposit Model:**
- Return briefly to the transformation: "Here's what the last 2 days have been building toward."
- Full pitch: Vehicle, Authority, Belief System
- Onion pitch structure: each layer adds value, price revealed after all layers
- The deposit model: instead of asking for full payment on the call, ask for a $500–$1,000 deposit directly to checkout. No discovery call. No "let me think about it." Click the link, put down the deposit, and one of the coaches follows up.
- Why deposits work:
  1. Catches people at peak emotional high (2 days of content have created maximum conviction)
  2. Irrevocable commitment (depositors show up to the follow-up call, they are bought in)
  3. Eliminates the need for closers in the room (cart-closes are self-service)
  4. 80% close rate on depositors in follow-up calls (vs. 40% typical)
  5. Real urgency/scarcity: close the cart after 7 days. Only 1 of Yahi's 40 depositors didn't reply to follow-up.

**Post-challenge:**
- Setter follows up with every depositor within 24 hours: no discovery, go straight to answer questions and confirm enrollment
- Replay available for 48 hours (not more)
- Non-purchasers get a follow-up email sequence pushing them toward a discovery call

---

### How Ben Bader Funnel-Hacked Iman Gaji's Challenge

Ben's team analyzed Iman Gaji's challenge funnel structure in detail:
- Used GPT to analyze the full transcript of Iman's webinar/challenge content for copywriting structure
- Matched the visual design of the registration page (color, layout, video player type)
- Extracted the emotional arc of Days 1–3 from Iman's public content
- Applied the same structure to their niche (AI operating) with their own content

This is the correct way to borrow from competitors: analyze the structure, not the content. The structure is the innovation. The content is yours.

---

### Challenge Funnel Economics

**Conservative scenario:**
- 200 registrants → 50% show rate → 100 on Day 3 → 10% deposit rate → 10 deposits → 80% close → 8 enrollments × $7,500 avg = $60,000
- Ad spend to generate 200 registrants: $3,000–$5,000
- Net: $55,000–$57,000 from one challenge

**Aggressive scenario (Yahi's result):**
- 4,100 registrants (organic only) → ~1,300 on Day 1 → deposit model → $622,000 in 3 days

**Timing:** Quarterly. January, April, July, October align with Jeremy's recommended calendar. 60-day promotional cycle means you start promoting 2 months before the event.

---

> **SABBO APPLICATION — Challenge Funnel**
>
> **Start with Amazon Coaching. Deploy Q2 (April).**
>
> **Promotion starts: February 1st.**
>
> **Challenge structure for Amazon OS:**
> - Day 1: Break the beliefs ("Amazon is dead," "I need $50K to start," "it's too competitive," "I can't compete with big sellers")
>   - Use data from your own sourcing pipeline
>   - Show deals with 30%+ ROI that required under $2K in capital
>   - Case study from a student who started with $7K and hit $10K/month
> - Day 2: Teach the sourcing framework (the 5-step process, the profitability calculator, the retail check process)
>   - Give them the actual checklist — the real one
>   - If they can use it and find one deal before Day 3, they are sold
> - Day 3: Full pitch
>   - Vehicle: Amazon FBA works, here's the math
>   - Authority: Sabbo's numbers, student results
>   - Belief System: "If [Student Name] started where you are and hit $12K/month in 90 days, you can too"
>   - Deposit model: $500 deposit toward the $7,500 program. Direct to checkout. Cart closes in 7 days.
>
> **Target:** 500 registrants → $15,000–$30,000 net from first challenge. Use that to fund the next one.

---

## SECTION 3.6 — PROOF SYSTEMS

**Root: Alex Hormozi / $100M Playbook — Proof Checklist**

---

### Framework

> "Everyone can make the same promise, but no one can have the same proof." — Hormozi

Proof eliminates the primary obstacle to every purchase decision: risk. The customer's question is: "Will this work for me, the way I want, on the timeline I need?" Proof is the data that answers that question.

**Hormozi's discovery:** When he analyzed the top 50 ads of all time for Gym Launch against the thousands of low-performers, the pattern was clear. 80% of winning ads:
- Had no educational content
- Were not focused on the offer
- Didn't center him
- Told one story: *This product works.*

The low-performers were about the business, the mechanism, the offer. The winners were about proof.

> **Your promise is not a differentiator. Your proof is.**

---

### The 13-Point Proof Checklist

The more of these boxes you check, the more compelling your proof becomes.

**1. In-Person > Virtual**
When someone sees proof with their own eyes, they believe it more than any digital version. Application: bring clients to events, fly in best-performing students to speak live at your challenge funnel close. The cost is recovered many times over.

**2. Live > Recorded**
Live testimonials are more compelling than recorded ones. At every live event, webinar Q&A, or challenge Day 3, have a live student or client share their result. "Living proof" is the most powerful category.

**3. Raw > Processed**
Lightly edited or unedited testimonials outperform heavily produced ones for authenticity. An iPhone selfie video from a student who just hit their first $10K month converts better than a studio-produced testimonial from the same student.

**4. Show > Tell**
Visual proof beats verbal description every time. Screenshot of a Seller Central dashboard beats "my student did $12K this month." Video of a student's first profitable buy list beats any written description.
- Build this into the customer journey: prompt students to screenshot milestones, record their reactions to first sales, document sourcing finds.

**5. Other People Saying Your Stuff's Great > You Saying It**
No one cares what you say about yourself. Build systematic proof collection. At every milestone (first purchase, first sale, first $1K month, first $10K month), trigger an automated request for a testimonial.

**6. Identical to Them > Opposite of Them**
Match the proof to the prospect's demographics: age, gender, capital level, starting point, niche, location.
- If your ICP is a 35-year-old professional with $8K to invest, show testimonials from 35-year-old professionals who started with $8K.
- Run different testimonials for different audiences in paid ads. The demographic match drives response.

**7. Personal > Generic**
Specific pain beats vague enthusiasm. A testimonial that starts with "We were two months from shutting our doors" is infinitely more powerful than "This program is amazing."
- Interview template: "Describe the conditions you were in that forced you to seek help." / "What specific things happened that drove you to change?" / "Tell me an example of an experience you have now that you would never have had before."

**8. Big Results > Small Results**
The biggest result becomes the anchor for all other proof. Capture it in every format possible: video, screenshot, written case study, short-form clip, email testimonial. Reach out to your best-performing client or student and invest real time and money in capturing their result.

**9. Newer > Older**
Unless results are up to date, prospects assume you haven't had a good outcome since the last one. Set up systematic testimonial collection so fresh results arrive in your inbox weekly.

**10. More Proof > Less Proof**
You cannot have too much proof. Build a proof page. Build a proof wall in every presentation. 5,000 testimonials on a single page converts because the sheer volume overcomes every remaining doubt.

**11. Third-Party Verification > Zero Verification**
Accreditations, industry awards, certifications, and public approval from trusted third parties amplify every other proof point. "You don't need to believe me — believe them."

**12. Numbers > No Numbers**
Data is irrefutable. Specific numbers beat vague claims.
- "54% of students who complete the first 30-day sourcing challenge find a profitable product" beats "most students find profitable products."
- Track data at every milestone. Make the data public. Update it quarterly.

**13. Metaphors > Technical Jargon**
When proof involves complex mechanisms, translate through analogy.
- Amazon FBA example: "Think of your sourcing operation like a vending machine route. Each product is a machine in a different location. Once it's stocked and placed, it generates income on autopilot while you add more machines. Our job is to help you identify which machines are worth placing and where to put them."
- Agency example: "Ads are like renting attention. SEO and content are like owning a building. We install the building first — the system that generates leads from owned assets — and then we layer paid on top so you're not paying rent forever."

---

### The Proof Collection System

**Step 1: Map the milestone moments**
Every coaching offer has natural milestone moments when proof is most genuine and most emotionally charged:
- Amazon: first product sourced, first profitable buy, first sale, first $1K month, first $10K month
- Agency: first $1M in tracked revenue generated, first client they retain beyond 90 days, first case study result

**Step 2: Automate the collection request**
At each milestone, trigger an automated request:
- Text: "You just hit [milestone]. That's huge. Would you be willing to hop on a quick 5-minute Zoom so we can celebrate this properly?"
- Email: "Congratulations on [milestone]. Many clients who reach this point have valuable insights others need to hear. Would you share your story?"

**Step 3: Extract with probing questions**
Do not ask "How was your experience?" Conduct structured interviews with probing questions:
- "What was your situation before you joined?"
- "What had you tried before that didn't work?"
- "What specifically made you finally commit to this?"
- "Tell me about the first time you [milestone]. What were you feeling?"
- "What would you tell someone who is sitting where you were 90 days ago?"

Keep asking "why" until you reach the emotional core.

**Step 4: Capture in multiple formats**
From one testimonial session, extract:
- Long-form video (YouTube testimonial channel)
- 60-second highlight clip (Instagram/TikTok/Reels)
- Written quote with photo (email and ads)
- Screenshot of result with caption (story sequences and ads)
- Case study document (PDF for sales deck and proposal)

**Step 5: Deploy at every stage**
- Top of funnel (ads): raw, personal, demographic-matched clips
- Webinar registration page: big result + specific number + demographic match
- Confirmation page: 3–5 proof pieces that match the registrant's profile
- Hammer Them campaign: proof-heavy content in retargeting rotation
- Sales call: case study of someone who was exactly where this prospect is now
- Post-purchase: proof that they made the right decision (prevents buyer's remorse, increases LTV)

---

### Building a Proof Wall

A proof wall is a single page with hundreds or thousands of proof points. Hormozi ran a page with 5,000 testimonials and a CTA button every 3–5 testimonials. People stayed up all night reading the whole page.

**For Sabbo:**
- Build a dedicated proof page at [domain]/results or [domain]/students
- Populate with every case study, screenshot, DM conversation (with permission), student result
- Embed on the website, link from every email, reference in every webinar

---

> **SABBO APPLICATION — Proof Systems**
>
> **Immediate actions:**
>
> 1. **Student result interview:** Reach out to your 3 best-performing Amazon students this week. Schedule a 20-minute Zoom. Record it. Extract proof in every format.
>
> 2. **Client case study:** For every agency client who has seen results, document the before state (what was broken), the intervention (what you installed), and the after state (revenue generated, leads driven, CAC reduced). This is your agency proof wall.
>
> 3. **Automated milestone triggers:** Set up in your CRM/email system: when a student hits [first product sourced], send a congratulation + 5-minute testimonial request. Do this at every major milestone.
>
> 4. **Proof checklist audit:** Before running any ad, webinar, or challenge, audit the proof you plan to use against the 13-point checklist. How many boxes are checked? The higher the score, the more the proof will convert.
>
> 5. **Demographic matching:** Create at least 3 distinct testimonial clusters: (a) Tier A beginners who started with $5K–$10K and hit first $5K month, (b) Tier B existing sellers who stalled and broke through, (c) Tier C investors who treat this as asset-building. Match the proof to the audience seeing each ad.
>
> 6. **Agency proof (for the B2B audience):**
>    - Use IQ-level vocabulary in all proof: "reduced CPL by 43%," "3.2x ROAS on first campaign," "installed a 90-day acquisition engine"
>    - Avoid lifestyle proof with agency prospects — they want systems, data, and results, not lifestyle
>    - Use numbers wherever possible (Hormozi: numbers > no numbers, especially for B2B buyers)

---

## MASTER CHECKLIST — PART 3

Use this checklist to audit your leads system before going live with any new campaign or offer launch.

### Lead Magnets
- [ ] Lead magnet exists for each offer (agency + Amazon)
- [ ] Magnet type selected (reveal problem / free trial / one step of many)
- [ ] Name tested — at least 3 headline variations created
- [ ] Gap is clearly established at end of magnet
- [ ] Qualifying question included in opt-in form
- [ ] UTM tracking set up for each magnet

### Lead Nurture
- [ ] Sub-60-second automated response set up for all opt-ins
- [ ] First-week outreach cadence built in CRM (3 day 1, 2 days 2–3, 1 days 4–7)
- [ ] Automated reminder sequence live (immediate, 24hr, 12hr, 3hr)
- [ ] Manual reminder tasks configured (night before, morning of, 60 min before)
- [ ] BAMFAM protocol enforced: every call ends with next call booked
- [ ] Hammer Them campaign built (minimum 30 short-form + 15 long-form pieces)
- [ ] Hammer Them retargeting audience configured (booked calls last 14 days)
- [ ] Pixel conditioning implemented (confirmation page gated, drop-sell page not pixeled)
- [ ] Application questions are IQ-based and qualifying

### Setter / DM System
- [ ] Setter hired and onboarded (48-hour training + quiz gate + mock call)
- [ ] 50/50/50 KPIs set and tracked daily
- [ ] Opener style confirmed (yes/no binary, low friction)
- [ ] DM qualification script built for each offer (commitment, urgency, resources)
- [ ] Phone setting scripts built for each offer
- [ ] New vs. old follower outreach protocol established
- [ ] iPhone confirmed for all setter outreach
- [ ] Selfie video protocol confirmed (within 1 hour of every booking)
- [ ] Weekly setter review meeting scheduled

### Webinar Funnel
- [ ] Webinar outline complete (Vehicle, Authority, Belief System structure)
- [ ] Registration page live
- [ ] Pre-webinar email sequence live (4–6 emails between registration and show time)
- [ ] Pre-webinar SMS sequence live (day before, day of AM, 1 hour before, live)
- [ ] Hammer Them campaign activated for registrants (48–72 hours before)
- [ ] Weekly cold webinar scheduled (exclude all warm)
- [ ] Monthly warm webinar scheduled (first week of each month)
- [ ] Financial endurance budget reserved (8–12 webinar iterations minimum)
- [ ] Post-webinar setter follow-up protocol in place (DM within 24 hours)
- [ ] Replay available for exactly 48–72 hours (not indefinitely)

### Challenge Funnel
- [ ] Challenge planned quarterly (January, April, July, October)
- [ ] 60-day promotional cycle confirmed (challenge date set 60+ days from now)
- [ ] Day 1 belief-breaking content outlined
- [ ] Day 2 deep value content outlined
- [ ] Day 3 pitch + deposit model configured
- [ ] Deposit checkout page live (no discovery call required)
- [ ] Setter follow-up protocol for depositors (24 hours, answer questions, confirm enrollment)
- [ ] Cart close date set (7 days after challenge ends)

### Proof Systems
- [ ] Top 3 students/clients interviewed for proof extraction
- [ ] Proof captured in: video (long), clip (60 sec), written quote + photo, screenshot, case study
- [ ] Proof organized by demographic cluster (Tier A, Tier B, Tier C for Amazon; revenue level + niche for agency)
- [ ] Milestone-triggered testimonial collection automated in CRM
- [ ] Proof wall page built and populated
- [ ] Proof audited against 13-point checklist before each campaign launch
- [ ] Agency proof uses data/numbers, not lifestyle (ICP is B2B founders, not aspirational seekers)
