## 1. CLOSING SOP [root: Hormozi $100M Playbook]

### Why Closing Is The Most Leveraged Skill

Hormozi's gym launch story: Sales teams going 2-for-14, 0-for-7. He wrote a closing playbook, drilled it daily, focused on one objection at a time. Result: approval rates went from 70% to 94% over 13 months. Revenue went from $100K/quarter to $1.5M/month.

> "Closing determines who gets the massive number of customers from bucket three — the people who might say yes... if only somebody closed them. Better ads make the pie bigger. Closing gets you a bigger slice of it."

**The Three Buckets:**

```
NO     <-- UNQUALIFIED
              Goal: Filter out ASAP

MAYBE  <-- AREN'T SURE YET
              Goal: THIS is why we train closing.
              The money is here.

YES    <-- READY TO BUY (laydowns)
              Goal: Don't mess it up. Shut up and collect.
```

### What Closing Actually Is

Closing is NOT about convincing people. It is about giving people enough power to make a genuine decision — yes or no. People avoid decisions because they have too little decision-making power. They blame external things (circumstances, other people, themselves) to avoid owning the choice.

**Your job:** Remove the blame. Return the power. Force a genuine decision.

**Closing starts AFTER you've asked the prospect to buy.** Selling happens before the ask. Closing happens after.

---

### The Onion of Blame Framework [root: Hormozi]

People on the fence avoid decisions by blaming things that look reasonable. Three layers:

```
EXTERNAL -----> CIRCUMSTANCES (outer layer)
                    - "I'm too busy"
                    - "It's too expensive"
                    - "I don't have the money"

            OTHER PEOPLE (middle layer)
                    - "I need to check with my partner"
                    - "I've been burned before"

INTERNAL -----> SELF (inner layer)
                    - "I need to think about it"
                    - "It might not work for me"
                    - "Send me a brochure"
```

Key insight: People often swap objections when you close correctly. Keep peeling back the layers. You haven't failed when they give a second objection — you're succeeding. The first objection was just the outer layer.

---

### The 28 Rules of Closing [root: Hormozi] — Essential Reading

1. **When in doubt, repeat back what they said.** Buys you thinking time + shows you're listening.
2. **Acknowledge or agree, but NEVER disagree.** Disagreement creates hostility. Always validate first.
3. **Before getting real, get permission.** "Can I be a coach instead of a friend for a second?"
4. **Learn to stack closes.** First close doesn't land? Hit it from another angle immediately.
5. **You don't need to memorize. You need to understand the logic.**
6. **You only need 2-3 closes per objection.** Pick the ones that feel natural.
7. **Use nudges when someone is right on the edge.** One-liners tip deals over.
8. **Yellows are golds. Practice on unqualified leads.** More reps = better closer.
9. **Volume negates luck.** Do enough reps and it stops being luck.
10. **Don't assume objections mean they won't buy.** "It's expensive" is sometimes just an observation.
11. **NEVER change your price on the spot to get a sale.** Caving = you lose all future authority.
12. **If you're always in a battle, look at what happens before they show up.** Fix the pre-call.
13. **Only ask for the sale when you think you've got 'em.**
14. **People want to believe you.** They want to buy. Help their brain justify the decision they already want.
15. **Selling happens before you ask for the sale. Closing happens after.**
16. **It's easier to handle problems before you ask for money than after.**
17. **Expect and plan for no.** It's not failure. It's expected.
18. **Price shock isn't a no.** Unless they say there's a problem, assume they're processing.
19. **Selling properly is the first step to becoming a coach.** Help people decide for themselves.
20. **The person who cares most about the prospect wins the sale.** Keep their wellbeing at center.
21. **Seek to understand, not to argue.**
22. **Selling is a transference of belief over a bridge of trust.**
23. **Belief and trust are a continuum, not binaries.** Always get better at building both.
24. **Closers ask hard questions because they genuinely care.** Be kind, not nice.
25. **If you're going to say something offensive, say it about someone like them or your past self.**
26. **ONCE THE PROSPECT SAYS YES, SHUT UP.** Do not sell yourself out of a sale.
27. **Record all your sales.** Champions watch game tape. Improve one thing at a time.
28. **Power is the ability to direct or influence people.** Close = power.

---

### The B2B Sales Call Framework [root: Ben Bader / Hormozi]

B2B sales are fundamentally different from B2C. Do not follow a rigid script. Get an accurate picture of their situation. Provide the solution based on what they tell you.

**Phase 1: Chit-chat / Intro**
Show you're a normal person. Read their energy — some are direct, some need warmup.

**Phase 2: Transition + Quick Context**
> *"So for some quick context, [your background/credibility in 30 seconds]. My goal here is basically to see if it makes sense to install [system] into your business. Cool if we run through what you're doing now and I'll have a better vantage point on what we could do to scale?"*

**Phase 3: Gather Info**
Start with: *"Give me a little context on what you've got going on."*

Then probe based on their answer:

For founders who haven't sold info/high-ticket yet:
- What type of content are they making?
- How engaged is their audience? Do they get inbound DMs asking for help?
- Why haven't they monetized yet?
- What offer are they considering?

For founders already running an offer:
- What type of offer(s)?
- How does their funnel work?
- Where does traffic come from?
- Do they have an email list? Sending consistently?
- If low-ticket only: what's their thinking on not having high-ticket?

**Phase 4: Strategy**
Based on their answers, show them what they should do. Explain WHY your solution makes sense using logic, not emotional pressure.

**Phase 5: Transition to Close**
> *"OK so if I were you, I'd add [X]. Does that make sense and does it sound like something you'd want to implement?"*

[They say yes]

> *"Cool. So we can go over what it would look like having me build this out for you — strategy, timeline, pricing, etc. Sound good?"*

[Permission granted to pitch]

**Phase 6: The Close**
Run through exactly what you'll do. Give a timeline. State the price clearly.

> *"For this type of project, it'll be $X upfront and [X]% rev share over the initial 90 days."*

Then: **do not start justifying your price if they're silent.** Let them sit in the silence. The first one to speak loses.

---

### The Closer Script Framework — North Star Method [root: Ben Bader]

This is the emotional architecture of a high-ticket B2C/B2B call. Use it for coaching sales (Amazon OS).

**Step 1 — Find the North Star (Why Now)**

*"Could I ask, do you know what you're specifically looking for... just to see if what we do can actually solve it?"*

Dig until you have the North Star — the ultimate goal.

*"What are you currently doing to achieve [goal]? How long have you been doing it that way? Do you feel that approach can get you there, or do you feel you need to make some changes?"*

*"Why do you feel the way you've been doing it isn't going to get you there as quickly as you want?"*

**WHY NOW question:**
*"So why now — like, other than [achieving X] and [achieving Y] — why is now important? Rather than just keeping doing what you've been doing?"*

Alternative: *"Besides the obvious which is to make more money... why is it really important we make a change now?"*

**Step 2 — Future Pace**

*"Let's say when we get you to [goal]. What does that allow you to have?"*

Pick and choose from these emotionally loaded prompts:
- *"What does getting to [income] do? Besides obviously putting more 1s and 0s in your bank account?"*
- *"Personally, how would things change compared to where you are now?"*
- *"Your family — how would things change when you get to [X]?"*
- *"What would you do with the extra?"*
- *"How would that allow you to feel? Your kids feel? Your partner feel?"*
- *"For you — as a [parent/partner/entrepreneur] — but more so for yourself — how would you feel knowing you achieved this?"*

End with: *"So that is at the top of the mountain feeling. [X outcome, Y feeling]."*

**Step 3 — Inaction Questions (The Dark Side)**

This is where most closers chicken out. Don't.

Step 1: *"The other side of this is NOT doing anything."*
Step 2: *"The other side of this is you make no change and you don't take the option to be on top of the mountain. What does that look like moving forward? NOT getting to [X]?"*
Step 3: *"Could I ask how that would make you feel, knowing you haven't made the steps to get to where you want to go for your family and yourself?"*
Step 4: *"I don't mean to put you on the spot. But are you going to ALLOW/SETTLE/BE OKAY if that becomes the reality... again, like it has in the past?"*
Step 5: *"Why not?"* [Say this with a skeptical tone — this creates a double bind. They have to justify to YOU why they WON'T settle. This reinforces their need to change.]
Step 6: *"Can I ask — who is in control here of whether you go achieve everything you said you wanted?"*
Step 7: *"Okay, YOU are."* [Reaffirm.] *"Well, what decisions do you feel you need to make to go and achieve this?"*

Then transition to the pitch.

---

### All-Purpose Closes [root: Hormozi] — Word for Word

**IMPORTANT:** Assume all replies have "totally understand" or "totally get it" or "I hear you" before the close. Always validate before responding.

---

**The "What's Your Main Concern" Close**

*"What's your main concern? What are you afraid of happening?"*

If they give fluff: *"What are you afraid of happening?"*
If still deflecting: *"So you're afraid of spending money and me stealing it and spending it in Vegas?"* [They'll laugh, you're back in the sale]

---

**The "Reason" Close**

*"The reason you're telling yourself not to do this is the reason you should do it."*

- Money objection: *"How long do you want 'I can't afford this' to be on your list of problems? The fact that you don't have money is the very reason you need to do this more than anyone."*
- Time objection: *"The fact that you don't have time is the very reason you need to do this."*
- Authority: *"The fact that you're so dependent on your partner is the reason you need to take this decision and own it."*

---

**The "Hypothetical" Close**

*"If this were perfect, would you do it? Then what's the difference between perfect and what we've got?"*

If they can't find a real difference: *"Right, well because it sounds like it's nothing to do with the program — it's something else. What are you afraid of happening? Let's talk about that."*

---

**The "Zoom Out" Close**

*"Let's zoom out for a second. You want [X]. We sell [X]. Do you think overanalyzing the details might be the reason you haven't made it happen yet? At the end of the day, you just need to decide whether you think this makes it more likely for you to hit your goal than doing this on your own. And if you've tried that already, then maybe this is just the thing you've been waiting for — it just doesn't look like you expected it to."*

---

**The "1 to 10" Close**

*"On a scale of 1 to 10, where 1 means you're not interested at all and 10 means you're ready to start right now, where do you see yourself?"*

If 10: *"Great. Let's rock and roll."*
If 9 or less: *"What would it take to get you to a 10?"* [They respond] *"No big deal. I think we can take care of that. Feeling 10ish now?"*

---

**The "Best Case Worst Case" Close**

Simple version: *"Best case we change your life. Worst case you get [X time/result/learning] along the way. Either way you get closer to your goal. Ready to start?"*

With guarantee: *"Best case you do the thing and get the result. Option two, you don't do the thing and you don't get the result — because you didn't do the thing. Only one of these guarantees you won't get there. Which risk-free option do you want — the one that guarantees you won't get there, or the one that has the potential to?"*

---

### Objection Handling — Full Playbook [root: Hormozi]

#### TIME OBJECTIONS

---

**"I'm too busy right now"**

*"Totally understand. Honestly, here's some good news: the busier you are, the better time it is to start. Because life is always going to have busy seasons, and if you can't figure out how to do it during busy seasons, it isn't going to last. And you want this to last, right? Then what better time than when you need it most?"*

---

**"I'll start when things slow down"**

*"Totally understand. Even if things did slow down, you'd get busy again, right? So if you learn how to make this work when you're busy, you'll be able to stick with it no matter what life throws at you. And besides — this is geared to give you time back, not cost you time. The first thing we're going to do is get you to stop doing all the stuff that isn't working."*

---

**"It's not the right timing"**

*"Can I ask you a real question? What are you doing that's more important than this right now? Either you're never going to have time, or something needs to become less important so this can be more important. It sounds like it's more a question of priorities than timing. Either [goal] is more important than these interruptions, or it's not. If it is — let's do it."*

---

**The When/Then Close**

*"This is a classic when/then issue. When I get healthy, then I'll go to the doctor. When I'm rich, then I'll start saving money. It flips the order. You have to start now to create the conditions you're waiting for."*

---

#### MONEY OBJECTIONS

First, know the four flavors:
1. **Not enough value** — has the money, doesn't see the value
2. **Can't afford it** — genuinely limited resources
3. **Others do it for less** — competitor comparison
4. **Would buy for less** — haggler

Translate "price too high" into "value too low." Shift focus from what they pay to what they get.

---

**"It's too much"**

*"I understand that it feels like a lot, and that's actually why I believe this is the right step for you. Most of our biggest success stories started exactly where you are — seeing this as a big investment. And honestly, that's a good thing. The fact that this feels significant means you're more likely to take it seriously."*

---

**"It's not cheap"**

*"Let me ask you a question. How many free PDFs have you downloaded and made no more money? We had two choices: give the bare minimum, or stack so much support that it would be unreasonable not to succeed. So yes, it's not cheap. But would you rather be less likely to hit your goal? Right — us neither."*

---

**"Would you even believe me if it were less?"**

*"Totally hear you. Let me ask — would you even believe it could do what I say it could do if it were one-third the price?"* [They say no] *"Then what are we talking about?"* [laugh] *"Let's get you going."*

---

**"You're gonna spend the money either way"**

*"In the next 12 months, you're gonna spend this amount of money one way or another. All we're deciding is where it goes. On stuff that doesn't matter, or on something 12 months from now you'll look back on and say 'that was the best decision of my life'?"*

---

**"I can't afford it" — genuinely limited resources**

*"Do you know the difference between a self-made millionaire when they had nothing and someone who has nothing? Nothing financially. The only difference is: when they succeeded, it proved it wasn't about the resources they had. It was about how resourceful they were."*

Nudge: *"If you needed life-saving surgery, would you find a way to pay for it? Of course. So the question is — is saving yourself from the life you're living worth it?"*

---

**"The guy down the street does it for less"**

Cheap Comparison Close: *"If we were the same price, which one would you pick?"* [They say you] *"Why?"* [They list all your advantages] *"I totally agree. Couldn't have said it better myself. So now you understand why we aren't the same price."* [laugh and ask for the sale]

Good Fast Cheap: *"Have you ever heard of the value triangle? Good. Fast. Cheap. Pick two. I'm the good and fast guy. Want to know the most expensive option? The most expensive option is using the fast and cheap guy, regretting it, then ending up with me anyway — a day late and a dollar short."*

---

**"Can you do it for less?"**

*"Uhh... we could do it for more."* [pause and smile]

OR counter-anchor: *"We could do it for $[higher price than quoted]."* — Works shockingly well. Shows you believe in your price.

NEVER discount on the spot. Discounting destroys all value authority and takes you from closing to haggling.

---

#### OTHER PEOPLE OBJECTIONS

---

**"I need to talk to my partner/spouse"**

Prevention is best: get all decision makers on the call upfront. If you can't:

*"What if they don't give you permission?"*

- If "I'd do it anyway" → *"Awesome. Let's get you started."*
- If "Then I wouldn't do it" → *"What part specifically do you think they wouldn't approve of? The price? The program? Or me?"* [handle the real objection]
- If "I just don't make decisions without my spouse" → *"Does your spouse approve of your current struggle? If they don't, then why would they be against you fixing something they already don't approve of?"*

If they still won't move:

*"I think you're asking for support, not permission. It's your life, not theirs. If you give that power to them and two years from now you're [still stuck], who are you going to blame? That's when resentment sets in."*

Nuclear option (with humor): Sign up, delay payment 72 hours so they can talk to their partner. *"Lock in your spot, then you've got time to chat it over. Fair enough?"*

---

**"I've been burned before"**

*"Totally understand your reservations. I'd feel the same. But here's something worth considering: if you don't do this, you let that bad decision burn you twice. It burned you once when you made the poor investment. It burns you again if that bad decision prevents you from making a good one. There are good coaches and bad coaches. The only thing worse than a bad investment is letting one bad investment stop you from making a good one. Don't let that bad decision burn you twice."*

---

#### SELF-BLAME / AVOIDANCE OBJECTIONS

---

**"This isn't right for me" / "I don't like this part"**

First: *"What specifically would make this work for you vs. not for you?"* [Isolate the real objection, then solve it]

If it's a preference battle:

*"We know these variables, in this order, create this outcome. If you change the variables, you change the outcome. You want this outcome, right? Then this is the best way we know how to get you there."*

Pain of staying the same: *"We change when the pain of staying the same is higher than the pain of change. What I'm hearing is that you like what's going on in your life more than the pain of change. But from everything you've told me, that doesn't seem like what you really want — is it?"*

---

**"I need to think about it" / "This is happening too fast"**

*"What would make this a no?"* [If they can't define a clear no, they're just scared. That's closeable.]

---

*"I definitely don't want you to feel pressure, but... do you think maybe you're in this situation because you've delayed making this decision? Do you think it would be a bigger mistake to make the same decision again?"*

---

**"Another Year of Almost" Close**

*"No one wants another year of almost, do you? Another year of almost hitting your goals. Of almost getting to [X]. Of almost hiring the team you wanted. If you're tired of another year of almost, then we can't do what we've been doing. So what about a 'this is my year' kind of year for a change?"*

---

**"It doesn't take time to make decisions, it takes information"**

*"After all, you're not going to go home, sit in the rocking chair and stare at the wall thinking 'hmm, am I going to do this?' No. You're going to get in your car, pick up the kids, do groceries, and three, four, five days from now you'll be right back in the same situation. The decision is going to get made. Let's just make it now, with me as the source of information."*

---

### The Buyer Spectrum — 4 Types [root: Jeremy Haynes]

Imagine your audience as a stadium of 80,000 people:

| Type | Profile | What They Do | Your Strategy |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Type 1** | High-risk first mover. Already sold by your content. | Books immediately, no hesitation | Court aggressively. Don't mess it up. |
| **Type 2** | Considered risk taker. Has questions but has risk appetite. | Has objections but overcomes them | Court with structured objection handling |
| **Type 3** | High-skepticism, low-risk. Needs group-think, long cycle. | Needs social proof, time, reassurance | Back-end systems can convert. Proceed with caution. |
| **Type 4** | Skeptic/cynic. Never buys. Creates damage. | No-shows, chargebacks, reputation risk | **Actively deter.** |

**The stadium metaphor:**
- Front rows (Type 1 & 2): Ready. Your messaging resonates. They act.
- Middle rows (Type 3): On the fence. Need more info, social proof, time.
- Back rows (Type 4): Will never buy. Active sources of damage.

**Critical mistake:** Trying to convert the back rows. Every dollar spent on Type 4s is a dollar not spent deepening conviction in Type 2s.

**Active deterrence methods:**
- State your price in the VSL (financially qualifies before the call)
- "This is NOT for you if..." language in ads and content
- Application questions that filter by capability, not just interest
- Tonality and character that resonates with your target and alienates others

**Sabbo Application:**
- Amazon OS: Type 4 is the person with under $3K capital who wants passive income without work. Deter them in the VSL and application. This is the primary deterrence to optimize first.
- Agency OS: Your copy should repel pre-revenue founders and attract 7-figure operators. Type 4 for the agency is the founder who wants you to "just run some ads."

---

### The Consultative Close [root: Ben Bader]

Ben Bader's closing philosophy is the antithesis of high-pressure scripts:

> "Don't be Jordan Belfort with the script. Be casual. Consultative. Just figure out what they want. Place it to them."

**The consultative closer's mindset:**
- You are a consultant diagnosing a problem, not a salesperson pitching a product
- Your job is to understand their situation and show them the right solution — which happens to be yours
- The best closers build their own scripts, coach the clients they close, and go above and beyond

**Core principle:** 80% of conversion should happen in the marketing BEFORE the call. By the time they're on the phone, they should already want it. The call is just confirmation.

*"If your marketing is good enough, you don't even need sales calls."*

**The consultative sequence:**
1. Pre-call research: review their profile, their content, their DM conversation with your setter
2. Open with what you already know about them — "They thought they were talking to you in the DMs. Make sure you understand what your setter did."
3. Ask about their situation, their goals, their history
4. Identify the real gap
5. Present your solution as the logical answer to what THEY told you — not a canned pitch
6. Close

**B2B-specific note:** Rich founders can smell performed confidence vs. real confidence. Be certain, direct, unimpressed by your own success. Never over-explain or over-justify.

---

## 2. PRICING [root: Hormozi $100M Playbook]

### The Genie Framework — Why Doubling Price Is The Move

Imagine a genie offers to double ONE thing:

| Option | What Changes | Profit Impact |
|---|---|---|
| Double new customers | Revenue 2x, costs 2x | **3.5x profit** |
| Double retention | Revenue 2x, costs 2x | **3.5x profit** |
| **Double prices** | **Revenue 2x, costs STAY THE SAME** | **6x profit** |

Profitwell data (512 companies): improving pricing by 1% improves the bottom line by **12.7%** — nearly 4x more efficient than improving acquisition.

Companies with continual price optimization had **11.09 LTV/CAC** vs. companies with no pricing function at **1.68 LTV/CAC**.

---

### 16 Rules of Pricing [root: Hormozi]

1. **Raising prices makes you money in two ways:** More profit per customer AND lower delivery costs (fewer customers, same infrastructure).
2. **Price to make the most money, not sell the most customers.** The price that maximizes lifetime gross profit, not first purchase.
3. **Higher prices often don't cut conversions in half.** If you double price, you don't lose 50% of buyers.
4. **High close rate (50%+) = prices too low.** You have room to raise.
5. **Full capacity = prices too low.** If you're sold out, raise prices.
6. **Fixed capacity + sold out = raise prices immediately.**
7. **Keep raising until the extra money from new sales no longer offsets lost sales.**
8. **Raising prices usually means raising value.** Make the product better to justify it.
9. **Hearing "no" more often doesn't mean making less money.** Do the math.
10. **How to know you raised too much:** You stop making sales, or NPS drops.
11. **Different prices for different customer types.** One avatar may have 5-10x the WTP of another.
12. **Believe in your price.** If you don't believe it, make the product better until you do.
13. **Bill less frequently to reduce churn.** More frequent billing = more frequent cancel decisions.
14. **Display price in smallest increment, bill on longest increment.** "$5/day" billed annually.
15. **Match billing to how you provide value.** Separate one-time value from ongoing value.
16. **Bill as much as you can while keeping customers happy.** Premium price → reinvest → better product → more customer surplus.

**The Lookback Window Rule:** If you make a client $60K in month 1 and $0 in month 2, they cancel. They don't compare to the whole relationship — they compare to the last billing cycle. This is why longer billing cycles reduce churn.

---

### 10 Instant Profit Pricing Plays [root: Hormozi]

A business running 10% margins can turn some of these plays into profit doublers.

| # | Play | Price Increase |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Month → 28-Day Billing Cycles | +8.3% |
| 2 | Processing Fees + Second Card on File | +3-4% |
| 3 | Pass-Through Sales Tax | +0-10% |
| 4 | Annual CPI-Linked Price Increase | +3-10% |
| 5 | Annual Billing Options | +10-15% |
| 6 | Round Up (.99 endings, 7s → 9s) | +1-3% |
| 7 | Annual Renewal Fee On Top of Monthly | +10% |
| 8 | Automatic Continuity / Continued Access | +10% |
| 9 | Ultra High Ticket Anchor (10x your main price) | +10-15% |
| 10 | Priced Guarantee or Warranty Upsell | +5-20% |
| | **TOTAL POTENTIAL** | **+26-63%** |

**Play 8 — Automatic Continuity (High Priority for Sabbo):**
Whatever you sell, create a stripped-down, zero-work version for 5-20% of the main price. Bolt it onto every front-end purchase. One Hormozi company went from $5.6K LTV to $7.4K (32% increase) just from this play. His COO didn't even know where the revenue line was coming from — it was that passive.

*Script:* After the sale, add: "You're automatically enrolled in [continued access/support] at $[X]/month after your program ends. This keeps you in the community with access to [benefit]. You can cancel anytime."

**Play 9 — Ultra High Ticket Anchor:**
Add something 10x your core offer price. The tailor who shows you the $16,000 suit first makes the $2,000 suit feel like relief. This doesn't just affect who buys the anchor — it shifts the price perception of your entire offer suite upward.

**Play 10 — Priced Guarantee/Warranty:**
*Script at checkout:* "You want the standard warranty on that?" [They ask what it is.] "Oh, it's for anyone who likes that extra bit of peace of mind. If this doesn't go as planned, you're covered. A lot of people do it."

---

### Reverse-Based Pricing [root: Nik Setting — unique 50/50 milestone model]

Instead of a flat fee, structure pricing as half upfront + half upon milestone achievement.

**Example:** Offer is $14K total.
- Client pays $7K upfront
- $7K when they hit $50K in cash collected

**Why this dramatically increases close rates:**
- Total price anchors perceived value higher
- Only paying half reduces risk perception and lowers the initial barrier
- It aligns incentives — you're betting on your own ability to deliver
- Improves cash flow as clients hit milestones
- Dramatically increases conversion because the prospect feels you're "in it together"

**The psychology:** Instead of selling a $14K program, you're saying: "Pay $7K now. When I help you make $50K, pay the other $7K. I'm so confident I can do this that I'm only charging you the second half when you win."

**Sabbo Application — Amazon OS:**
- "$3K to start. $2K more when you hit your first profitable product with [X] ROI."
- Creates massive urgency for the student to execute — their second payment is contingent on it

**Sabbo Application — Agency OS:**
- $5K-$25K/month retainer is the published structure
- Alternative pitch for budget-sensitive founders: "$5K to install the system. $10K more when we hit [specific result]."
- This eliminates the "prove you can do it first" objection entirely
- Only offer this for new clients where the relationship isn't yet established

---

### Three-Tier Presentation: DIY/DWY/DFY [root: Nik Setting — gap psychology]

**The Gap Psychology:** The gap between Tier 1 and Tier 2 should feel LARGE. The gap between Tier 2 and Tier 3 should feel SMALL. This anchors Tier 2 as "obviously the right choice" and makes Tier 3 feel like an easy upgrade.

| Tier | Name | Price | What's Included |
|---|---|---|---|
| **DIY** | Do It Yourself | $4,000 | Self-paced course, minimal support |
| **DWY** | Done With You | $8,000 | Group coaching, some 1:1, accountability |
| **DFY** | Done For You | $10,000 | Full-service implementation |

**The math creates the anchor:**
- $4K → $8K: Feels like a big jump. You get a LOT more for $4K extra.
- $8K → $10K: Feels like a small upgrade. DFY for only $2K more than DWY?

Result: Prospects anchor to the range and gravitate toward DWY or DFY.

**Critical rule:** Only market ONE offer publicly. Never present all three in your content or ads. You market the DWY. On the call, if they're not qualified for DWY, offer DIY. DFY is for upsells.

**Sabbo Application — Amazon OS:**
- DIY: $3,000 — Self-study course, community access
- DWY: $7,000 — Group coaching calls, accountability, product review sessions
- DFY: $10,000 — Hands-on sourcing, deal review, Sabbo's personal involvement
- Market only the DWY in all content and ads

**Sabbo Application — Agency OS:**
- DIY equivalent: Growth OS course/workshop ($2,000)
- DWY: Full growth operating partnership ($5-10K/month retainer)
- DFY: Elite operator model — Sabbo's team embedded in client's business ($15-25K/month)
- Market only the retainer partnership
- Note: Agency three-tier marketing is deferred until coaching channel is established and generating consistent proof.

---

### Price Raise — The RAISE Framework [root: Hormozi]

Use this when you need to raise prices on existing clients. Tested across hundreds of businesses.

**RAISE stands for:**
- **R** — Remind them of value already received
- **A** — Address the price change directly (rip off the bandaid)
- **I** — Invest: show how the extra revenue gets reinvested for them
- **S** — Soften with a loyalty discount (expiring)
- **E** — Explain away concerns + PS statement

**The Template Letter:**

---

Dear [NAME],

Over the past [X] months, we've added so much value to [PRODUCT/SERVICE]:
- We've helped you achieve [specific result]
- [Feature/deliverable] helped you [specific improvement]
- [Specific metric] improved by [amount]

For us to continue investing in making [PRODUCT] even better for you and the [CLIENT COMPANY] team, we need to increase our prices.

With these extra resources, we're going to:
- [Investment 1] — so that you can [benefit 1]
- [Investment 2] — so that you can [benefit 2]
- [Investment 3] — so that you can [benefit 3]

You've been insanely loyal to [YOUR COMPANY], though — using us for the past [X] months. So, as of today we're raising prices on new customers, but since you've been so loyal, we're going to keep you on your existing plan for the next [3-6 MONTHS]. We're giving you a [$XXXX] credit as a way of saying thank you. After that, we'll bump you up to the new price of $[XXX].

Thank you for letting us be a part of [COMPANY]'s mission. If you have any questions at all, let me know. All replies go directly to me.

[YOUR NAME — SIGN IN INK IF PHYSICAL]

PS — if this materially impacts your business, let me know and we'll work something out.

---

**Three types of people who respond:**
1. **See the value:** May not like it but they comply. Majority.
2. **Actually affected:** Sob stories. Offer them 6 more months at the old rate.
3. **Were going to cancel anyway:** You just pulled forward churn by one month. Not a real loss.

**Price Raise Rules:**
- Don't grandfather existing customers or do lifetime deals
- Never sell "one-time price for lifetime access"
- Raise prices at least once per year
- Test price raises on new customers first
- Meet with people individually if raising more than 50%
- Pair a price raise within 90 days of a new product launch

**The math on "how many customers can I lose and still make money?"**
If you raise price 50% and can afford to lose up to 33% of customers, you break even. Lose fewer, and you profit. This is almost always the outcome.

**For Sabbo:**
- Agency clients: Annual price raise baked into contracts from day one. Script: *"To ensure we can keep reinvesting in our team and systems to get you the best results, our contracts include an annual 10% CPI adjustment."*
- Amazon students: Run price increases quarterly ($3K → $5K → $7K) as case studies accumulate

---

## 3. BACK-END SELLING SYSTEMS [root: Jeremy Haynes — his 5-system framework]

### Why Back-End Systems Are The Highest-ROI Investment

These systems don't require more ad spend. They don't require new offers. They work on the funnel you already have. Deploying them on an existing call funnel can shift:
- Show rate: from 50% to 70%
- Close rate: from 20% to 30%
- AOV: from $5K to $8K
- Payment terms: toward larger upfront payments

That's a 2-3x revenue increase from the same leads, the same ads, the same offer.

**The 5 Systems:**

---

### System 1: Confirmation Page

The moment someone books a call, they're at peak commitment. Most businesses send a generic Calendly confirmation email and waste this moment. Wrong.

**What the confirmation page should contain:**

1. **Confirmation video (60-90 seconds):** You, on camera, direct. *"Hey [Name], [Your Name] here. You just booked a call with me/my team. Here's exactly what to expect..."* Set expectations, create excitement, establish authority. The prospect went from content-consumer to almost-client — welcome them into that.

2. **Breakout videos (3-5 short videos):** Address the top questions you get on sales calls BEFORE the call happens. Common formats:
   - "How the program works" (2-3 min)
   - "What our clients' first 30 days look like" (2 min)
   - "The most common question I get before calls" (2 min)
   - A client testimonial video (1-2 min)

3. **Testimonials:** Identifiable, contactable people. Screenshot format from original source (text messages, social media DMs). Not polished videos alone — raw proof converts.

4. **"Do Your Research" section:** Address what they'll find when they Google you. Link to your YouTube. Link to reviews. Show you have nothing to hide.

**Sabbo Application:**
For Amazon OS: *"Here's how our sourcing system works. Here's a real deal I found last week. Here's what a student found in their first month."*
For Agency OS: *"Here's what the first 30 days look like. Here's what you'll have at day 30. Here's what clients say after month 1."*

---

### System 2: Hammer Them Strategy

After someone books a call, you run a concentrated content campaign targeting ONLY that person (and anyone else in that custom audience). The goal: compress what would normally take 5 months of organic content consumption into 48-72 hours through paid distribution.

**Volume requirements (minimum to create the "concentrated messaging" effect):**
- 30-50 short-form pieces (60-90 second videos)
- 15-30 long-form pieces (YouTube, podcast clips)

**The 4 Quadrants of Hammer Them Content:**
1. **Common questions from sales calls** — What do people actually ask? Answer those questions on video.
2. **Common objections** — What stops people from buying? Handle them on video before the call.
3. **Expectations for success** — What should they expect if they buy? Set expectations.
4. **Second-order questions** — Questions that arise AFTER the first questions are answered.

**Deployment:**
- Set up a custom audience: people who booked a call but haven't had it yet
- Run these videos as paid content ads to this audience
- Budget: $5-15/day to this tiny audience is enough — they're seeing 10-15 pieces of content per day
- The prospect thinks: "This person is everywhere." They arrive pre-sold.

**Advanced: The Tornado**
When ALL hammer them campaigns are deployed simultaneously at ALL funnel stages (post-booking AND post-registration AND post-low-ticket-purchase). Maximum saturation.

---

### System 3: Value-Dense Email Sequences

Not reminder emails. Not "we can't wait to speak with you" emails. **Educational emails** that provide actual value and build conviction before the call.

**Post-booking email sequence structure (5-7 emails over the days between booking and call):**

| Email # | Type | Content |
|---|---|---|
| 1 (Immediate) | Confirmation + access to pre-call page | Excitement + logistics |
| 2 (Day 1) | Value education | Key concept from your framework |
| 3 (Day 1-2) | Case study | Specific client result with details |
| 4 (Day 2-3) | Process walkthrough | "Here's exactly what we'll do together" |
| 5 (Day 3) | Expectation setting | "What our best clients have in common" |
| 6 (24 hours before) | Logistics reminder | Reply "YES" to confirm |
| 7 (Morning of call) | Text-only | "We still good for [time]?" |

The key: Emails 2-5 are NOT about selling. They're about educating and building trust. The prospect arrives on the call already believing in the mechanism.

---

### System 4: Setter Outreach — The iPhone Selfie Video + Personalized Text

This is Jeremy Haynes' most cited high-impact setter action. Most people neglect it. It's the single biggest show rate lever available.

**The protocol:**

**Immediately (within 1 hour of booking):**
1. Setter records a selfie video on iPhone (must be iPhone — rich people do not respond to green texts)
2. 30-60 seconds, casual and direct
3. Reference something specific from their application or profile
4. *"Hey [Name], just saw you booked a call with [Owner]. I'm [Setter Name]. Just wanted to reach out personally — excited to connect. Before your call, we've put together a short video that'll save you a ton of time on the call itself. I'll send that over. And if you have any questions before then, hit me back."*

**Personalized text (within 2 hours of booking):**
*"Hey [Name], just saw you booked — [Setter Name] here from [Company]. I was looking at your [profile/application/situation] — noticed [specific detail they mentioned]. That's exactly the kind of situation [Owner] works with. Can't wait for your call."*

**Why it works:** Authority transfer. The prospect went through the funnel because of the founder's credibility. The setter inherits that credibility by referencing the founder's work and showing genuine knowledge of the prospect's situation.

**SooWei add — Send targeted YouTube video per pain point:**
Instead of sending one generic "watch this before the call" video, send a SPECIFIC video that matches their stated pain point from the application.

Examples:
- If they said they struggle with product sourcing: *"Hey, I noticed you mentioned sourcing is your bottleneck. [Owner] just did a deep-dive on exactly that — [link]. Worth watching before the call."*
- If they said they struggle with show rate: *"Saw you mentioned show rates are an issue. Here's [Owner] walking through exactly how we fixed that for [client] — [link]."*

This creates a "this person actually read my application" effect that spikes show rates by 15-25%.

---

### System 5: AI Manipulation Best Practices

Jeremy Haynes withholds this from his YouTube content — it is only available in his paid program (Jeremy's Inner Circle, $10K/month). Noted here as an open slot in the framework.

---

## 4. SHOW RATE OPTIMIZATION [root: Jeremy Haynes]

### Why Show Rate Is The Most Underrated Metric

Ben Bader's math on the value of show rate:

**At 50% show rate:** 100 booked calls → 50 show. At 40% close rate → 20 deals.
**At 70% show rate:** 100 booked calls → 70 show. At 40% close rate → 28 deals.

That's 8 extra deals per month from the same ad spend, same offer, same close rate.

At $5K per deal: **$40,000 in additional monthly revenue** from improving ONE metric by 20 points.

**Target show rate:** 70%+ (Jeremy's benchmark). Acceptable minimum: 50-60%.

---

### The Full Post-Booking Process (11-Touchpoint Protocol) [root: Hormozi / Jeremy Haynes]

**Immediately after booking:**
1. Immediate email confirmation
2. Immediately email video training / pre-call page link (ask if they want it texted too)

**Between booking and call:**
3. Automatic Calendly reminder 12 hours prior
4. Manual email confirmation 24 hours prior (from sales rep email, not automation)
5. Manual text 24 hours prior OR morning of call

**The 24-hour email script:**
> Subject: Reply "Yes" to confirm appointment
>
> Hey [Name],
>
> Excited for our call on [DATE] at [TIME]. Be ready to go on time.
>
> Please reply "Yes" to this email to let me know you can still make it.
>
> [If relevant: Also, if you have a partner or anyone who'd support you in this decision, could you please make sure they're in attendance?]
>
> Best,
> [Salesperson name]
>
> P.S. If you cannot make our scheduled time, please let me know in advance. We're getting about [X] applicants a day and I want to be fair to the others.

**Morning of call:**
6. Automatic Calendly reminder 2 hours prior
7. Manual text morning of call:
   - Text 1: "Name!"
   - Text 2: "It's just [Setter] with [Company]. We still good for our call at [time]?"

**If no response 3-4 hours before:**
8. Email bump: Reply to confirmation email with "^ bumping this up"

**At call start time (if no-show):**
9. Call twice. Text: "[Name] I'm ready for our meeting, are you coming?"
10. Leave voicemail: *"Hey [Name]... this is [Closer] with [Company]. You had booked for now about [what you discussed]. My number is [phone]. I should be around for a little bit today if you'd like to reach me. Talk soon."*
11. Send no-show email

*If after 11 touchpoints they still aren't engaging: something during the booking process turned them off.*

---

### Tie Downs — Financial Qualification, Partner, Pre-Call [root: Hormozi / Setters]

Tie-downs are used during the SETTING CALL (when booking the appointment) to pre-qualify, get all decision makers committed, and create psychological investment before the closing call.

---

**Calendar Booking:**
*"We have openings tomorrow and [X]. Which works better? Are you a morning or afternoon person?"*

---

**Financial Qualification:**

*"I want to make sure I'm doing my due diligence to provide the most value — I wouldn't want to get you excited about what we do if you didn't have the means to actually go out and succeed. So my team asks that I ask a few basic financial questions to figure out the best direction for your business."*

*"There are two areas. First: over the past 6 months, where would you say your monthly revenue is? [Qualification threshold]. Second: liquid capital, cash on hand, or credit lines you could put strictly toward business growth?"*

*"Just to confirm — [time] would work for the full hour, right? You'll be able to give 100% of your focus and attention?"*

---

**Partner / Decision Maker Tie Down (CRITICAL — must be done on every call):**

*"Part of our team's process is making sure we can help everyone involved, not just you individually. With that said — do you have any business partners or other decision makers who should be on the call as well?"*

If NO: *"So just to clarify — hypothetically, if you wanted to move forward, you wouldn't need anyone's permission or approval to do so?"*

If ANOTHER DECISION MAKER: *"Can both of you 100% be on the call at [time] on [day]?"*
- If that time doesn't work: Reschedule to when BOTH can attend.
- If they don't know the other person's schedule: *"Let's lock in a tentative time, you confirm with them, and if they can't make it we'll find another through text. What time do you think they could make?"*

**THIS IS NON-NEGOTIABLE.** If you close without the decision maker present, you close one party who then has to re-sell another party who wasn't there. Your deal will die in that re-sell.

---

**Pre-Call Tie Down (The Video Commitment):**

*"Now, one last thing — this is arguably the most important piece of the entire process. My consultant makes sure everyone I place on their calendar watches an important pre-call video beforehand. It takes just 20-30 minutes. It'll go through and answer a ton of your questions and show you exactly how you'll be able to implement this. If you don't watch it, both you and my consultant waste a lot of time — and they put my head on the chopping block for that one. [laugh] So I just need you to 100% commit to watching it before your call — can you do that for me?"*

[They commit]

*"Awesome. So you'll for sure go through that and take notes? You're not going to get me fired? [laugh] Only reason I go so hard on that is because it's so important that if you're not able to watch it beforehand, it's our policy for consultants to cancel the call to protect their time."*

[Edification handoff:]
*"Your [advisor/consultant] is [Name]. They have a wealth of knowledge about this process — I think you'll get a ton of wisdom from them. They'll reach out within the next few minutes with the video link."*

---

### Show Rate Optimization Checklist

- [ ] Confirmation page built and linked in Calendly confirmation email
- [ ] Setter selfie video protocol active (within 1 hour of booking)
- [ ] Personalized text from setter (within 2 hours of booking)
- [ ] Targeted YouTube video sent based on stated pain point
- [ ] Email sequence active (7-email post-booking sequence)
- [ ] Hammer them campaign running to booked-not-yet-shown audience
- [ ] 24-hour manual email with reply-to-confirm mechanism
- [ ] Morning-of-call manual text
- [ ] Automatic Calendly reminders at 12 hours and 2 hours
- [ ] No-show protocol scripted (voicemail, email, text)
- [ ] Financial qualification completed on setting call
- [ ] All decision makers committed to the call

---

## 5. SALES TEAM MANAGEMENT [root: Hormozi — calendar utilization / Jeremy Haynes — narrative management / Ben Bader — culture]

### Calendar Utilization Sweet Spot [root: Hormozi]

**70% utilization is the target.** This means a closer working a full week should have approximately 70% of their available slots filled with booked calls.

- Below 70%: You have a lead flow or show rate problem
- Above 80-85%: You have a scaling problem (need to hire more closers or expand calendar)
- At 90%+: You're leaving money on the table and burning your closer out

**Why 70% and not 100%?**
- Closers need buffer time between calls to reset mentally
- Some calls run long
- No-shows happen — a fully packed calendar means one no-show cascades
- Room to shadow calls and review recordings

**The second-closer threshold:** Don't wait until your calendar is full to hire a second closer. By the time you hire and ramp them (30-50 calls to hit KPI), you'll have already lost weeks or months of capacity. Hire at 65-70% calendar utilization.

---

### Narrative Management [root: Jeremy Haynes — unique framework]

This is Jeremy's most controversial teaching. The principle: **control what the sales team knows about lead quality**.

> "Sometimes you have to manage the narrative. If you tell them the leads are bad, they'll prove you right."

**The self-fulfilling prophecy of "bad leads":**
When closers believe leads are low quality, they approach every call with lower conviction, less energy, and less investment in the outcome. This causes worse performance, which confirms their belief that the leads were bad. The cycle compounds.

**What to do instead:**
- Never tell your team the leads are "test leads" or from an unproven new source
- Always frame lead quality in neutral or positive terms
- If testing new messaging that might bring slightly lower-quality leads, don't announce it
- Let the data speak through the disposition system — not through blanket announcements

**The disposition system replaces subjective "good lead / bad lead" feedback:**
Instead of letting closers say "the leads suck," give them specific categories:
- "Not financially qualified"
- "Wrong business model"
- "Timing issue — check back next quarter"
- "Already working with competitor"
- "No-show — first attempt"
- "No-show — third attempt"

This gives marketing actionable data to adjust targeting without poisoning the team's belief system.

**Practical rule:** If you're testing a new ad angle or new lead source, don't announce it to the team. Tell them it's a strong batch. Measure the actual close rate. If the close rate drops, diagnose the actual cause (lead quality vs. closer performance vs. pitch). Don't assume and don't announce assumptions.

---

### Sales Team Culture [root: Ben Bader — energy > process]

Ben Bader's single most shocking observation from running high-ticket sales teams:

> "One offer went up 40% month-over-month with zero changes to funnel or ads — just better team energy."

The same funnel. The same leads. The same offer. 40% more revenue. From team energy alone.

**What "energy" looks like in practice:**
- "Good morning" in all-caps in the team Slack. Everyone hyped. Everyone lit.
- Celebrates wins loudly and publicly the moment they happen
- Creates a culture where closers WANT to bring wins back to the group
- Cuts underperformers fast — one low-energy closer brings down the whole team

**The A-player filter:**
- Takes ownership without being asked
- Goes above and beyond the listed responsibilities
- Doesn't need to be managed — checks in proactively
- If they're not going above and beyond after 30 days, cut them

**Ben's rule:** It's the same as the winning-product analogy for dropshipping. Run clients (and closers) like Facebook ad campaigns. The best performing ones get more attention and resources. The underperformers get cut. Going from 6 closers to 3 closers (keeping only the best) often INCREASES revenue.

---

### Sales Manager Daily Operating System [root: Hormozi / Ben Bader]

**Daily Priority Order:**
1. Complete daily manager checklist
2. Check who completed KPI sheets — tag reps who didn't
3. Execute action items from checklist (deep work first)
4. Respond to Slack threads (last — these are time drains)
5. Listen to calls and develop coaching material

**KPI Sheet Requirements (per closer, daily):**
- Calls scheduled
- Calls shown (show rate)
- Calls closed
- Revenue collected
- Objections hit
- Disposition of each call

**One-On-One Meeting Protocol:**
1. Ask if they have questions (always leads somewhere)
2. Review a call they struggled with — walk through it together
3. Practice: Explain what they could do differently. Then DRILL it (sheer number of reps)
4. Ask them to restate their takeaways. Verify alignment.

**Group Coaching Meeting Protocol:**
1. Ask if anyone has questions
2. Weekly update: congratulate top performers, reveal week's cash collected
3. Teach ONE specific thing you observed everyone needs help with
4. Drill it live — mock calls, simulation, role play
5. End with encouragement

**Critical management rule:**
> "Make a big deal out of wins. Celebrate performance at the end of the month. Coaching calls are just another sales call with a different frame. Show up 110% every time. Your lasting impression IS their lasting impression. Make reps seek your approval."

---

### Hiring Closers — The Interview Framework [root: Hormozi]

**What you're evaluating:**
- Body language and tonality on the call
- Clarity of thought and depth of answers
- Temperament under light pressure

**Immediate red flags:**
- No camera on the interview call
- Late to the meeting
- Conducting interview while commuting or driving
- Lack of clarity on what sales actually is

**What you're really looking for:**
> "Hire for attitude. Train for skill."

*"What you're looking for is a creative, vibrant energy. Someone who has the desire and passion to sink their teeth into something and help others."*

**If it's not a "Hell Yes" — it's a no.** Candidates are abundant. Never hire someone with a bad attitude or lack of clarity just because they have experience.

**Interview questions that reveal what you need to know:**
- Walk me through your sales experience specifically
- How much have you personally invested in sales training and education?
- What are you most proud of professionally?
- Tell me about the worst incident you handled
- Sales can be challenging — how do you balance competing demands?
- What's the bigger picture for you in the next 12 months?

**Ramping timeline:**
- Days 1-7: Drinking from the firehose. Shadow calls. Review recordings. Script and drill.
- Days 7-14: Take limited call volume. Get heavy feedback. Keep drilling.
- Days 15-30+: Full call volume. Goal: hit KPI well before 50 calls.

**KPI thresholds:**
- Within first 10 calls: 1-2 deals minimum
- Within first 20-30 calls: Close to or at KPI
- Within 50 calls: At KPI consistently

**Statistical significance note:** 50 calls is the minimum for meaningful data. But you're also evaluating qualitatively the whole time — coachability, culture fit, hunger, how they show up to meetings.

---

### The Upsell Framework [root: Hormozi / Ben Bader]

The best time to upsell is NOT when the program ends. It's when they hit a NEW bottleneck that requires a different solution.

> "The moment of greatest satisfaction is the moment you ask for a referral. The moment of greatest pain is the moment you ask for an upsell or renewal."

**The upsell framework call:**

Setting the call (via setter):
*"Hey, it's [Setter] from [Company]. [Owner] wanted us to reach out to get some feedback on how things have been going — to see how we could better the product/journey. You got a few minutes to chat?"*

Discovery questions:
1. *"What made you want to pull the trigger on [program] in the first place?"*
2. *"Looking back [X months] — what have you seen improve?"*
3. *"What were you looking to improve specifically when you joined?"*
4. *"What do you wish was in this program that you might still be seeing issues with?"*
5. *"What are you noticing specifically when it comes to [problem]? How long has that been going on?"*

Transition to close:
*"So would you say it's less of a problem of [X] and more of a problem of [Y]? How has not having [Y] been impacting you? And if we never address [Y], what do you feel would happen?"*

*"Can I make a suggestion? Depending on where you are, [Owner] has put together something for clients at your stage that might help. I can get you with [team member] who runs our advanced program — it's basically a credit toward your existing investment if it makes sense. Do you feel like that conversation would help?"*

**Sabbo Application:**
- Amazon OS students: At 60-day check-in, if they've sourced their first product, upsell to ongoing monthly coaching
- Amazon OS advanced: At program completion (day 90), upsell to Premium 1-on-1 at $15K for students who want Sabbo's direct personal time
- Agency clients: At 90-day review, if results are strong, upsell from retainer to retainer + revshare on revenue generated

---

## 6. FAST CASH SOP [root: Hormozi $100M Playbook]

### What Fast Cash Plays Are

> "Revenue is vanity. Profit is sanity. Cash is reality."

**Definition:** Fast Cash Plays are limited-time offers advertised to your WARMEST audiences.

Warm audiences:
- Current customers
- Previous customers
- All engaged leads (people who have given explicit permission to contact them)

They are NOT nurturing new leads. They are NOT long-term content emails. They are more like "winning lottery tickets you cash in once per quarter."

**Run Fast Cash Plays quarterly — 4x per year.** Weekly doesn't work (fatigue). Annual doesn't work (leaving money on the table). Once per quarter is the sweet spot.

---

### The 10x the 10% Rule

If you get 10% of your customers to pay 10x the price, you double your revenue.

Since you already paid to acquire these customers, all the extra revenue (minus delivery) drops straight to profit. This is why Fast Cash Plays, despite being ~15% of annual revenue, can represent nearly 50% of annual profit.

**Quarterly ROI example** (business doing $25K/month recurring):
- Q1: 10 buyers at $6,000 = $60,000 + 3 new customers
- Q2: 13 buyers at $5,000 = $65,000 + 2 new customers
- Q3: 8 buyers at $6,000 = $48,000 + 1 new customer
- Q4: 14 buyers at $4,000 = $56,000 + 2 new customers
- **Total extra cash: $229,000**

Old annual revenue: $300K. Net income: $75K.
New annual revenue: $529K. Net income: **$281K** — nearly 4x.

---

### What to Sell

Think: scarcity, urgency, exclusivity, premium price. Think of the most unscalable things you can offer:

- 1:1 attention from you personally (or senior team members)
- "Many on 1" — your full team focuses on ONE customer (more valuable than 1:1)
- Personalized/customized versions of your standard solutions
- 24/7 support, extended hours, exclusive access
- In-person experiences, retreats, behind-the-scenes access
- Your personal cell phone (for the duration)
- Your personal network and introductions
- Priority access and fast-track positioning

**Offer structure:** 1-3 core components + 3 bonuses. Drop bonuses one at a time during the campaign sequence to drive urgency. Each bonus = another reason to buy NOW.

**How many to sell:** Cap it. 5-10% of your customer base maximum. You want to SELL OUT. Selling out makes your next offer more compelling.

**Price:** 10x to 50x your normal transaction size. Start with whatever your average cart value is and add a zero.

---

### The 7-Day Push-To-Consult Sequence [root: Hormozi]

Prep ALL emails and texts BEFORE you launch. This is a sequence — don't improvise.

---

**Sunday (7 days out) — Text only:**
*"Hey [NAME] — would it be cool if I got you [to their goal] and saved you a ton of money? Give me a thumbs up if that sounds cool. I'm sending you something you're gonna like tomorrow."*

---

**Monday (6 days out) — Email + 2 texts:**

**Email:**
> Subject: We need to talk
>
> I'll keep this short. I want to help you [achieve your goal] faster. And make it easier. And I'm gonna make it cheaper for you. Crazy, I know. But there's a selfish reason I'm doing this...
>
> Main reason: Transparently, I want to invest in [big business improvement] — which will benefit you in these ways:
> - [Benefit 1]
> - [Benefit 2]
> - [Benefit 3]
>
> So, as a way of saying thank you for supporting our business, **for [10 customers] I'm going to give you this ONE TIME ONLY DEAL — available this week only. EXPIRES [DAY] AT MIDNIGHT.**
>
> What the first [10] people get:
> - [Core offer or savings]
> - [Premium feature 1]
> - [Premium feature 2]
> - [Premium feature 3]
>
> So yes, you're going to GET MORE and PAY LESS than everyone else.
>
> I'm limiting this to [10] people only. This is a one-time deal.
>
> If you want in → [scheduling link] OR reply to this email with: "I'm in."
>
> PS — I have never done a deal of this magnitude before. It's limited to [10] people and expires [Saturday at midnight] or once the slots are filled. Whichever comes first.

**Text AM (after email send):** *"Hey, sooo I just sent you an email! Did you get it?"*
**Text PM:** *"That email about our special offer has my inbox blowing up. Click the link >>[LINK]<< to set a time to talk about it."*

---

**Tuesday (5 days out) — Email + 1 text:**

**Email:**
> Subject: best. deal. ever. [for 10 people only]
>
> In case you missed it. Yesterday, I made a limited offer for [10] people — only good until [Saturday at midnight].
>
> **What the first [10] people get:**
> - [Core savings or offer]
> - [Premium feature 1]
> - [Premium feature 2]
> - [Premium feature 3]
>
> **Update:** About half the spots are already gone, and we still have five days left. I doubt we'll make it until [Saturday]. So contact me immediately.
>
> Book here: [LINK] / Call or text: [phone] / Reply: "I want in. Yes, charge my card."
>
> PS — to skip the line, text "I want in" to [phone].

**Text:** *"Don't be like this guy... [meme about waiting]"*

---

**Wednesday (4 days out) — Text only:**
*"Hey, I know I sent you an email about our offer, but I wanted to send a text too — because this won't happen ever again. Click >>[LINK]<< to set a time. Or just reply."*

---

**Thursday (3 days out) — Email:**

**Email:**
> Subject: how to [get dream result] and save money doing it
>
> People were asking me how many spots were left.
> Answer: Over half the spots are gone. [X] people have already committed.
>
> They'll be getting:
> - [Premium feature 1]
> - [Premium feature 2]
> - [Premium feature 3]
>
> No other customers will get these. Just my way of saying thank you.
>
> **It's easy to say you support something. It's another thing to show it.**
>
> Book here: [LINK] / Text: [phone] / Reply: "I want in."

---

**Friday (2 days out) — Email + text:**

**Email:**
> Subject: 2 spots left + game changer
>
> We have TWO spots left. [X] of you have already committed.
>
> As my way of saying thank you, they're getting:
> - [Premium feature 1]
> - [Premium feature 2]
> - [Premium feature 3]
>
> AND — GAME CHANGER I WAS SAVING UNTIL NOW
> - [YOUR BEST BONUS — worth more than the entire offer price if you can]
>
> Hit reply or text me at [phone] immediately.

**Text:** *"[NAME] — we're down to our last couple of spots. When is a good time to talk?"*

---

**Saturday AM (last day):**

> Subject: Saving $XXX ends tonight. Don't kick yourself tomorrow.
>
> I've heard it from a few of you: "I'll wait until the next one!"
>
> What if there is no next one? What if, by not taking action now, you don't make the NEXT STEP?
>
> And maybe... the habit of waiting for the next one is why you aren't where you want to be right now.
>
> The [OFFER NAME] expires tonight at [time]. To get in, reply or text [phone].
>
> PS — I'm also giving [FINAL BONUS] to anyone who commits today. That's [X] bonuses total.

---

**Saturday PM (if spots still remain):**

> Subject: RE: your goals we set
>
> Hey — looks like someone backed out because of an unforeseen issue. And it's a bummer for them, but great for YOU.
>
> Can I call you now to talk about it? REPLY YES or text "YES IM IN" to [phone].

---

**After selling out:**

**Text (or email):** *"The program sold out! If you missed out, don't worry. We'll do something like this (not exactly like this) in the future. Until then — keep rocking!"*

---

### Fast Cash Checklist

- [ ] Pick and assemble the warm audience list (past + present customers + engaged leads)
- [ ] Design the offer: max out unscalable value, model the ultra-premium examples
- [ ] Set the price: 10x to 50x your normal transaction size
- [ ] Decide: consult-based (open cart immediately, drive to appointments) or automated checkout (build hype, open cart on day 5)
- [ ] Prep ALL emails and texts before launch
- [ ] Have all bonuses ready before announcing them
- [ ] Launch the sequence
- [ ] Take consults / Close deals
- [ ] Deliver the value
- [ ] Collect 4Rs: Reviews, Results, Referrals, Resells
- [ ] Let the list cool down
- [ ] Set next date — run again in 90 days

---

### 5 Reasons to Run Fast Cash Plays Every 90 Days

1. **Cleans the pipeline:** Qualified-but-on-the-fence leads finally get off the fence. A great offer with urgency and scarcity tips them over.
2. **Increases customer value:** People who buy more often are more likely to keep buying — it deepens the relationship.
3. **Keeps things fresh:** Shows there's always something new happening. Keeps customers engaged.
4. **Creates a cadence:** 90 days is enough time to deliver and reset before the next one.
5. **All revenue drops to profit:** The ad spend to acquire these customers is already sunk. Every dollar from a Fast Cash Play is nearly pure profit.

---

### Sabbo Application — Fast Cash Plays

**For Amazon OS (Primary — run this first):**
- Quarterly "Sourcing Intensive": $3,000-$5,000 for a private 3-day live sourcing session with Sabbo
- Includes: live product research, 1:1 profitability analysis on their specific products, direct deal access
- Offered to: email list, past students, Instagram engaged followers
- 10-15 spots — price creates artificial scarcity

**For Agency OS (Secondary — run when agency client base is established):**
- Quarterly "Growth Sprint" offer: $15,000-$25,000 for a 30-day intensive with Sabbo's full team embedded
- Includes: full funnel audit, ad creative refresh, email sequence rebuild, weekly strategy calls
- Offered to: warm leads who haven't yet signed, past clients, engaged email list
- 5-8 spots maximum — sell out every time

**Timing rule:** Run in Q1 (January), Q2 (April), Q3 (July), Q4 (October). Align with natural buying cycles and the quarterly business rhythm.

---

## QUICK REFERENCE — SABBO SALES SYSTEM

### Agency OS Call Flow
1. Chit-chat / quick intro (30-60 seconds)
2. Give credibility context + frame the call (30 seconds)
3. "Give me context on what you've got going on" — gather info
4. Identify the gap (no repeatable acquisition system, burning ad spend without systems)
5. Build the strategy: here's what you need + why
6. "Does that make sense? Sound like something you'd want to implement?"
7. Get permission to pitch: "Want to go over what it would look like to have us do this?"
8. Present the operating system — what you do, how long, cost
9. State price. Silence. Let them respond.
10. Handle objections using the stack above
11. Close

**Key B2B pricing rule:** $[Setup fee] upfront + [% revshare OR monthly retainer]. State it clearly. Do not justify the number if they're silent.

### Amazon OS Call Flow
1. Quick rapport
2. Find the North Star: "What are you specifically looking for?"
3. WHY NOW question
4. Future pace: emotionally loaded questions about what their life looks like at $10K/month
5. Inaction questions: what does NOT doing this look like? Steps 1-7 of the North Star method
6. Transition to pitch
7. Present the coaching program (three-tier: DIY/DWY/DFY — pitch DWY first)
8. Price: reverse-based pricing option available
9. Handle objections
10. Close

### Objection Quick Reference

| Objection | First Response |
|---|---|
| "Too busy" | "The busier you are, the better time it is to start..." |
| "Too expensive" | "It's good that it's a lot — that means you'll take it seriously..." |
| "Can't afford it" | "The difference between a self-made millionaire and someone who has nothing... resourcefulness." |
| "Need to talk to spouse" | "What if they don't give you permission?" → test commitment |
| "Been burned before" | "Don't let one bad decision burn you twice." |
| "Need to think about it" | "What would make this a no?" |
| "Another option is cheaper" | "If we were the same price, which would you pick? Why?" |
| "Can you do it for less?" | "We could do it for more." |
| "This is happening too fast" | "It doesn't take time to make decisions — it takes information." |

### Key Metrics (Weekly Tracking)

| Metric | Target | Problem Threshold |
|---|---|---|
| Show rate | 70%+ | Below 50% = emergency |
| Close rate | 25-40% | Below 20% = training issue |
| Close rate above 50% | — | Prices too low |
| Calendar utilization | 70% | Above 85% = hire another closer |
| Fast Cash frequency | Quarterly | Annual = leaving money on table |
| Price raise frequency | Annually minimum | Never = margin erosion |

# PART 5: FULFILLMENT — Delivering + Retaining

> **Purpose of this section:** Turn paying clients into long-term assets. Every dollar spent acquiring a client is only worth something if the client stays. Fulfillment is where the real business is built — it drives retention, referrals, renewals, and reputation.

---
