## 1. RETENTION SOP

> **Root:** Alex Hormozi — $100M Playbook

### The Core Problem: The Leaky Bucket

Most businesses treat churn as an inevitable cost of doing business. Hormozi proved otherwise. His gym owners were losing 15% of members every month — meaning 83% of their membership base turned over in a single year. A business with a revolving door of customers "is hardly a business at all."

The math is brutal:
- 250 members on January 1
- 15% monthly churn = 208 new clients needed by December 31 *just to stay flat*
- At 12.5% margins, falling behind by even two clients per month means you lose the gym

**The same logic applies directly to Sabbo's agency retainers and coaching programs.** A $10K/mo retainer client who churns after two months is worth $20K. A client who stays 18 months is worth $180K. The acquisition cost was the same either way.

---

### The Inversion Technique: What Would Make Clients Leave?

Before building a retention system, flip the question. Ask: **"What would make 100% of my clients leave?"**

- Ignore them
- Break promises
- Miscommunicate
- Treat them poorly
- Set unrealistic expectations
- Hide progress and results from them
- Keep them isolated from other successful clients
- Make working with you difficult and confusing

**The retention system is simply the exact opposite of this list.** Not complicated. Just consistently executed.

---

### The 9-Step Churn Checklist (Hormozi Framework)

These are the actions, in order, that Hormozi implemented across hundreds of businesses. The claim: "I have never not made more money by going through and applying this checklist. It works every time."

---

#### Step 1: Find Your Activation Points

**What it is:** The specific action or result that, when a client achieves it, dramatically increases their likelihood of staying long-term.

**The formula:** "Every client who does [X] or achieves [Y] within the first [Z days] stays [W times] longer than those who don't."

**How to find yours:**
1. Pull a list of every churned client
2. Pull a list of clients who stayed 3+ months (or your program length)
3. Sort the retained list by total revenue paid (top 20% = your avatar)
4. Study what they did differently: When did they first get a result? What actions did they take in week 1?
5. Find the common factor — that's your activation point

**Real examples by offer type:**
- B2B service company: First time they get qualified leads from the system
- Software: First time they log in and see the dashboard working
- Coaching: First time they make their investment back (or hit a specific milestone)

**Sabbo Application:**
- **Amazon OS:** Activation point = student sources their first profitable product (BUY verdict, real deal, not simulated). Build a "First Deal Fast Track" sequence that gets them to this moment within 2 weeks of onboarding.
- **Agency OS:** Activation point = client sees their first batch of qualified leads come through the new acquisition system within 30 days. Build the "Fast Cash Play" equivalent: a 30-day sprint to get one visible, attributable result within the first month.

**Action:** Update all marketing messaging to attract clients most likely to hit your activation point quickly. Update onboarding to drive directly to it.

---

#### Step 2: Onboard Every Client

**What it is:** A structured process that teaches clients exactly how to reach the activation point.

**The onboarding hierarchy (best to worst, all better than nothing):**
1. Custom 1-on-1 (best)
2. Small group (good)
3. Live group (decent)
4. Recorded walkthrough (acceptable)
5. No onboarding (guaranteed higher churn)

**What strong onboarding must include:**
- Resell the decision they just made (re-anchor on why they bought)
- Set realistic expectations (timeline, what hard work looks like, what results look like)
- Show them exactly where to start (one clear first step, not fifteen options)
- Introduce them to the community and connect them to 2-3 specific people
- Unlock incentive once they complete the first action (courses, access tiers, recognition)
- Schedule the next touchpoint before the call ends — always (BAMF: Book A Meeting From A Meeting)

**Hormozi case study:** A portfolio company moved from group onboarding to 1-on-1 onboarding. Result: 25% boost in client upgrades and ascensions. Revenue went from $2M/month to $2M/week. "The more personalized the onboarding, the better."

---

#### Step 3: Incentivize Activation

Once you know what clients should do (Step 1) and you've told them to do it (Step 2), make it worth doing.

**Incentive types:**
- Courses that unlock after completing homework
- 1-on-1 consulting calls after reaching a milestone
- Tickets to live or virtual events after staying X months
- Custom badges, profile indicators, recognition as being "in"
- Free lifetime access for reaching an elite engagement level (Skool's Level 8)

**Time-based incentives:** Place unlocks just after major churn points. If most clients leave after month 3, put something valuable that unlocks in month 4. The unlock pulls them past the danger zone.

**Sabbo Application:**
- **Amazon:** After first sourced deal approved by Sabbo, unlock "Advanced Deal Analysis" module + access to the live deal-review sessions. Speed to first unlock = speed to retention.
- **Agency:** After first 30-day report shows results, unlock "Growth Accelerator" session (90-min strategy deep dive with Sabbo personally). This makes staying through month 1 feel like winning.

---

#### Step 4: Community Linking

**The gym world truth:** "It's easy to quit a membership. It's hard to leave a relationship."

**Clients don't just stay for you — they stay for each other.** The goal is to build a mesh network (every client connected to multiple other clients) rather than a hub-and-spoke (every client only connected to you). A hub-and-spoke breaks if you leave or scale. A mesh is self-sustaining.

**How to build it:**
- Group onboarding: Introduce 4-6 new clients together so they already know each other
- Manually connect specific clients who share the same problem, industry, or goal
- Elevate "micro-celebrities" within the community — call out wins publicly
- Host regular events (every 21, 42, or 63 days — random to them, systematic to you)
- Start a community podcast or interview series featuring members

**Sabbo Application:**
- **Amazon:** Weekly group live sourcing sessions where students analyze deals together. The community becomes the product as much as Sabbo's coaching does.
- **Agency:** Monthly group "Growth Ops Review" calls where all agency clients share what's working. They learn from each other, not just from Sabbo.

---

#### Step 5: Fire or Correct Bad Clients

Bad clients don't just cost you time — they poison the community. They complain publicly, set unrealistic expectations for others, and make good clients feel like they're in the wrong room.

**The three-strikes approach:**
1. Strike 1: Direct feedback on the specific behavior + what good looks like
2. Strike 2: Written warning with clear consequences
3. Strike 3: Removal from the program

**Simultaneously, reward good behavior publicly:**
- Pin wins prominently in the community
- Praise specific clients by name in group calls
- Create content categories that surface positive engagement (wins, discoveries, connections)

---

#### Step 6: Add Annual Payment Options

Clients who pay annually stay longer. This is not a theory — it's structural. When someone has paid for a year, their psychology shifts from "should I keep going?" to "how do I get the most out of the year I already paid for?"

**Pricing model:**
- If average client stays 6 months at $10K/month ($60K total), price the annual option above $60K
- Standard approach: "Buy 10 months, get 2 free" = 16% discount, typically 10-20% uptake
- For high-ticket offers: The "Big Head, Long Tail" model (see Section 2)

**Alternatively:**
- **Founder Rate:** 50% discount for founding clients who pay annually upfront. Converts more people AND keeps them longer.
- **Large upfront + small monthly:** $6,800 setup fee (education/implementation) + $199/month ongoing community access. LTV can go from $6,800 to $12,800+ as the recurring component compounds.

---

#### Step 7: Cancellation Calls (Exit Interviews)

**The data:** You can save approximately half of clients who request cancellation if you speak to them before they leave.

**The setup:** At onboarding, tell every client: "If you ever want to pause or cancel, our process is a quick 15-minute call first. We do this with everyone."

Setting this expectation upfront removes resistance — it's not a "gotcha," it's a standard process they agreed to.

**On the cancellation call:**
1. Let them vent. Do not get defensive.
2. Match or exceed their frustration level — "That's completely unacceptable. You're right to be frustrated. Will you give me the chance to make it right?"
3. Only one person can occupy the angry position. When you're angrier on their behalf, they start defending you.
4. Ask: "If I fixed [specific issues], would you be willing to stay?" — this creates a clear roadmap.
5. Two save paths:
   - **Save via redo:** Take responsibility, reset expectations, give them another genuine shot
   - **Save via upgrade:** "You should have been sold into the higher tier from the start — that's on me. Credit what you've paid toward the upgrade."

**For high-volume, lower-ticket programs:** If phone calls don't scale, build a cancellation video. The video: (1) reminds them why they started, (2) acknowledges the frustration, (3) shows them what other clients who pushed through achieved, (4) offers a clear path forward.

**Hormozi's stat:** Implementing cancellation calls + this exact script saved approximately 50% of attempted cancellations. That's a ~33% increase in LTV with zero additional acquisition cost.

---

#### Step 8: Survey Clients Twice Per Year

**The two-question survey (Hormozi's exact format):**
1. "If I removed everything I provide but one thing, what would you want to keep the most?"
2. "If I kept everything but could remove one thing, what would bother you least to lose?"

This isolates your highest-value deliverables and reveals where you're wasting time and money on things clients don't actually value.

**Between large surveys — the ACA Framework for regular touchpoints:**
- **A**cknowledge what you've seen them do
- **C**ompliment them on something specific
- **A**sk a question

Example: "I saw you sourced three deals this week — that's a serious pace. The H-Mart find was especially smart given the BSR. What's your goal for units bought this month?"

**Reach out to clients 1-on-1 every 2-3 weeks.** Not to sell. To stay connected. The clients who feel seen and recognized churn last.

**Note from Hormozi:** Counterintuitively, wealthier clients typically want less hand-holding, not more. Read the client, don't over-manage.

---

#### Step 9: Build a Four-Milestone Client Journey

Every client should be guided through four milestones, in this order (or close to it):

```
1. ACTIVATE → Client hits the activation point (first real result)
2. TESTIMONIAL → Client provides a documented win (video, written, case study)
3. REFER → Client sends someone they know
4. ASCEND → Client buys a higher tier or extends their engagement
```

**Why this order matters:**
- Activation creates the genuine satisfaction that makes the other three possible
- Testimonial is easiest to request right after a win (SooWei's rule: "The moment of greatest satisfaction is the moment you ask for a referral")
- Referrals come from clients who've achieved results and feel part of something worth sharing
- Ascension happens naturally when a client trusts you and hits a new ceiling that your next tier solves

**Incentivize each milestone:** Each should unlock something of value. This creates a gamified journey that makes long-term engagement feel like progression rather than a subscription.

---

### The Churn Math — Why This Work Compounds

| Metric | High Churn (10%/mo) | Low Churn (3%/mo) | Impact |
|---|---|---|---|
| Price | $10K/mo | $10K/mo | Same |
| Average months | 10 months | 33 months | 3.3x |
| LTV | $100K | $333K | 3.3x |
| Revenue on 10 clients | $1M | $3.33M | $2.33M more from same clients |

"If you cut your churn from 10% to 3%, you 3.3x the lifetime value of every client. I have yet to see a business with less than 3% churn that doesn't make great money." — Hormozi

**The five-percent rule:** Harvard Business Review found that a 5% increase in retention rates increases profits by 25% to 95%. If average client tenure goes from 10 months to 10.5 months on average, profits can nearly double.

---

## 2. LIFETIME VALUE SOP

> **Root:** Alex Hormozi — $100M Playbook

### What Is LTV and Why It's the Fuel

**LTV (Lifetime Gross Profit / LTGP)** = the total gross profit collected over a client's full engagement, net of delivery costs.

This is the most important number in a business because:
- The business owner who extracts more value from each client can outbid every competitor for attention
- Ad costs only go up. LTV is the lever that makes rising acquisition costs survivable.
- Increasing LTV has no hard ceiling. CAC can only hit zero. LTV can grow infinitely.

**"He who can make a customer worth more to his business than to his competition wins."** — Hormozi

---

### Calculating LTV: 3 Steps

**Step 1 — Gross Profit Per Client:**
```
Revenue per client - Cost to deliver = Gross Profit
$10,000/mo retainer - $2,000/mo delivery cost = $8,000 gross profit/mo
```

**Step 2 — Average Transaction Count (or Churn Rate):**
- Transactional: Export lifetime client data, average the number of purchases per client
- Recurring: Use monthly churn rate (% who leave each month)

**Step 3 — LTGP Calculation:**
```
Recurring: Gross Profit / Monthly Churn Rate = LTGP
$8,000 / 5% churn = $160,000 LTGP per agency client

Transactional (coaching): Gross Profit x Avg Transactions = LTGP
$7,000 avg program value x 1.4 avg transactions = $9,800 LTGP per coaching student
```

---

### The "Big Head, Long Tail" Model

> **Root:** Alex Hormozi

The core insight for education and coaching businesses: **the value of learning peaks before it happens, then drops to near zero immediately after.**

The day before a student learns how to source Amazon deals = incredibly high value.
The day after = the value of that same content approaches zero (they already know it).

This creates a pricing paradox: how do you charge for ongoing access when the core education was a one-time event?

**The Big Head, Long Tail structure solves it:**

```
BIG HEAD: High one-time fee for the education/implementation
LONG TAIL: Low monthly fee for ongoing consumables (community, deal alerts, coaching calls)
```

**Example for Amazon OS:**
- Big Head: $7,500 enrollment fee (90-day coaching program, Sabbo 1-on-1, deal analysis tools)
- Long Tail: $197/month ongoing (deal alert emails, live group calls, community, tool access)

**Why this dramatically increases LTV:**
- "Buy 10 months get 2 free" at $197/month = $1,970 additional annual recurring per student
- 50 students on the long-tail community = ~$9,850/month recurring baseline
- The big-head sale funds the business; the long-tail compounds it

**Critical rule:** Present both the setup fee AND the monthly fee together in the pitch. Never separate them into two distinct sales conversations. The monthly fee must be anchored against the large upfront number so it feels trivially small by comparison.

---

### The Crazy Eight: Eight Ways to Increase LTV

> **Root:** Alex Hormozi

The traditional framing ("increase order value or increase purchases") is too vague to act on. Hormozi breaks it into eight specific, actionable levers:

| # | Method | Description | Sabbo Agency Example | Sabbo Amazon Example |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Raise Prices** | Charge more for the same thing | Current $10K/mo retainers → test $15K | Current $5K program → test $8K |
| 2 | **Decrease Costs** | Reduce delivery costs to increase gross margin | Move from 1:5 to 1:10 client-to-operator ratio | Group coaching model vs. pure 1-on-1 |
| 3 | **Increase # of Purchases** | Get clients to buy the same thing again | Monthly retainer auto-renewal at milestone review | Annual coaching renewal after 90-day program |
| 4 | **Cross-Sell** | Sell a different but complementary product | Agency clients → Amazon coaching access | Coaching students → agency services when revenue grows |
| 5 | **Upsell Quantity** | Sell more of the same thing at once | 6-month prepay at 15% discount | Cohort enrollment (3 students together, group discount) |
| 6 | **Upsell Quality** | Sell a better version (premium tier) | VIP retainer: daily Slack access + bi-weekly calls | Platinum coaching: daily deal reviews + weekly Sabbo 1-on-1 |
| 7 | **Downsell Quantity** | Sell less rather than nothing | Paused retainer (maintenance mode, lower fee) | Self-paced course for clients who can't afford coaching |
| 8 | **Downsell Quality** | Lower-service version vs. full cancellation | Done-with-you audit (not full DFY) | Community-only access ($47/month) after program ends |

**Hormozi's rule:** Never downsell a qualified prospect — only downsell those who genuinely cannot afford the main offer. Downselling a qualified buyer cannibalizes your main offer revenue.

**The upsell favorite:** "More of — or more help with — what they just bought, but with faster results, less risk, less effort, and less hassle — for more money." Surveying a company revealed 85% of clients wanted exactly this over any other cross-sell option. It 2.2x'd their LTV per client, allowing them to 5x advertising spend profitably.

---

### How to Test Price Increases

The close rate table tells you if you're underpriced:

| Current Close Rate | You're Underpriced By |
|---|---|
| 80%+ | 3-4x |
| 60-80% | 2-3x |
| 50-60% | 1.5-2x |
| 40-50% | 1.25-1.5x |
| 30-40% | Appropriately priced |
| Below 30% | Fix the offer/avatar, not the price |

**Protocol:** Test a 20% price increase every 10 new sales. Track conversion rate. If conversion x gross profit per unit is still higher than before, keep raising. Stop when total revenue-per-visitor starts declining.

---

## 3. CLIENT ONBOARDING — The 72-Hour 3-Call Sequence

> **Root:** SooWei Goh

### Philosophy: Fulfillment Before Marketing

SooWei Goh paid $15K to a dedicated fulfillment coach to rebuild his backend before scaling marketing. His thesis: "The best marketing is a good product. If you don't have a good product, you are shooting yourself in the foot and overcompensating on the marketing side."

The 72-hour onboarding sequence is how he operationalized this belief. Three dedicated calls in the first three days — each with a different specialist — signals immediately that this is not a typical program, builds conviction in the investment, and drives toward quick wins that reduce refund risk and increase testimonials.

---

### The 72-Hour 3-Call Sequence (SooWei's Exact Model)

**Trigger:** Client pays. Sequence begins within 24 hours.

---

**Call 1 (Hour 0-24): Welcome Call with CSM**

**Who runs it:** Client Success Manager (not the founder)

**Purpose:** Program overview, expectation setting, accountability architecture

**Agenda:**
1. Warm welcome — acknowledge the decision and reframe it as the right one
2. Walk through the Notion roadmap: what the 90 days look like, milestone by milestone
3. Set communication norms: how to reach the team, response time expectations, where community lives
4. Accountability setup: what they commit to tracking (content cadence, products sourced, deals submitted)
5. Identify their single biggest bottleneck right now (this feeds Call 2 and Call 3 focus areas)
6. Schedule Calls 2 and 3 before the call ends — BAMF (Book A Meeting From A Meeting)

**Script for opening:** "You made a serious decision and I want to make sure the next 72 hours set you up to actually feel that. By the end of this week you're going to have a clear roadmap, your first priority action, and at least two people in this community that you personally know. Let's build that now."

---

**Call 2 (Hour 24-48): Specialist Audit Call**

**Who runs it:** A specialist (not the founder) — in SooWei's model, the closer (George) ran the appointment-setting audit. The closer was part of fulfillment.

**For Sabbo:**
- **Agency OS:** Growth Ops Audit (Sabbo's operator reviews their current acquisition system, identifies gaps, builds 30-day priority list)
- **Amazon OS:** Product Sourcing Audit (review their current sourcing criteria, tool setup, deal-finding process)

**Purpose:** Rapid diagnostic + immediate quick wins

**Agenda:**
1. Review everything they brought in from Call 1 briefing
2. Live audit of their current state (their website, their product list, their ad accounts, their sourcing setup — whatever is relevant)
3. Identify one specific, immediate win they can execute in the next 48 hours
4. Build their Week 1 priority list (no more than 3 actions)
5. Remove anything they're doing that's actively hurting them
6. Send them a written summary within 4 hours of the call ending

**Key principle (SooWei):** "The closer is part of fulfillment. They don't close people they can't help." The specialist on Call 2 must be genuinely invested in the client's outcome, not just completing an onboarding task.

---

**Call 3 (Hour 48-72): Founder Strategy Call**

**Who runs it:** Sabbo

**Purpose:** Business-level strategy, personal connection, north star clarity

**This is the call clients will reference for months.** It's the one where the founder is fully present and says the thing that reframes their entire approach.

**Agenda:**
1. Review what was discovered in Calls 1 and 2
2. Ask the three core questions:
   - "What does success look like for you at the end of this 90 days?"
   - "What has stopped you from getting there before?"
   - "What are you most afraid won't work?"
3. Address each fear directly — not dismissively, but with specific evidence or reframe
4. Set the personal north star metric (one number they'll be measured against)
5. Share one principle or insight that is not in the program materials — make it personal
6. Schedule the Week 1 check-in before hanging up
7. Personally introduce them to 2-3 community members by name (over Slack or text) before end of day

**Post-call protocol:**
- Send a personal voice memo within 2 hours summarizing the key insight from the call
- Assign them their first homework (one specific, completable action within 24 hours)
- Check that their community introduction was acknowledged by at least one community member

---

### After the 72 Hours: Week 1 Continued

**Access to module library:** Unlock their first tier of content after completing Call 1 homework

**Community introduction post:** They write a structured post introducing themselves (SooWei's model: specific structure, comment on 2 other posts, connect with 2 people above and below their level)

**Accountability tracker live:** Their tracking begins Week 1 — content frequency, products sourced, deal submissions, calls attended

**Week 1 check-in call with CSM:** Assess progress against homework, identify blockers, refine Week 2 plan

---

### SooWei's Ongoing Fulfillment Infrastructure

| Element | Cadence | Owner |
|---|---|---|
| Notion roadmap | Always accessible | CSM manages |
| Accountability tracker | Updated weekly | Client + CSM |
| Group coaching calls | Weekly | Sabbo |
| Weekly CSM reviews | Weekly | CSM (identifies highest-engagement clients for extra support) |
| Community wins channel | Always on | Community (CSM moderates) |
| Guest speakers | Monthly | Sabbo books |
| In-person masterminds | Quarterly | Sabbo |
| 1-on-1 with Sabbo | Monthly (at minimum) | Sabbo |

**Client tracking dimensions:**
- Posting cadence (content output)
- Implementation speed (how fast they execute suggestions)
- Results milestones (first deal, first sale, first $X)
- Community engagement level

**Highest-engagement clients get more:** CSM flags the top 20% of engaged clients weekly. Sabbo gives them additional attention, public recognition, and early access to new resources. This reinforces the behavior that creates success stories.

---

### The BAMF Rule (Book A Meeting From A Meeting)

> "There always has to be a meeting from a meeting." — SooWei Goh

Every client interaction must end with the next interaction already scheduled. Not "I'll follow up soon." An actual calendar invite before the call ends.

Sales call → onboarding Call 1 → Call 2 → Call 3 → Week 1 check-in → Monthly 1-on-1 → renewal conversation

This creates predictability for clients (they always know when they're being seen next) and operationally ensures no client falls through the cracks.

**The upsell/renewal rule (SooWei):** "The moment of greatest satisfaction is when you ask for a referral. The moment of greatest pain is when you ask for an upsell or renewal." Do not ask for upsells or renewals at the end of a program — ask for referrals. Upsell when the client hits a roadblock that the next tier uniquely solves. Renewal conversations happen at the moment of a win, not the moment of contract expiry.

---

## 4. THE 8 FUNCTIONS OF DELIVERY

> **Root:** Ben Bader — his framework for full-stack info/agency delivery

### Overview

Ben Bader built his agency (94 Marketing) by operating every backend function for info product creators. He codified these into 8 functions that define what complete, professional delivery looks like. For Sabbo, these 8 functions are what the agency IS — they are the Growth Operating System installed for every client.

Knowing the 8 functions is also useful for the coaching offer: it gives students a clear map of what they're building, and it's a framework Sabbo can teach as a module.

---

### The 8 Functions

#### Function 1: Offer Creation and Optimization
**What it is:** Defining what the client sells, how it's priced, and how it's positioned.

**In practice:**
- Audit the current offer against Hormozi's Value Equation (Dream Outcome x Perceived Likelihood) / (Time Delay x Effort)
- Test pricing against close rates (see the close-rate pricing table in Section 2)
- Reposition from commodity to Grand Slam Offer: stack in bonuses, reduce risk, increase speed to result
- Apply the "mall test": can you explain the offer in 20 seconds to a stranger?

**Sabbo Agency deliverable:** A restructured offer document (one-pager) with new positioning, pricing, and guarantee architecture.

---

#### Function 2: Funnel Buildout
**What it is:** The technical and copy infrastructure that converts traffic into leads and leads into calls.

**Components:**
- Landing page (for agency: VSL or profile funnel; for coaching: application page)
- Video Sales Letter (VSSL): 8-12 minutes, structured around Ben's three sales (Vehicle, Authority, Belief System)
- Application questions that pre-qualify and pre-frame
- Calendly integration for booking
- Post-booking page: confirmation video + FAQ + testimonial wall (this alone improves show rates by 10-15%)

**Key principle:** Build for cold traffic from day one. Organic-first offers eventually need to scale to paid. Build the funnel with that intention.

**Sabbo Agency deliverable:** Full funnel built, tested, and live within Month 1 of engagement.

---

#### Function 3: Sales Process
**What it is:** The systems and automations that ensure every lead is tracked, warmed, and handled correctly.

**Components:**
- CRM setup (Close CRM or equivalent): all leads logged, tagged, and owned
- Slack notifications when leads apply or book
- Zapier automations: Calendly booking → email sequence → Slack alert → CRM update
- Lead handoff protocol between setter and closer (documented in SOP)
- Post-booking nurture: email + SMS reminder sequence before the call
- Pre-call research template: closer reviews lead's profile, DM history, application answers before every call

**Sabbo Agency deliverable:** A tracking sheet with daily KPIs (visitors, video plays, applications, bookings, show rate, close rate, cash per call) reviewed weekly.

---

#### Function 4: Sales Team Management
**What it is:** Hiring, training, and managing closers and setters to hit KPI targets consistently.

**Hiring:**
- Setters: hire for energy, coachability, and response speed — not experience
- Closers: look for people who describe their work in specific metrics on interviews

**Onboarding (24-48 hour model from the Hormozi DOCX):**

*Day 1: Setter Onboarding*
- Provide company email credentials (firstname@company.com)
- Set up Slack, Close CRM, and tracking sheets
- Assign Loom video walkthroughs for each tool
- Give access to SOP documents for inbound and outbound setting

*Day 2: Testing and Certification*
- Quiz on the offer, ICP, and objection handling — must score 90%+ to advance
- Mock DM conversation with the sales manager
- Approved or rejected; approved setters begin live conversations Day 3

*Closer Onboarding (additional requirements):*
- Zoom account (company email), Calendly integration, Fathom (call recording)
- Connect all tools to each other: Zoom → Fathom, Calendly → Google Calendar → CRM
- Review 5 recorded calls before taking live calls
- Setter-to-Closer handoff SOP: setter notifies in Slack, closer replies to lead within 5 minutes, logs notes in CRM

**Ongoing management:**
- Weekly team call: KPI review by person (not just total)
- Monthly call analysis using Manis AI (or manual review): common objections, what attracted prospects, closer performance
- EOD reports submitted daily by every setter and closer via Slack by 12:00 AM EST
- MVP vote: monthly, anonymous, $1K bonus + public recognition

**Show rate optimization:**
- 50% → 70% show rate on 100 booked calls = 20 additional at-bats
- At 40% close rate = 8 additional closes
- At $5K per close = $40K additional revenue from one metric improvement
- Improve show rates with: post-booking confirmation video, 2-3 email touchpoints, manual SMS from setter before call

---

#### Function 5: Email Nurture
**What it is:** A systematic email cadence that builds trust between initial contact and purchase, and drives reactivation after purchase.

**Sequences to build:**
1. **Welcome sequence** (5-7 emails over 14 days): Who you are, your story, your proof, your method, the risk of not acting
2. **Post-booking sequence** (3 emails between booking and call): Confirm excitement, share a client win, send a preparation prompt
3. **Non-booker sequence** (for leads who applied but didn't book): 5 emails over 10 days, social proof heavy, ends with "last chance" CTA
4. **Reactivation sequence** (quarterly): For inactive leads — share a new win or offer a time-limited call slot

**Daily campaigns (Ben Bader's #1 compounding habit):**
- One email per day to the list, for anyone who has opted in
- Style: storytelling + analogy + business lesson + soft CTA
- Not a pitch every time — the give-to-ask ratio should be 4:1 minimum
- Ben: "Eventually they just need an excuse to buy. One email can be the difference."

**Building the AI email engine:**
1. Ben's method: Upload every email ever written into Claude/ChatGPT as a custom project
2. Prompt: "Based on all of these emails, create a comprehensive email copywriting guide"
3. Feed this guide + client content → all future emails use the same voice and framework
4. For Sabbo: Build "Sabbo Email Brain" in Claude Projects, trained on voice and positioning

---

#### Function 6: Community and Delivery
**What it is:** The actual coaching, content, and community experience that delivers the promised outcome.

**Components:**
- Course content platform (School, Notion, or equivalent)
- Structured curriculum organized into milestones (not just a folder dump)
- Group coaching calls (weekly minimum for high-ticket programs)
- Community management: wins channel, Q&A, accountability
- Quality protection: say no to bad-fit clients who would poison the community

**Delivery principles:**
- Less is more — "Overwhelm is the #1 reason for churn" (Hormozi). Gym Launch is now on its 10th version and each one is shorter and simpler.
- Decide on the core 2-3 deliverables and make them excellent rather than 10 deliverables that are decent
- Retention comes from ensuring clients CONSUME the value, not from overwhelming them with it
- When clients stop engaging, increase outreach frequency — that's the early warning signal

**SooWei's tracking:** A tracker that monitors calls attended vs. missed, content posting frequency, and implementation speed per client. The top 20% of engaged clients get disproportionate attention. The bottom 20% get a recovery protocol (personal outreach, adjusted expectations, extra support).

---

#### Function 7: Tracking and Data
**What it is:** The daily KPI sheet and reporting infrastructure that makes every decision data-driven.

**Daily KPI tracking (per business):**
```
Traffic: Unique visitors, profile visits, video plays
Applications: Number submitted, qualification rate
Calls: Booked, confirmed, showed, no-showed
Sales: Offers made, closed, revenue collected
Post-sale: Onboarded, activated, testimonials secured
```

**Fulfillment tracking (per client):**
```
Activation: Did they hit the activation point?
Engagement: Calls attended, content posted, actions submitted
Results: Milestones reached (deal sourced, revenue generated, etc.)
NPS: Satisfaction score at 30/60/90 days
Referrals: Number of clients referred
```

**Weekly reviews:** Every Sunday — 15-minute KPI review. Flag any client whose engagement dropped from the prior week. That's the usage churn signal (still subscribed but no longer active = high churn risk in 30-60 days).

**Tool stack:** Google Sheets → Looker Studio dashboard for visualization. Zapier automations to auto-populate from CRM and booking tools.

---

#### Function 8: AI in Action
**What it is:** Using AI tools throughout the delivery process to increase speed and quality while reducing costs.

**Applications:**
- **Content generation:** Sabbo's voice + proven framework → AI drafts → human polishes last 10-20%
- **Email writing:** The AI email brain (see Function 5) handles 80-90% of email production
- **Call analysis:** Manis AI ingests call recordings → outputs objection patterns, closer performance, prospect motivations
- **Client communication templates:** CSM uses AI to draft check-in messages, accountability nudges, and follow-up notes
- **Deal analysis (Amazon OS):** The existing sourcing pipeline (`fast_grocery_scan.py`, `deal_scanner.py`) IS AI in action for the coaching offer — students learn the tool as part of the curriculum

**The Poppy AI + Claude stack (Ben Bader's method):**
1. Scrape all client content (YouTube, Instagram) into Poppy AI
2. Add proven framework (VSSL script, email guide, webinar structure)
3. Connect both to Claude chat
4. Prompt: "Write [deliverable] for [client] in [client's] voice using [framework]"
5. Result: 80-90% complete, human finalizes

**Sabbo note:** The existing nomad-nebula execution scripts are the AI-in-action layer for Agency OS. When onboarding an agency client, the Python-powered sourcing pipeline and dashboard become part of the DFY deliverable — not just back-office tools.

---

## 5. AI TOOLS AS RETENTION MOAT

> **Root:** Sabbo-specific

### The Core Insight

Both of Sabbo's offers generate proprietary AI tools as a side effect of the work:

- **Agency OS:** The growth tracking dashboard, sourcing pipeline, and automation scripts built for clients become assets that are difficult to replicate without Sabbo
- **Amazon OS:** The deal scanner (`fast_grocery_scan.py`), profitability calculator, and live sourcing pipeline give coaching students a technical edge that generic Amazon courses cannot provide

This is not just a fulfillment mechanism — it's a **retention moat.** Canceling the engagement means losing access to tools that are generating real, tangible results. The switching cost becomes real.

---

### How to Deploy This Strategically

#### For Agency OS Clients

**Month 1 delivery: The Growth OS Dashboard**
- Custom tracking sheet (Looker Studio) showing acquisition metrics, funnel performance, and client LTV in real time
- Agency clients see their data in a way they've never seen it before — this creates immediate stickiness
- Canceling means losing the dashboard and the operator who knows how to read it

**Month 1-3: Automation Stack**
- Zapier workflows connecting their CRM, email platform, ad accounts, and calendar
- Slack notification system for lead alerts
- Custom scripts adapted from the nomad-nebula execution layer for their specific use case
- Each automation represents hours of work that disappear on cancellation

**Ongoing: Proprietary Reporting**
- Monthly Growth OS Report (custom-generated, not a template)
- Shows exactly which acquisition channels are performing and where to allocate next month's budget
- Clients cannot replicate this without the operator who built the underlying tracking

**How to present this in sales:** "At the end of 30 days, you'll have a full growth intelligence system — not just a marketing service. Your entire acquisition funnel will be tracked, automated, and visible in real time. Canceling the retainer doesn't just lose the operator; it loses the system."

---

#### For Amazon OS Coaching Students

**The 24/7 Profits Deal Pipeline (student access):**
- Students get access to the live `fast_grocery_scan.py` pipeline outputs — curated deal alerts from Target, Walgreens, and Walmart, pre-analyzed for profitability
- Each deal comes with: buy link, Amazon price, estimated FBA fees, net profit, ROI, and a BUY/MAYBE/SKIP verdict
- This is a continuous stream of sourced opportunities — the program never "ends" while deals keep coming

**Why this drives retention to the long-tail:**
- The $197/month community access (Big Head, Long Tail model) gets students continued access to deal alerts
- Students who are actively buying profitable products will not cancel a service generating those opportunities
- The tool access creates a clear, quantifiable ROI: if one deal per month generates $500 net profit, the tool access pays for itself 2.5x

**Proprietary advantages that can't be commoditized:**
- Custom `normalize_pack_size()` logic that adjusts profitability for multi-packs vs. singles
- Direct buy links (non-negotiable — Sabbo's standing directive) so students can act immediately
- Keepa integration showing BSR trends and historical price data
- Playwright-based retailer scraping that circumvents pricing API limitations

**Framing in onboarding:** "While you're in the program, you're getting live deal flow from a proprietary sourcing engine. Most Amazon courses give you a method. We give you the deals. The difference is $500-$2,000/month in additional profit per student while they're learning."

---

### Building Tool Dependency the Right Way

The goal is NOT to trap clients — it's to genuinely create more value through tools than they could create without them. When the tool is generating real money, retention is not a manipulation; it's a natural outcome of value delivery.

**Signs you've built the right tool-based moat:**
1. Clients reference the tool when asked why they're staying
2. Cancellation conversations start with "but what about access to [tool]?"
3. Clients recommend you specifically because of the tool ("other agencies don't have this")
4. Students track deals from the pipeline in their onboarding homework within the first week

**Anti-pattern:** Building tools that are impressive demos but don't generate tangible, measurable results. The moat only works if the tools work.

---

## 6. THE CHAIN MECHANISM

> **Root:** Nik Setting — 4 chains at 100% simultaneously

### The Framework

Every business has four connected chains. These chains form a cycle. If any one receives zero attention while you focus on the others, the entire system underperforms — and revenue becomes a roller coaster.

```
OFFER → ACQUISITION → SALES/CONVERSION → FULFILLMENT
```

**The core problem (Nik Setting):** Founders oscillate between acquisition and fulfillment. When creating content and running ads (acquisition), client delivery gets neglected. When fulfilling clients, acquisition stops completely. The result: spike to $80K, drop to $20K, spike again. Month-to-month volatility kills forecasting and team morale.

> "This is the #1 reason info businesses have inconsistent revenue." — Nik Setting

---

### The Four Chains in Detail

#### Chain 1: Offer
**What it is:** What you sell, how it's priced, and whether it solves a real problem.

**Failure mode:** Changing the offer constantly instead of fixing the other three chains. "Offer hopping" (Hormozi's term) — changing what you sell every year instead of fixing retention.

**100% attention means:** Quarterly offer audits. Survey (the two-question Hormozi survey). A/B test pricing annually. Update positioning based on what the market is actually saying in sales calls and DMs.

---

#### Chain 2: Acquisition
**What it is:** Traffic, content, ads — everything that gets eyes on the offer.

**Failure mode:** Going dark on content during intense fulfillment periods, causing lead flow to collapse 60-90 days later (the 90-day lag — SooWei's principle: "What you do today shows up in 90 days").

**100% attention means:** A content calendar with 8+ pieces in backlog at all times. Automated ad campaigns that run whether or not you're posting that week. A setter who handles DM outreach daily. The founder is NOT required for this chain to run at 100%.

---

#### Chain 3: Sales/Conversion
**What it is:** Everything between a lead expressing interest and a client paying.

**Failure mode:** Call volume drops when the founder is overwhelmed with delivery. Setter has no one to report to. Closer takes days off without coverage.

**100% attention means:** A trained closer who handles all calls. A setter who manages DMs without the founder. CRM with automated follow-ups so no lead goes cold. EOD reports reviewed by the sales manager (not the founder) daily.

---

#### Chain 4: Fulfillment
**What it is:** Delivery, retention, results — everything after the client pays.

**Failure mode:** The founder is always in fulfillment because there's no system. This makes acquisition impossible and creates the revenue roller coaster.

**100% attention means:** A CSM who handles client communication and check-ins. A Notion roadmap that clients self-navigate. Group calls that don't require the founder to be active in every conversation. AI tools that deliver ongoing value (deal alerts, dashboard) without manual effort.

---

### The Simultaneity Solution

All four chains must receive 100% attention at the same time. This is impossible for one person. It requires:

**Team structure (minimum viable for simultaneity):**
```
FOUNDER (Sabbo): Offer design, strategic client work, high-level content
CSM: Fulfillment chain — client check-ins, accountability, community
SETTER: Acquisition chain (outbound) + Sales chain (lead qualification)
CLOSER: Sales chain (calls + closes)
```

**Automation filling the gaps:**
- Email sequences running 24/7 (nurture + post-booking + reactivation)
- CRM with automated follow-ups and status updates
- Slack notification bots for lead alerts
- Looker Studio dashboards refreshing automatically
- Deal scanner running on schedule (Amazon OS)

**The benchmark question (Nik Setting):** "Which chain is getting 0% attention right now while I'm working on another?" That's the chain to fix first.

---

### Diagnosing Chain Failures

| Symptom | Broken Chain | Fix |
|---|---|---|
| Revenue spikes then collapses | Acquisition | Content backlog, automated ads, setter KPIs |
| Leads not converting to calls | Sales/Conversion | Show rate optimization, pre-call nurture |
| Calls not closing | Sales/Conversion | Call analysis, closer training, pricing audit |
| Clients churning fast | Fulfillment | Onboarding redesign, activation point work |
| No referrals or testimonials | Fulfillment | Milestone journey, ACA framework reach-outs |
| Pricing pressure from competitors | Offer | Reposition, raise prices, add guarantees |

---

## 7. REMOVING KEY MAN RISK

> **Root:** Alex Hormozi — 5-step process + Phone Test

### Why This Is an Existential Risk for Both Offers

If Sabbo is the product — the person running every client call, writing every piece of content, analyzing every deal, closing every sale — then:

1. The business cannot grow beyond what one person can physically handle
2. The business has zero exit or acquisition value (you can't sell a job)
3. A health issue, travel, or personal crisis stops all revenue
4. Every client becomes aware that their results depend entirely on Sabbo's capacity

"I have yet to see a business not grow when they implement the Rule of 100. I have yet to see a business pass the phone test unless they've systemized delivery." — Hormozi

**The Phone Test:**
- Leave for 3 months with no involvement.
- **Business shrinks** = key man dependent (most agencies and coaching businesses at this stage)
- **Business stays flat** = systems are working but growth is on pause (acceptable)
- **Business grows** = you have a sellable, scalable company

The goal is to pass the Phone Test. Everything in this section is the path to passing it.

---

### The 5-Step Key Man Removal Process

#### Step 1: Self-Inventory (Time Study)

Spend one week logging every task you do in 15-minute intervals.

Then categorize every task:
- **Green (delegate now):** Tasks that any trained person can do with a written SOP
- **Yellow (build process first):** Tasks that need documentation before delegation
- **Red (hire specifically for):** Tasks requiring a specific skill set you don't have, or that you should hire away from yourself as a priority

**Common findings for Sabbo:**
```
Green (delegate now):
- Client check-ins and accountability tracking → CSM
- EOD report review → Sales Manager
- Deal alert email compilation → Automated pipeline
- Social media scheduling → VA

Yellow (build process first):
- Client onboarding calls → Document script, train CSM, then delegate Call 1 and Call 2
- Content ideation → Build content calendar SOP, then delegate to editor/strategist

Red (hire for):
- Sales calls (closer) → Hire and train one dedicated closer
- Ad management → Hire media buyer or agency
- Community moderation → Full-time CSM role
```

---

#### Step 2: Decision Trees for Common Scenarios

For every recurring decision you currently make, build an if/then decision tree.

**Template:**
```
IF [situation] AND [condition]
THEN [action]
OTHERWISE [escalate to Sabbo]
```

**Agency OS examples:**
```
IF client requests scope change AND change < 10% of retainer value
THEN CSM approves and documents

IF client requests scope change AND change > 10%
THEN CSM documents, escalates to Sabbo within 24 hours

IF client misses two consecutive check-in calls
THEN CSM sends recovery protocol (specific message template)
THEN flags in Slack for Sabbo review

IF client requests cancellation
THEN CSM books cancellation call within 48 hours
THEN follows Hormozi cancellation call script
THEN escalates outcome to Sabbo
```

**Amazon OS examples:**
```
IF student asks whether to buy a specific deal
AND the deal meets all five criteria (BSR, ROI, buy links, brand, competition)
THEN CSM confirms: "Go for it — this meets the criteria"

IF deal is borderline (MAYBE verdict from scanner)
THEN CSM escalates to Sabbo for same-day review

IF student hasn't posted content in 10+ days
THEN CSM sends accountability message
THEN books a recovery call
```

Build these trees into Notion pages. Every team member can reference them without asking you.

---

#### Step 3: Shadow → Supervise → Support (Training Protocol)

For every task being transferred from Sabbo to a team member, use this three-phase handoff:

**Phase 1: Shadow (1-2 weeks)**
- Team member watches Sabbo do the task (recorded via Fathom or Loom)
- Team member takes notes and builds their own SOP
- Team member asks clarifying questions after, not during

**Phase 2: Supervise (2-4 weeks)**
- Team member does the task while Sabbo watches (or reviews async)
- Sabbo gives real-time feedback and corrections
- Standard: 3 perfect executions in a row before advancing to Phase 3

**Phase 3: Support (ongoing)**
- Team member operates independently
- Sabbo is available for edge cases only (not routine questions)
- Weekly 15-minute check-in to surface patterns and improvements

**The test for Phase 3 readiness:** "Can they handle the 5 most common scenarios without asking me?" If yes, they're ready. If not, more Phase 2 reps.

---

#### Step 4: Remove Yourself from Marketing

This is the hardest step for most founders, but the most important for scale. The business cannot depend on Sabbo being the face of all content indefinitely.

**Hormozi's 7 Systems for Founder-Independent Marketing:**

1. **Weekly social proof screenshots** → Run as ads. Automate: CSM collects, media buyer runs
2. **Incentivized testimonials** → Credit toward next month, tier upgrade, community recognition
3. **Lifecycle ads** → Compress the client journey into a timeline ad (they joined → first result → milestone → testimonial). Film once, runs forever.
4. **Key moment documentation** → Every client win is filmed and added to the ad library
5. **Customer support paid per mini-testimonial** → CSM earns bonus for every client win documented
6. **Community and review mining** → Mine Skool community wins and DMs for ad copy (with permission)
7. **Affiliate/referral program** → Existing clients send referrals; they earn credit toward services

**For Amazon OS specifically:**
- Student deal-sourcing results become content: "Student found a $847 profit deal in 15 minutes using the pipeline"
- Anonymous or named — the pipeline becomes the star, not just Sabbo
- The tools prove themselves and market the offer independently

---

#### Step 5: Install 7 Marketing Systems That Don't Require Your Face

Each of these should be running independently within 6 months:

```
1. Email sequences (automated, AI-written in Sabbo's voice)
2. Ad campaigns (managed by media buyer, optimized weekly)
3. Content calendar (executed by VA/editor, approved by Sabbo async)
4. Referral program (CSM manages, automated tracking)
5. Community-generated content (CSM surfaces wins, moderates quality)
6. Lifecycle video ads (filmed quarterly, evergreen)
7. Lead magnet + automated follow-up sequence (runs 24/7 without intervention)
```

**Target:** Sabbo spends 1 day per week on delivery, 1-2 days on high-level strategy and content, and the rest of the calendar is protected deep work or genuine time off.

---

### Selling the Systemized Version (Key Man Risk as a Sales Asset)

Paradoxically, removing key man risk makes the agency MORE attractive to buy and MORE convincing to pitch:

**Agency pitch:** "We don't build campaigns that depend on a single person. We install a growth operating system — documented, automated, and transferable. When you hire us, you're getting a system, not a person. If our team member changes, your system doesn't."

**This addresses one of the biggest fears of 7-8 figure founders:** They've been burned by agencies where one account manager left and took all the institutional knowledge. Positioning the system as the product (not Sabbo personally) solves this objection before it's raised.

---

## 8. CSM INCENTIVE STRUCTURE

> **Root:** Nik Setting — base + referral + renewal + testimonial bonuses

### Why Incentive Structure Is a Retention Mechanism

The CSM (Client Success Manager) is the primary human touchpoint for every retained client. Their incentives must be perfectly aligned with the outcomes that drive business growth: referrals, renewals, testimonials, and client wins.

A flat-salary CSM has no financial reason to go above and beyond. A bonus-structured CSM has every reason to care.

Nik Setting's insight: "Sit down and visually show the CSM the math so they see the vision." When a CSM understands that their total comp can hit $8-10K/month (on a $3K base) by doing the things that also make clients successful, they operate with founder-level intent.

---

### The CSM Incentive Structure

**Base Compensation:**
- **$3,000/month** (or local equivalent) — full-time, dedicated CSM
- This is the floor. The ceiling is determined by performance.

**Bonus Components:**

| Bonus | Amount | Trigger | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| Referral commission | 10% | Per referred client who pays | CSM facilitates referral conversation, Sabbo closes |
| Payment plan renewal | 5% | Per client who renews their payment plan | Applies to both agency retainer renewals and coaching renewals |
| Upsell commission | Negotiated % | Per upsold offer | Example: 5% of the upsell value |
| Testimonial bonus | $250 | Per video or written testimonial secured | Must be usable in marketing |
| Client win bonus | $100 | Per documented client win added to the win library | Screenshot, brief description, client name |

**Example monthly earnings breakdown:**
```
Base: $3,000
3 referrals closed at $7,500 avg x 10% = $2,250
2 retainer renewals at $10,000 x 5% = $1,000
1 upsell at $5,000 x 5% = $250
4 testimonials x $250 = $1,000
6 client wins x $100 = $600

Total comp: $8,100/month
Total generated for business from these activities: $22,500 (new) + $20,000 (renewals) + $5,000 (upsell) = $47,500+ in revenue influenced
CSM ROI: 5.9x on their total cost
```

---

### CSM Role Definition

**Primary responsibilities:**

1. **Onboarding Execution** — Run Call 1 (72-hour sequence). Manage the Notion roadmap. Track accountability metrics.

2. **Ongoing Client Communication** — Weekly check-in touchpoints with every active client. ACA framework (Acknowledge, Compliment, Ask) for regular reach-outs.

3. **Usage Churn Prevention** — Monitor engagement dashboard weekly. Flag clients whose engagement drops (calls missed, no content posted, no deals submitted). Initiate recovery protocol for disengaged clients immediately.

4. **Testimonial Collection** — After every client win, request documentation. Video preferred. Written acceptable. Timing: ask within 48 hours of the win while the emotional peak is highest.

5. **Referral Facilitation** — After client hits their first major milestone, explicitly ask: "Who do you know who's trying to solve the same problem you were six weeks ago?" Make the introduction frictionless.

6. **Renewal Preparation** — 30 days before any renewal date, CSM prepares a "Results Report" for that client: milestones hit, ROI generated, next-phase opportunity. Presents this to the client and to Sabbo for the renewal conversation.

7. **Community Moderation** — Pin wins. Facilitate connections between members. Flag toxic behavior for correction. Surface the best content to amplify (Hormozi: pin the top 1-2 posts, publicly praise the poster).

---

### CSM Onboarding (First 30 Days)

**Week 1: Systems and Knowledge**
- Full access to all client files, Notion roadmaps, and CRM
- Shadow Sabbo on 3-5 client calls (all recorded via Fathom)
- Read and quiz on: Retention SOP, Onboarding sequence, ACA framework, Cancellation call script
- Set up all tools: Slack, CRM, tracking sheet, calendar, community platform

**Week 2: Supervised Execution**
- CSM runs 3 client check-ins with Sabbo reviewing async (via Fathom recording)
- CSM reviews one client tracking dashboard and flags any at-risk clients
- CSM sends first round of ACA-framework touchpoints, Sabbo reviews tone and quality

**Week 3: Independent Execution**
- CSM runs all routine client touchpoints independently
- Escalation protocol live: any client flagged as high-churn-risk → Sabbo briefed within 24 hours
- First testimonial request attempt (CSM guided)

**Week 4: Full Ownership**
- CSM takes ownership of all fulfillment chain communications
- Weekly report to Sabbo: clients at risk, clients winning, referrals in progress, testimonials collected
- First bonus earned (if applicable)

---

### Scaling the CSM Role

As the client roster grows past 20 active clients, the single CSM model breaks. The expansion path:

**20-30 clients:** One senior CSM handles strategy and risk; one junior CSM or VA handles routine check-ins and tracking

**30-50 clients:** CSM team of 3, each owning a defined cohort. Senior CSM manages the team and reports to Sabbo.

**50+ clients:** Dedicated community manager (separate from CSM), full CSM team, and an Ops Manager who owns the fulfillment chain entirely.

**The goal:** At 50+ clients, Sabbo's fulfillment involvement is limited to: (1) high-stakes cancellation saves, (2) recording monthly group calls, (3) 1-on-1 calls with top 10% clients only.

---

## PUTTING IT ALL TOGETHER

### The Fulfillment Stack — How Everything Connects

```
CLIENT PAYS
    ↓
72-Hour Onboarding (SooWei: 3 calls, 3 specialists)
    ↓
Activation Point Sprint (Hormozi: drive to first result in 30 days)
    ↓
Incentivized Milestones (Hormozi: Activate → Testimonial → Refer → Ascend)
    ↓
Community Linking (Hormozi: mesh network, not hub-and-spoke)
    ↓
AI Tools Running in Background (Sabbo: deal alerts, dashboards, automations)
    ↓
Chain Mechanism Running at 100% (Nik Setting: all 4 chains simultaneously)
    ↓
CSM Managing the Relationship (Nik Setting: bonus-aligned retention engine)
    ↓
Usage Churn Monitoring (Hormozi: flag disengaged clients immediately)
    ↓
Cancellation Call SOP (Hormozi: save ~50% of attempted cancellations)
    ↓
Renewal / Ascension (Hormozi: Crazy Eight, Big Head Long Tail)
    ↓
Referral Request at Peak Satisfaction (SooWei: timing is everything)
    ↓
KEY MAN RISK REMOVED (Hormozi: Phone Test passed, business is sellable)
```

---

### The North Star Metrics for Fulfillment

**Agency OS:**
- Monthly churn rate: Target < 3%
- Average client LTV: Target > $150K
- Activation rate (clients who get results in 30 days): Target > 80%
- Testimonials collected: Target 2+ per client
- Referrals per 10 clients: Target 3+
- CSM satisfaction response time: < 4 hours

**Amazon OS:**
- Time to first deal sourced: Target < 14 days
- 90-day program completion rate: Target > 80%
- Long-tail conversion rate (program → $197/month community): Target > 50%
- Student revenue generated in first 90 days: Track as portfolio metric
- Testimonials collected: Target 1 per student
- Student-to-student referrals: Track and incentivize

---

### The Business This Creates

When the fulfillment system works, this is what compounds:
- Client stays longer → LTV increases → CAC becomes irrelevant
- Client gets results → Testimonial → More qualified leads attracted
- Client refers someone → New acquisition with zero CAC
- Client buys more → Ascension → Revenue grows without new clients
- Key man risk removed → Business passes Phone Test → Sellable or scalable

"When you implement the churn checklist and keep your customers, you grow every year no matter what, even if your sales stay the same. Your business compounds. You sleep knowing your bills are paid. You get positive word of mouth. You keep the best talent because they see you're actually helping people." — Hormozi

The inverse is also true, and it compounds in the wrong direction. High churn forces a hamster wheel of constant acquisition just to stay flat. It destroys team morale when they see clients failing. It makes the business unsellable. And it prevents the kind of deep product iteration that comes from long-term client relationships.

**Fulfillment is not the back office. It is the business.**

# PART 6: THE MATH

> "If you put $1 in and get $34 out in 48 hours — is that good?" / "It's amazing." — Alex Hormozi, $25K mentor call
> "82% of businesses fail due to poor cash flow. If you've got no money, you've got no business." — Hormozi, $100M Money Models Launch

---

## 6.1 Money Models [root: Hormozi — $100M Money Models launch]

### What Is a Money Model?

A money model is your monetization structure — how you collect money, how you charge for what you do. Most businesses fail not because their product is bad, but because their money model is broken.

Hormozi's core definition:
> "A money model gets more customers to spend more money in less time, over and over again."

The $100M Money Models framework is built on a single insight: **the sequence in which you make money determines whether you can keep making money.** A good money model means the cost of getting a customer is recovered before the next month's costs are due. A bad one means you're always behind.

**The Four Things You Can Sell:**
1. Software
2. Information
3. Services
4. Physical products

Money models work in all four. Sabbo operates in Information (#2) and Services (#3). Both have high margins, low delivery costs, and can be priced using value-based pricing — the only model that scales.

---

### The Business Genie Framework: The Most Powerful Lever [root: Hormozi, pricing.md]

Hormozi poses a thought experiment: A genie offers to double ONE aspect of your business. Which do you pick?

- Option A: 2x number of new customers
- Option B: 2x how many times they buy (retention)
- Option C: 2x your prices

All three double revenue. But they do NOT produce equal profit.

**Baseline:** 30 clients/mo, 33% churn (3-month avg), $100/mo price, 20% net margin, $10K revenue, $2K profit.

| Option | Revenue | Profit | Profit Multiplier |
|---|---|---|---|
| A: Double new customers | $20,000 | $7,000 | 3.5x |
| B: Double retention | $20,000 | $7,000 | 3.5x |
| **C: Double prices** | **$20,000** | **$12,000** | **6x** |

**Why Option C wins:** Revenue doubles AND costs stay the same. Gross margin goes from 50% to 75%. Net margins go from 20% to 60%. ZERO additional CAC. ZERO additional delivery costs.

**Profitwell data (512 companies):**
| Growth Lever | Impact on Bottom Line per 1% Improvement |
|---|---|
| Acquisition | 3.32% |
| Retention | 6.71% |
| **Pricing (Monetization)** | **12.7%** |

Pricing is 4x more efficient than acquisition at improving profit. This is why Sabbo's pricing must be non-negotiable, not negotiated down on every call.

---

### The Three Pricing Models [root: Hormozi, pricing.md]

| Model | What It Is | Problem |
|---|---|---|
| Cost Plus | Costs + arbitrary margin | You miss customers who'd pay more |
| Competitor Based | Average of what everyone charges | You're a copycat — "Hard to make a shoe fit when it's not yours" |
| **Value Based** | What the customer is willing to pay | **THIS IS THE GOAL** |

> "People usually price by looking at what everyone else charges. This is the recipe for break even and burnout. You run a nonprofit with none of the benefits."

**Value-based pricing formula:** Value = (Dream Outcome x Perceived Likelihood) / (Time Delay x Effort & Sacrifice)

To charge more, either increase the numerator (bigger outcome, more believable) or decrease the denominator (faster, easier).

---

### Hormozi's Pricing Rules [root: Hormozi, pricing.md]

These rules govern all pricing decisions for both offers.

| Rule | Statement |
|---|---|
| 1 | Raising prices makes you money TWO ways: more gross profit per customer + fewer customers to serve. Revenue up, costs down simultaneously. |
| 2 | Price to maximize total lifetime profit, not first-purchase conversion. |
| 3 | High close rate = underpriced. Below 50% is target. |
| 4 | Full capacity = underpriced. Raise immediately. |
| 5 | Keep raising until extra revenue from new sales no longer offsets lost sales. |
| 6 | Different prices for different customer types. Name tiers after aspirational titles. |
| 7 | Believe in your price. If you don't, make the offer better until you do. |
| 8 | Bill less frequently to reduce churn. The longer the billing cycle, the fewer cancellation opportunities. |
| 9 | Display price in smallest increment, bill on longest increment. |
| 10 | Match billing frequency to value delivery. One-time value = one-time fee. Ongoing value = recurring fee. |

**Close Rate Diagnostic [root: Hormozi]:**

| Close Rate | What It Means | Action |
|---|---|---|
| 80%+ | Underpriced by 3-4x | Raise price immediately |
| 60-80% | Underpriced by 2-3x | Raise price |
| 50-60% | Underpriced by 1.5-2x | Raise price |
| 40-50% | Underpriced by 1.25-1.5x | Small raise |
| **30-40%** | **Appropriately priced** | **Hold** |
| Below 30% | Fix selling or avatar, not price | Do not change price |

---

### The LTV:CAC Framework [root: Hormozi]

The ratio of customer lifetime value to cost of acquisition determines whether a business can scale.

| Human Touch Points in Delivery | Target LTV:CAC |
|---|---|
| 0 (full automation: ads → checkout → software) | 3:1 |
| 1 human in loop (salesperson OR manual delivery) | 6:1 |
| 2 humans in loop (salesperson + service delivery) | 9:1 |
| 3 humans in loop (outbound + sales + service) | 12:1 |

Sabbo's businesses both have 2-3 humans in the loop (setter + closer + Sabbo/team). Target LTV:CAC = **9:1 minimum, 12:1 goal.**

**Application:**
- Agency: $18K/mo avg × 12-month avg = $216K LTV. Target CAC ≤ $24K. At $10K ad spend/month to generate 1 new client, CAC = $10K. LTV:CAC = 21.6:1. Exceptional.
- Coaching: $7K enrollment + $3K recurring (avg 6 months) = $10K LTV. Target CAC ≤ $1,100. At $10K/mo ad spend generating 10 students, CAC = $1,000. LTV:CAC = 10:1. Strong.

---

### The Instant Profit Pricing Playbook [root: Hormozi, pricing.md]

These pricing plays can add 26.8% to 63.8% to revenue with minimal impact on sales.

| Pricing Play | Revenue Increase |
|---|---|
| Monthly → 28-day billing cycles | 8.3% |
| Credit card processing fee (3-4%) | 3-4% |
| Sales tax passthrough | 0-10% |
| Annual CPI increase (3-10%) | 3-10% |
| Longer-duration billing options | 10-15% |
| Annual renewal fee on top of monthly | 10% |
| Ultra high option (anchoring) | 10-15% |
| Priced guarantee or warranty | 5-20% |
| **TOTAL POSSIBLE** | **26.8% - 63.8%** |

> Average US small business runs 7-10% net margins. Adding 26.8% pricing optimization could be a 6x+ increase in profit.

**Sabbo Application:** A $200K/mo business with 70% gross margin at 30% net margin = $60K/month profit. Apply even a conservative 15% pricing optimization (28-day billing + processing fee + annual increase) = $230K/mo revenue, margins hold, profit = $90K/mo. That is $30K/mo additional profit from pricing alone — no new clients, no new content, no new ads.

---

## 6.2 Revenue Architecture: The $200K/Month Breakdown

### The Split

**Coaching-first model with agency as compounding MRR layer.** This reflects the current growth strategy: prove coaching at scale first (existing proof of concept), then layer agency MRR on top as coaching case studies build credibility with 7–8 figure founders. Follows Hormozi's top-down pricing principle and Ben Bader's Phase 4 operator model (revshare compounds; retainers cap).

**Target: $70K Coaching + $130K Agency = $200K/month**

Coaching provides the velocity, cash-in-hand, and social proof to fund ad spend and build the credibility layer needed for premium agency positioning. Agency provides the stable MRR floor once the coaching machine is running. Each offer makes the other easier to sell (coaching volume creates case studies and social proof for agency; agency results generate referrals back to coaching).

---

### Agency Revenue Model

**Pricing Tiers:**

| Tier | Price | Target Client | Expected Volume |
|---|---|---|---|
| Core retainer | $15K/mo | 7-figure founder, needs full growth OS installed | 4-5 clients |
| Premium retainer | $25K/mo | 8-figure founder, operator-level embed | 2-3 clients |
| Setup fee (one-time) | $10K-$15K | All new clients | 1 per month |
| Revshare bonus | 10-15% of incremental revenue above baseline | High-ceiling clients | 1-2 clients |

**Agency Revenue Math:**
```
Active clients:             7 (steady state, month 6+)
Average retainer:           $18K/mo
Monthly recurring:          $126,000
Setup fees (1 new/mo):      $12,000
Revshare bonuses:           ~$5,000
                            ─────────
Total Agency MRR:           ~$143,000/month
```

**Agency Unit Economics:**
```
Average retainer:           $18,000/mo
Team cost per client:       $4,000/mo (senior operator + tools + overhead)
Gross profit per client:    $14,000/mo
Gross margin:               78%

CAC (agency):               ~$5,000-$15,000 (high-touch outreach, 1-3 calls to close)
LTV (avg 12-month retain):  $216,000
LTV:CAC ratio:              14-43:1 (target floor: 12:1)

Break-even timeline:        First retainer payment covers all acquisition costs
```

**Churn Target [Hormozi]:** <5% monthly. At 7 clients, max 0.35 churns per month. Target: 1 churn every 3-4 months, replaced immediately by the outreach pipeline.

---

### Amazon FBA Coaching Revenue Model

**Pricing Tiers:**

| Tier | Price | What They Get | Primary Market |
|---|---|---|---|
| DWY Coaching (core) | $7,000 | 90-day program, group calls, AI sourcing pipeline access, accountability | Market ONLY this |
| DIY Course | $3,000 | Self-paced course, community, basic tool access | Downsell on call if DWY not right fit |
| Premium 1-on-1 | $15,000 | Direct mentorship, custom sourcing plan, Sabbo's personal time | Upsell after DWY results proven |

**Coaching Revenue Math:**
```
New enrollments/month:          10 students
Average enrollment price:       $7,000
New cash collected:             $70,000
Recurring (community + tools):  $3,000-$5,000
                                ─────────
Total Coaching Monthly:         ~$73,000-$75,000/month
```

**Coaching Unit Economics:**
```
Enrollment price:           $7,000
Fulfillment cost/student:   $800/mo (group calls, AI pipeline compute, ops)
Gross profit per student:   $6,200 (month 1), ~$2,500/mo ongoing
Gross margin (enrollment):  89%

CAC (coaching):             $700-$1,000 (at $10K/mo ad spend, 10 students)
LTV (enrollment + 6mo recurring): $10,000
LTV:CAC ratio:              10-14:1

Payment plan impact [Hormozi]:
  Pay-in-full ($7K):        Offer 10% discount = $6,300 collected today
  3-pay ($2,500/mo):        Total = $7,500 (collect more over time)
  Default to 3-pay for most; push pay-in-full as the "deal"
```

### Combined $200K/Month Dashboard

```
                        MONTH 6 TARGET STATE

AGENCY
  7 active clients × $18K avg              = $126,000
  1 new client setup fee × $12K            = $12,000
  Revshare bonuses                         =  $5,000
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Agency Total                             = $143,000

  10 new students × $7K avg enrollment     = $70,000
  Community/tool recurring (50 students)   =  $5,000
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────

COMBINED
  Gross Revenue                            = $218,000
  Gross Profit (blended ~80% margin)       = $174,400
  Team + Ops ($30K target burn)            - $30,000
  Ad Spend ($15K target)                   - $15,000
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
  NET PROFIT (target)                      = $129,400
  Net Margin                               =    59%
```

**Why this math holds:**
- Agency is recurring, low-churn, high-margin. Once a client is in, they stay (12+ months avg).
- Coaching is volume-dependent but low fulfillment cost per student (group model, AI-assisted).
- The two offers cross-pollinate: agency clients are coaching students who made it, coaching students become agency referrals.
