## 6.3 Brand Audit Diagnosis [root: Ben Bader, July 31 call — 150-200 calls needed, volume is lever]

### The Core Diagnosis

Ben Bader's July 31 call produced the single most important insight for Sabbo's growth trajectory:

> **The bottleneck is NOT sales. The bottleneck is TRAFFIC and VOLUME.**

This is counterintuitive. Most founders think they have a closing problem. They practice scripts. They hire better closers. They tweak offers. But if they're only running 20-30 calls per month, no amount of sales improvement will produce the volume of clients and students needed to hit $200K/mo.

**The math is brutally simple:**

```
Target: $200K/month
Avg blended deal value: $7K-$18K (coaching + agency)
New cash needed from new clients/students per month: ~$82K

At $7K avg coaching + $18K avg agency:
  Coaching: 10 new students = $70K
  Agency:   1 new client/mo = $18K (MRR addition)

Total new sales needed/month: 11 deals

At 40% close rate: 11 ÷ 0.40 = 27.5 → ~28 sales calls needed per month
At 30% close rate: 11 ÷ 0.30 = 36.7 → ~37 sales calls needed per month

BUT — show rates are not 100%.
At 70% show rate: 28 closed calls ÷ 0.70 = 40 booked calls needed
At 70% show rate: 37 closed calls ÷ 0.70 = 53 booked calls needed

PLUS — not all leads qualify.
At 50% qualification rate: 40 ÷ 0.50 = 80 conversations needed
At 50% qualification rate: 53 ÷ 0.50 = 106 conversations needed
```

**Ben Bader's thesis:** To hit and sustain targets with a buffer for churn, missed closes, and variance, you need **150-200 sales calls per month** — not 28-53. The difference between "doing okay" and "scaling reliably" is that buffer. You need the pipeline to be so full that a bad month still produces enough closed deals.

---

### The Volume Math: 150-200 Calls/Month

**At 200 calls/month with 40% close rate:**
```
200 calls × 40% close rate    = 80 deals closed/month
80 deals × $7K avg (coaching) = $560,000/month (hypothetical ceiling)

Realistic blended (not all coaching):
  70% coaching × 80 deals × $7K  = $392,000
  30% agency    × 80 deals = 24 agency clients (not realistic to absorb)

Correction: Volume creates OPTIONS.
- You pick the best 10-12 coaching students (capacity constraint)
- You pick the best 1-2 agency clients per month
- You create a waitlist (massive positioning advantage)
- You raise prices (close rate is 40% = still appropriately priced at $7K, hold)
```

**At 150 calls/month with 35% close rate (conservative):**
```
150 calls × 35% close rate    = 52.5 → 52 deals/month
Coaching (40 students × $7K)  = $280,000
Agency (12 clients × $18K)    = $216,000 MRR potential (pipe, not all close same month)

Month 6 realistic:
  10 coaching students/mo × $7K    = $70,000
  1 new agency client/mo × $18K    = $18,000 (adds to MRR, compounding)
  + existing 6 agency clients' MRR = $108,000
  TOTAL                            = $196,000
```

**The conclusion is clear: volume creates optionality.** With 150-200 calls/month, Sabbo can be selective, raise prices, build a waitlist, and compound MRR. Without it, every month is feast-or-famine.

---

### How to Get to 200 Calls/Month: The Acquisition Waterfall

Every booked call traces back to a daily action. This is the full waterfall:

```
DAILY ACTIONS (5-7 hours of input)
  Content: 1 long-form video (YouTube) + 2-3 short clips (Instagram/Reels)
  Outreach: Setter sends 150 DMs/day (50 new followers + 50 warm + 50 follow-ups)
  Ads: Active campaigns running at $300-$500/day

          ↓

WEEKLY VOLUME (inputs × 7 days)
  Content pieces published: 5-7 short-form, 1 long-form
  DM conversations initiated: 1,050/week
  Ad impressions: $2,100-$3,500 spend → ~100K-250K impressions

          ↓

PIPELINE (conversion benchmarks)
  DM conversations → qualified: 20% → 210 qualified/week
  Qualified → booked call: 25% → 52 booked calls/week
  Booked calls → showed: 70% → 36 showed/week

          ↓

MONTHLY OUTPUT
  Showed calls: 36 × 4.3 weeks = ~155 calls/month ✓
  (Target: 150-200 calls/month — Ben Bader's threshold)

          ↓

CLOSED DEALS (at 35-40% close rate)
  155 calls × 37% = 57 deals/month

  Managed to capacity:
    Coaching: 10 students enrolled/month → $70,000
    Agency: 1-2 new clients/month → +$18-36K MRR
```

**The math validates Ben Bader's diagnosis.** The acquisition waterfall above — 1,050 DM conversations per week, consistent content, $300-500/day in ads — produces the 150-200 calls per month needed. Without this VOLUME of daily inputs, the numbers simply cannot work at scale.

---

### What Breaks the Waterfall (And How to Fix It)

**Break Point 1: DM conversation volume < 150/day**
- Symptom: Fewer than 30 booked calls/week
- Fix: Hire setter immediately (Month 1 hire). Setter handles 150 DMs/day. Sabbo cannot do this alone AND produce content AND close deals.

**Break Point 2: Booked → showed rate < 60%**
- Symptom: Calendar is full but calls don't happen
- Fix: Implement Hammer Them strategy [Jeremy Haynes] — content ads running 24/7 to booked leads + iPhone selfie video from setter within 1 hour of booking + 5-email confirmation sequence
- Show Rate Math [Ben Bader]: Improving from 50% → 70% show rate with 100 booked calls = 20 extra calls = 8 more deals at 40% close = $56K additional revenue per month at $7K avg

**Break Point 3: Content → DM conversation rate too low**
- Symptom: Profile has views but DMs don't initiate
- Fix: Profile funnel optimization [Nik Setting] — bio CTA, pinned posts, "Start Here" highlight, single link in bio to YouTube

**Break Point 4: Close rate below 25%**
- Symptom: Lots of calls, few closes
- Fix per Hormozi: Do NOT lower price. Fix the avatar (wrong people on calls) or fix the sales process (pre-call warm-up). At below 30%, the issue is never price.

---

## 6.4 Unit Economics by Offer

### Growth Agency: Full Unit Economics Stack

```
ACQUISITION
  Channel mix:          Outreach (primary), content (secondary), referrals (bonus)
  CAC target:           $5,000-$15,000 per client (high-touch, long-cycle)
  Sales cycle:          2-4 weeks (1-2 discovery calls + proposal + close)
  Close rate target:    30-40% on qualified calls
  Calls to close:       2.5-3.3 qualified calls per closed client

ECONOMICS PER CLIENT
  Average retainer:     $18,000/month
  Setup fee (one-time): $12,000
  First-month cash:     $30,000 (setup + first retainer)
  Monthly gross profit: $14,000 (78% margin, $4K team/ops cost)
  LTV (12-month avg):   $216,000 + $12K setup = $228,000
  CAC breakeven:        First month (30-day payback) ✓

PORTFOLIO VIEW (7 clients)
  Monthly retainers:    $126,000
  New client setup:     $12,000
  Revshare bonuses:     $5,000
  Monthly gross profit: ~$109,000
  Team cost (7 clients × $4K): $28,000
  Net from agency:      $81,000/month

SCALING LEVER
  Adding client #8:     +$18K revenue, +$14K net profit (78% incremental margin)
  Raising avg from $18K → $20K: +$14K/month revenue, nearly all profit
```

**Key constraint:** Delivery capacity. Each operator can serve 3-5 clients. At 7 clients, Sabbo needs 2 operators. Hire at 5 clients (Month 3-4).

---

### Amazon FBA Coaching: Full Unit Economics Stack

```
ACQUISITION
  Channel mix:          DMs (setter), content, webinar/challenge funnel, ads
  CAC target:           $700-$1,000 per student
  Sales cycle:          1-2 calls (faster than agency)
  Close rate target:    35-40% on qualified calls
  Calls to close:       1.2 qualified calls per enrolled student

ECONOMICS PER STUDENT (90-day program)
  Enrollment:           $7,000 (or 3-pay: $2,500 × 3 = $7,500)
  Fulfillment cost:     $800/month × 3 months = $2,400
  Gross profit:         $4,600 (enrollment) → $6,600 over 90 days (at 3-pay)
  Gross margin:         66%-94% depending on pay structure
  CAC payback:          First payment ($2,500 or $7,000) covers CAC immediately

COHORT VIEW (10 students/month)
  New enrollments:      $70,000
  Fulfillment (10 × $800): $8,000
  Net new students:     $62,000

ACTIVE STUDENT BASE (50 students in pipeline)
  Recurring (community + tools): $297-497/mo × 50 = $14,850-$24,850/mo
  Fulfillment (50 × $500 blended): $25,000
  Net recurring:        -$10,000 to -$150 (near break-even → profit after Month 3)

UPSELL ECONOMICS [Hormozi 5-10x rule, 20% uptake]
  10 students/month → 2 upgrade to Premium 1:1 ($15K)
  Monthly upsell revenue: $30,000 (when triggered, not every month)
  Blended monthly when running: +$10,000/month average

SCALING LEVER
  Challenge funnel (3 days) → 50+ registrations → 10-15 deposits → 8-10 enrollments
  One challenge event = 1-1.5 months of normal enrollment volume
```

---

## 6.5 Scaling Thresholds and Team Hiring Sequence

### The Four Phases of Growth [root: Ben Bader's 4-Phase Growth Roadmap]

| Phase | Monthly Revenue | Primary Focus | Key Unlock |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | $0 → $10K | Get reps. Take anything. Build swipe file. | First paying client or student |
| 2 | $10K → $30K | Proof and systems. Define offer. Better reporting. | Content starts helping. Systems replace memory. |
| 3 | $30K → $100K | Scale and leverage. Focus on fewer higher-paying. | First A-player hire. Sabbo out of fulfillment. |
| 4 | $100K → $200K+ | Ownership and multiplication. Compound MRR. | Sales team runs. Sabbo runs only content + strategy. |

---

### Scaling Thresholds (Specific Triggers)

**Trigger 1 — Hire Appointment Setter #1**
- Condition: Doing 10+ calls/month AND spending 2+ hours/day on DMs
- Why: Setter generates pipeline at $3-5K/month. Without one, Sabbo is the setter AND the closer AND content AND delivery. That math never works.
- Cost: $3,000/month base + $50/booked call that shows
- Expected output: 40-60 booked qualified calls/month (4-6x Sabbo's solo output)

**Trigger 2 — Hire Video Editor**
- Condition: Producing 1 YouTube video/week AND manually editing
- Why: 4-6 hours of editing per video removed = 16-24 hours/month reclaimed for content ideation + client calls
- Cost: $1,500-$3,000/month
- Expected output: 3-4 short-form clips per long-form, consistent cadence

**Trigger 3 — Hire Closer #1**
- Condition: Doing 30+ sales calls/month, closing coaching offer consistently at 35%+
- Why: Sabbo cannot close 150-200 calls/month and run the agency and make content. One closer handles coaching calls. Sabbo keeps agency calls.
- Cost: Commission-only, 10-15% of enrolled cash
- Expected output: 150+ coaching calls/month without Sabbo's time

**Trigger 4 — Hire Operator #1 (Agency)**
- Condition: 5+ agency clients
- Why: Delivery quality degrades above 5 clients for one operator. Hire at 5 to onboard them on clients 4-5, allow scale to 8-10.
- Cost: $5,000-$8,000/month (senior operator, not VA)
- Revenue unlocked: Capacity for 3-4 additional clients = +$54-72K MRR

**Trigger 5 — Hire Setter #2**
- Condition: Setter #1 is consistently booking 40-50 calls/month AND close rate is >35%
- Why: Doubling setter output should produce proportional call volume without quality degradation
- Cost: Same as Setter #1
- Expected output: 80-100 booked qualified calls/month combined

**Trigger 6 — Hire CSM (Client Success Manager)**
- Condition: 20+ active coaching students OR 5+ agency clients
- Why: Retention is now worth more than acquisition. CSM owns onboarding, accountability, renewals. Prevents churn before it happens.
- Cost: $3,000/month base + incentive structure (renewal bonuses, testimonial bonuses)
- Impact: Each prevented churn at $7K = $7K retained. At 5% churn rate on 50 students, CSM pays for itself preventing 2-3 churns/month.

---

### Full Team Hiring Sequence and P&L Impact

```
MONTH 1 (Revenue: $30-50K)
  Hire: Appointment Setter #1 ($3K/mo)
  Monthly burn: $3,000
  Revenue unlocked: Pipeline generation (calls from 5/mo → 40/mo)
  Net impact: +$20-40K within 60 days

MONTH 2 (Revenue: $50-80K)
  Hire: Video Editor ($2K/mo)
  Monthly burn: $5,000
  Revenue unlocked: Content frequency, compound audience growth
  Net impact: Content-attributable leads grow over 60-90 days

MONTH 3 (Revenue: $80-120K)
  Hire: Closer #1 (commission, ~$3-5K variable at 12% of coaching cash)
  Monthly burn: $8,000-$10,000
  Revenue unlocked: Coaching calls handled without Sabbo's time
  Net impact: Sabbo's time freed for agency growth and content

MONTH 4 (Revenue: $100-150K)
  Hire: Operator #1 for Agency delivery ($6K/mo)
  Monthly burn: $14,000-$16,000
  Revenue unlocked: Agency capacity 5 → 8-10 clients (+$54K MRR potential)
  Net impact: Agency revenue can scale without Sabbo as delivery bottleneck

MONTH 5 (Revenue: $130-170K)
  Hire: Setter #2 ($3K/mo + bonuses)
  Monthly burn: $17,000-$19,000
  Revenue unlocked: Call volume 60/mo → 100/mo (approaching 150-200 target)
  Net impact: Approaching Ben Bader's volume threshold

MONTH 6 (Revenue: $180-220K)
  Hire: CSM ($3K/mo + incentives)
  Monthly burn: $20,000-$22,000
  Revenue unlocked: Churn prevention + upsell identification
  Net impact: LTV per student goes from $7K → $10K+ (community recurring)

MONTH 6 P&L (Target State)
  Gross Revenue:            $218,000
  Team + Ops burn:          $30,000
  Ad spend:                 $15,000
  COGS (delivery):          $28,000
  ─────────────────────────────────
  Net Profit:               $145,000
  Net Margin:               66%
```

---

### The Virtuous Cycle vs. The Vicious Cycle [root: Hormozi]

**Virtuous (what Sabbo is building):**
```
Higher price → Higher margins → Better talent hired → Better service → Better results
     ↑                                                                        ↓
More referrals ← Better reputation ← More demand ← Higher social proof ←───┘
```

**Vicious (what to avoid at all costs):**
```
Lower price → Lower margins → Worse talent → Worse service → Worse results
     ↑                                                              ↓
Fewer referrals ← Worse reputation ← Less demand ← Bad reviews ←──┘
```

Every pricing decision, every hire, every client selection either feeds the virtuous cycle or the vicious one. This is why Hormozi says: "Some of you are so cheap that people don't believe you're good."

---

## 6.6 The Complete Revenue Waterfall: Daily Actions to Monthly Revenue

Every number in Sabbo's business is traceable back to a daily action. This is the full chain.

```
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
DAILY (Inputs — 1 human doing all of this = impossible at scale)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Sabbo:
    [ ] 1 piece of long-form content (YouTube/recording)
    [ ] 2-3 short clips repurposed and posted
    [ ] 1-2 agency outreach pitches (Loom + DM, quality over quantity)
    [ ] High-level strategy for 2-3 agency client touchpoints
    [ ] 1 agency discovery or strategy call

  Setter #1:
    [ ] 50 DMs to new followers
    [ ] 50 DMs to warm followers (old, not yet converted)
    [ ] 50 follow-ups from prior conversations
    [ ] 5-10 qualified calls booked

  Closer #1:
    [ ] 5-7 coaching sales calls
    [ ] 2-3 closes (35-40% close rate on 5-7 = 2 closed)
    [ ] $14,000 in coaching cash collected (2 × $7K)

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
WEEKLY (Outputs from daily inputs)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Content: 5-7 short-form, 1 long-form published
  Pipeline: 35-50 booked calls from setter outreach
  Content-driven bookings: 10-15 (organic, ads)
  Agency outreach: 5-10 quality Looms sent
  Total booked calls: 45-65/week

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
MONTHLY (Conversion math at Week 4)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Total booked calls:        180-260 (target: 200)
  Showed (70% show rate):    126-182 (target: 150)
  Coaching calls (80% split): 100-145 with closer
  Agency calls (20% split):   25-37 with Sabbo

  COACHING MATH
    Calls: 120 (midpoint)
    Close rate: 38%
    Closes: 46 deals
    Capacity cap: 10 students/month (quality control)
    Revenue: 10 × $7,000 = $70,000

  AGENCY MATH
    Calls: 30 (midpoint)
    Close rate: 33%
    Closes: ~10 (over full pipeline, not all same month)
    Adding 1-2 new clients/month to MRR
    New MRR added: $18,000-$36,000/month
    Existing MRR (6 clients × $18K): $108,000
    Agency total: $126,000-$144,000

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
MONTHLY REVENUE (Month 6 target state)
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Coaching new enrollments:    $70,000
  Coaching recurring:          $5,000
  Agency retainers:            $126,000
  Agency setup fees:           $12,000
  Revshare bonuses:            $5,000
  ──────────────────────────────────────
  TOTAL GROSS REVENUE:         $218,000

  Gross Margin (~80%):         $174,400
  Team + Ops ($30K):          -$30,000
  Ad Spend ($15K):            -$15,000
  ──────────────────────────────────────
  NET PROFIT:                  $129,400
  NET MARGIN:                  59%
```

## 6.7 Pricing Optimization Plays Applied to Sabbo's Offers

### Agency: Immediate Pricing Plays

**Play 1: 28-Day Billing Cycles (+8.3% revenue)**
- Change all new retainers from "monthly" to "every 28 days"
- On $18K average: $18K/month × 13 cycles/year = $234K vs. $216K/year
- Additional annual revenue per client: $18,000
- 7 clients: +$126,000/year from billing cycle change alone

**Play 2: Annual Price Increase Clause (+3-10%)**
- All contracts include: "Retainer increases 5% annually to reflect CPI + value delivered"
- Year 2 client at $18K becomes $18,900/month. No renegotiation needed.
- Year 2 across 7 clients: +$75,600/year

**Play 3: Processing Fee (+3-4%)**
- Add 3.99% processing fee OR offer ACH (no fee) as alternative
- Reduces involuntary churn from failed cards (1.2-1.7% of monthly charges)
- On $18K retainer: +$719/month/client. 7 clients: +$5,033/month

**Play 4: Ultra High Option (Anchoring)**
- Add a "Full Operator Embed" tier at $50K/month (2 dedicated operators, Sabbo strategic oversight)
- Makes $25K premium look modest
- Expected take rate: 1-2 clients (4% per Hormozi). Revenue impact: +$50-100K/month if 1 closes

---

### Coaching: Immediate Pricing Plays

**Play 1: Pay-in-Full Incentive**
- Offer: "Pay in full today at $7K, or 3 payments of $2,500" (total $7,500 on 3-pay)
- Pay-in-full saves student $500. Sabbo collects immediately.
- Hormozi benchmark: 35% take pay-in-full when framed as a discount
- Monthly impact: 3-4 of 10 students pay in full. Cash in hand today vs. $2,500 now.

**Play 2: Continued Access Continuity (+$297-497/month per graduated student)**
- After 90-day program, offer "Alumni Access" tier
- Includes: deal alerts, community, monthly group call, ongoing pipeline access
- At $397/month: 50 active alumni × $397 = $19,850/month pure recurring
- This is the "long tail" of Hormozi's Big Head, Long Tail model for education businesses

**Play 3: Annual Renewal Fee**
- If running a community or ongoing program: annual renewal at $997-$1,997 on top of monthly
- 10% of monthly recurring → annual premium adds 10% to annual recurring revenue

**Play 4: The Premium 1-on-1 Upsell (20% uptake)**
- 10 students/month → 2 upgrade to $15K premium
- When running: $30,000 additional revenue/month
- This is the "upsell" tier that Hormozi says each tier should be 5-10x the previous

---

## 6.8 The Ben Bader Volume Imperative: Summary

**The diagnosis from July 31:** Volume is the lever. The bottleneck is not sales skill, offer quality, or pricing. It is number of conversations reaching the booking stage.

**The math:**
```
Target: $200K/month
Required: 150-200 calls/month (Ben Bader threshold)
Current state (no team): ~10-20 calls/month
Gap: 130-180 additional calls needed

Source of those calls:
  Setter outreach:      100-120 calls/month
  Content-driven:       30-50 calls/month
  Paid ads:             20-30 calls/month
  TOTAL:                150-200 calls/month ✓

Required daily inputs to hit 200 calls/month:
  Setter DMs/day:       150 (50+50+50)
  Content pieces/week:  5-7 short-form, 1 long-form
  Ad spend/day:         $300-500

Required team to execute:
  Setter #1:            Month 1
  Video editor:         Month 2
  Closer #1:            Month 3
```

**The conclusion:** Every month without the setter is a month the waterfall doesn't flow. Every month without content is a month the ads have no organic data to amplify. The math is not about closing harder. It is about filling the top of the funnel with 6-8x more volume than Sabbo can produce alone, then letting a consistent close rate do the compounding.

At 200 calls/month, 35% close rate, $7K average — that is 70 deals/month available. Capacity constraints mean Sabbo takes 10-12 of the best. Everyone else goes on a waitlist. The waitlist raises prices. Higher prices raise margins. Higher margins fund better talent. Better talent delivers better results. Better results produce more case studies. More case studies fill the content pipeline. The loop closes.

**This is the money model.**

> **Primary Offer:** Amazon FBA Coaching ($3K–$10K programs) — PROOF OF CONCEPT IS HERE NOW
> **Secondary Offer:** Growth Agency ($5K–$25K/mo retainers) — defer as brand-builder, not primary push
> **Single Priority:** TRAFFIC. Volume is the lever. [root: Ben Bader brand audit, July 31]
> **Strategic Shift:** Amazon FBA coaching has the most active proof of concept. March is the month we scale what's already working — not what we want to work eventually.

---

## The Strategic Reframe

The original Part 7 treated the Growth Agency as the primary offer with Amazon coaching as secondary. That was wrong for March 2026.

Here is why the priority flips:

**Amazon FBA Coaching has proof of concept NOW.** Sabbo is actively sourcing, building the AI-powered sourcing pipeline (Keepa + Playwright + Claude), documenting real results, and coaching students through the process. That's content. That's proof. That's a sales conversation that's already had real wins behind it.

The Growth Agency is a real offer with real potential — but it requires a longer trust runway, higher-ticket positioning, and an audience that takes more time to build. It is not going away. But in March, trying to make it the lead puts more pressure on credibility infrastructure that isn't fully assembled yet.

**The correct move for March:** Pour all content fuel into Amazon FBA + AI + Coaching. Build that audience, prove that model at scale, and let agency content play a supporting role (2–3 pieces, not the primary weekly cadence).

> **Ben Bader's diagnosis still applies:** "The bottleneck is NOT sales. The bottleneck is TRAFFIC and VOLUME."
> The solution in March is max-volume content on the offer that converts fastest given current proof. That's Amazon coaching.

---

## The Proof-of-Concept Advantage

Amazon FBA coaching sits in a unique position entering March:

1. **Live system in production:** The sourcing pipeline (fast_grocery_scan.py, deal_scanner.py, seller_storefront_scan.py) is real, operational, and producing real deal data. You can show it live on camera.
2. **Keepa Pro tier active:** Real-time BSR data, product analysis, OA opportunities — all documentable on screen.
3. **AI integration is a differentiator:** "I use Claude to find 50 profitable products per week" is a hook that almost no Amazon coach in 2026 can match. That's the edge.
4. **Coaching students:** Even early-stage student results — first sourced product, first purchase, first $1K profit — are more compelling proof than theoretical agency frameworks.
5. **The market is red-hot:** Amazon FBA, OA sourcing, and AI automation content is performing at scale. The algorithm rewards specificity, and you have specific tools no competitor is showing on camera.

The agency will benefit when it has the same level of undocumented, live-system proof. It doesn't yet. March is not that month.

---

## March Targets (Recalibrated for Coaching Offer)

The math changes when the primary offer is $3K–$10K coaching rather than $5K–$25K/mo retainers. Volume needed per close is lower. Sales cycle is shorter. Lead magnet (7-Day Deal Alert Trial) self-qualifies people who actually want to source products.

| Metric | Target | Stretch |
|---|---|---|
| Content pieces published | 30+ | 40+ |
| New followers gained | 500+ | 1,000+ |
| DM conversations initiated | 1,500+ | 2,100+ |
| Leads captured (deal alert opt-ins + qualified DMs) | 150+ | 250+ |
| Sales calls booked | 25–35 | 50+ |
| Sales calls showed | 18–25 | 35+ |
| Coaching enrollments closed | 4–8 | 12+ |
| Revenue (March cash collected) | $15K–$40K | $60K+ |
| Ad spend | $1,500–$3,000 | $4,500 |
| Deal Alert Trial opt-ins | 100+ | 200+ |

**Revenue math at coaching pricing:**
- 4 enrollments × $5K avg = $20K
- 6 enrollments × $5K avg = $30K
- 8 enrollments × $7.5K avg = $60K
- 12 enrollments × $5K avg = $60K

The $15K floor is conservative. The stretch is real if content volume and setter system execute.

**March is Phase 1 → Phase 2 transition** [root: Ben Bader's 4-Phase Growth Roadmap]. The goal is not $200K/month this month. The goal is to build every input that makes $200K/month from coaching + agency (in that order) inevitable by Month 6.

## Week-by-Week Structure

---

### WEEK 1: March 1–7 — Foundation + Content Machine Launch

**Theme:** Build the infrastructure that all future volume runs on. Profile funnel leads with Amazon/AI identity. Lead magnet is the 7-Day Deal Alert Trial. Content machine launches with Amazon/AI as primary creative direction.

**The Priority Sequence for Week 1:**
1. Profile funnel (converts traffic into calls — leads with coaching identity, not agency)
2. Lead magnet (7-Day Deal Alert Trial is PRIMARY, audit is secondary)
3. Content machine (Amazon/AI hooks as primary weekly cadence)
4. Ad account setup (prepares paid amplification for Week 2)

---

#### Day 1 — Sunday, March 1: Profile Funnel Overhaul

**Morning (2 hrs): Instagram Profile Audit + Rewrite**

Implement Nik Setting's Profile Funnel SOP [root: Part 2.3]. The profile IS the funnel — it must function as a landing page, a VSL, a case study page, and a social proof wall simultaneously.

The bio must now lead with Amazon FBA + AI coaching identity. The audience Sabbo is trying to attract in March is: people who want to sell on Amazon, people who are curious about AI tools for e-commerce, and people who are already selling but stuck under $5K/month.

**Bio rewrite (use this exact structure):**

- **Line 1 (Headline):** "I teach people how to build profitable Amazon FBA businesses using AI | DM 'FBA' to start"
- **Line 2 (Credibility):** "Built an AI-powered sourcing pipeline that finds 50+ deals/week | Coaching students to $10K/month"
- **Line 3 (CTA):** "↓ Get 7 free deal alerts below"

*Note: "I teach people how to build profitable Amazon FBA businesses using AI" speaks directly to the Amazon ICP's desired outcome. Leading with "Growth Agency Owner" or "I install growth systems for 7-figure founders" targets the wrong avatar for March. The agency line belongs in the highlights, not the bio.*

**Profile picture:** Clean, high-quality headshot. Slight side angle. Same face that appears in all reels, stories, and ads — creates the "I know that person" familiarity effect [root: Nik Setting].

**Link in bio:** Single link only — not Linktree. Point to YouTube channel OR the 7-Day Deal Alert Trial opt-in page. The YouTube channel is the trust-builder. The trial opt-in is the lead gen vehicle. A/B test which generates more opt-ins by Week 2 and commit to the winner.

**Pinned Posts (3 slots — configure all three):**
- Slot 1 (Credibility): Best existing proof — a real sourcing result, a Keepa screenshot with 35%+ ROI, a student win, or your Amazon dashboard showing sales. This is the most visible proof element on the entire profile. It must show a real number.
- Slot 2 (Value): A framework reel — "The 5-step process I use to find profitable Amazon products every single week" — Miro board or talking-head walkthrough. This is the competence demonstration for the Amazon ICP.
- Slot 3 (Transformational): Personal origin story reel — "Why I built an AI-powered sourcing system instead of manually hunting for products." This is the emotional proof — differentiates from the manual-hustle Amazon coaches.

**Highlights structure (create all four today):**
- "START HERE" — 7-slide credibility sequence (who you are, who this is for — "if you want to sell on Amazon using AI tools," the problem you solve, your mechanism, student result 1, student result 2, CTA to 7-day deal trial)
- "RESULTS" — Screenshots of sourcing results, student wins, ROI screenshots, deal alerts delivered. Update monthly.
- "THE SYSTEM" — Your AI sourcing pipeline walkthrough (how Keepa + Claude + the scripts work together). This is the thing no other Amazon coach has.
- "AGENCY" — Minimal. 3-4 slides explaining the growth agency offer exists for founders, with a link. Not promoted actively in March — just present for anyone who finds it.

---

**Afternoon (2 hrs): Lead Magnet Setup — 7-Day Deal Alert Trial (PRIMARY)**

Primary lead magnet: **"The 7-Day Deal Alert Trial — Get 7 Real Profitable Amazon Products Delivered to Your Inbox"** [root: Part 3.1 — Type 2: Free Trial]

This is not a PDF. This is not a worksheet. This is a live delivery service. For 7 days, the lead receives one curated profitable Amazon sourcing opportunity per day — product name, ASIN, retail source, ROI %, FBA fees, and buy link. This is what the AI sourcing pipeline actually produces. Deliver the output directly.

**Why this is the primary lead magnet:**
- It self-qualifies immediately (broke people don't care about ROI percentages)
- It delivers real value that filters for buyers (the person who opens and clicks 7 days in a row is a serious seller or aspiring seller)
- It creates proof of system before they ever get on a call ("I've been receiving these deals — your pipeline is real")
- The capital question gates out non-buyers before they waste a call slot

**Lead magnet naming (Hormozi Formula 2):**
> "Get 7 Real Profitable Amazon Products Delivered to Your Inbox — Free. See Exactly What My AI Sourcing Pipeline Finds Before Your Competition Does."

**Setup today:**
1. Create opt-in page (Typeform, Carrd, or GoHighLevel) — fields: first name + email + "How much capital do you have available for inventory?" (filter: under $3K = still receive, but flag as lower priority for coaching call outreach)
2. Configure email sequence (7 emails, one per day, each containing one deal alert formatted as: Product Name | ASIN | Source Retailer | Buy Price | Amazon Sell Price | Estimated ROI | FBA Fees | Net Profit per unit | BUY LINK)
3. Post-opt-in page: 30-second selfie video from Sabbo — "Your first deal alert lands tomorrow morning. Here's what to do when you get it..."
4. Day 8 email (after the trial): "Your 7-day trial is over. Here's what to do if you want more." → CTA to book coaching call

**The pipeline for deal alerts:**
Use the existing execution/fast_grocery_scan.py output. Run it once per week. Select the top 7 deals by ROI%. Schedule delivery via email tool (ConvertKit, Mailchimp, or GoHighLevel). This costs zero additional time once configured.

**Secondary lead magnet (Agency, back-pocket only):**
> "Free 20-Minute Growth Audit" — keep this live but do not promote it in March content. Available in bio link or if an agency ICP DMs directly. Not featured in reels, not in bio, not in story sequences for March.

#### Day 2 — Monday, March 2: Content Calendar Planning + First Reel

**Morning (1 hr): Content Calendar — Full March Planning**

The content machine runs on a weekly cadence [root: Part 2.1, Content-to-Ads Pipeline]:
- 1 long-form YouTube video per week (20–45 min) — Amazon sourcing walkthroughs, Keepa tutorials, AI tool demos
- 3 Reels per week (60–90 sec each) — Amazon/AI/coaching as primary, occasional agency
- Daily Story sequences (5–8 slides, posted 11am–2pm)
- Optional: 2–3 carousel posts per week (Miro board breakdowns of sourcing systems)

**Content theme distribution for March:**
- Amazon FBA sourcing: 40% of content (walkthroughs, Keepa, product research, OA strategies)
- AI + Automation: 25% (how the pipeline works, tools used, what Claude does in the system)
- Coaching journey: 20% (student results, behind the scenes, coaching call moments with permission)
- Business/scaling mindset: 10% (universal entrepreneurship content — applies to both audiences)
- Agency content: 5% — maximum 2–3 pieces total for March

**Hook Bank — Amazon FBA + AI Primary (10+ hooks, these are the weekly workhorses):**

*Amazon FBA sourcing hooks (talking head or screen-record format — S/A tier):*
1. "I found a product with 35% ROI in 8 minutes using Keepa. Here's exactly how I did it — live."
2. "Most Amazon beginners make this mistake before they ever buy their first product. Here's what it costs them."
3. "I check these 5 things before I source ANY product. Miss one and you're losing money from day one."
4. "Live Keepa walkthrough: how to read a BSR chart and know if a product is actually worth sourcing."
5. "The difference between a $5 ROI product and a $50 ROI product is this one thing that most people miss."
6. "Why most OA beginners lose money on their first order — and the exact filter I use to prevent it."
7. "What a profitable Amazon FBA deal actually looks like from search to purchase order." (Undocumented format — document a real sourcing session)
8. "I asked Claude to help me find profitable Amazon products. Here's what happened." (AI hook — high virality potential)
9. "The sourcing mistake that costs Amazon sellers $500/month without them realizing it."
10. "Keepa just became the most important tool in my Amazon business. Here's why."

*AI + Automation hooks (screen-record or talking head):*
11. "How I use AI to find 50 profitable Amazon products per week without manual searching."
12. "The sourcing pipeline I built with Claude. It runs while I sleep."
13. "AI tools every Amazon FBA seller needs in 2026 — and the one that does the heavy lifting."
14. "I automated the most time-consuming part of Amazon sourcing. Here's what the output looks like."
15. "Why I stopped manually searching for Amazon deals and built this instead."

*Coaching journey hooks (talking head, documentary format):*
16. "What my students are doing differently in their first 30 days of FBA — vs. what I see most people doing."
17. "The 90-day path to $10K/month on Amazon. Here's the actual roadmap."
18. "A student just made their first profitable Amazon sale. Here's exactly what they did."
19. "The most common question I get from coaching students — and the answer most courses get wrong."
20. "What separates the Amazon sellers who hit $10K/month from the ones who quit at $500."

*Agency hooks (OCCASIONAL — 2-3 total for March, not weekly):*
21. "If you're a 7-figure founder burning ad spend without a system, here's the one thing that's actually broken." (Use once — Week 2 or 3)
22. "The difference between a marketing agency and a growth operator — and why it matters for your business." (Use once — Week 4)

**Content format priority for March (based on conversion tier):**
- S-Tier: Screen-recorded sourcing walkthroughs — LIVE Keepa analysis, live deal finding, live pipeline output. This is undocumented content [root: Nik Setting] applied to Amazon. No one else is showing their actual sourcing sessions on camera.
- S-Tier: Scripted talking head (cheapest to produce, highest authority transfer) — use for coaching journey hooks, AI hooks
- A-Tier: Miro board/system breakdowns — use for pipeline explanation content
- A-Tier: Student result reveals — screenshot + quick story format

**Avoid for March (D-tier):** Trending audio + text caption, generic "entrepreneur motivation" content, green screen overlays, anything that doesn't connect directly to Amazon FBA, AI tools, or coaching outcomes.

#### Day 6 — Friday, March 6: Film YouTube Video + Ad Account Setup

**Afternoon (2 hrs): Meta Ad Account Setup**

Steps (do not skip any):
1. Create Meta Business Manager account if not already set up
2. Create an Ad Account under Business Manager
3. Install Meta Pixel on the 7-Day Deal Alert Trial opt-in page (this is the primary pixeled conversion event for March)
4. Configure Pixel events: ViewContent (landing page visit), Lead (deal alert opt-in completed), Purchase (coaching enrollment)
5. Connect Instagram account to Business Manager
6. Verify domain
7. Set up custom audiences:
   - Instagram profile visitors (last 30 days)
   - Instagram video viewers (last 30 days, 50%+ watch time)
   - Deal Alert opt-in completions (from Pixel Lead events)
   - Lookalike audiences (will activate in Week 2 once pixel has 100+ events)

**Jeremy Haynes Pixel Conditioning rules [root: Part 3.2]:**
- The pixel confirmation page (deal alert opt-in confirmed) is accessible to anyone who completes the form — no blocking needed at this stage (it's a free trial, wide-top funnel)
- The coaching call booking confirmation page IS gated by the capital qualifier question — only leads who answer "$5K+" on capital get that pixel fired
- State price range in any future VSL within first 60 seconds: "The coaching program is a $3K–$10K investment depending on the tier"
- Never pixel the "not a fit" page

### WEEK 2: March 8–14 — Paid Ads Launch + Setter Hire

**Theme:** Turn on paid amplification of organic content — targeting Amazon/FBA/e-commerce audience. Hire the first setter trained on Amazon coaching qualification. Build the DM qualification playbook with coaching as the primary path.

**The core insight for Week 2:** A setter sending 150 DMs/day to people who followed after watching Amazon content is the single most leveraged hire Sabbo can make right now. The deal alert opt-in creates a warm lead pool the setter can work. Without it, Sabbo cannot hit the 50/50/50 KPI framework [root: Nik Setting] while simultaneously producing content and closing deals.

#### Day 8 — Sunday, March 8: Launch First Paid Ads

**Budget for Week 2:** $50/day ($350 total for the week)

**Campaign 1 — Profile Visit Traffic Campaign (Primary)**
Following Nik Setting's Profile Funnel architecture [root: Part 2.3]:
- Campaign type: Traffic campaign optimized for Instagram profile visits (NOT engagement, NOT leads)
- Ad set 1 (ABO — Ad Budget Optimization):
  - Targeting: Interest stack — "Amazon FBA," "Amazon seller," "online arbitrage," "e-commerce," "passive income," "side hustle" — people who are actively curious about Amazon
  - Budget: $25/day
  - Creative: Best-performing organic reel from Week 1 (use Post ID to carry over existing engagement — increases CTR 2–3x vs. fresh ad). The Keepa walkthrough reel or the "5 things I check" reel will perform best here.
- Ad set 2 (ABO):
  - Targeting: Interest stack — "artificial intelligence," "ChatGPT," "automation," "passive income," "entrepreneurship" — the AI-curious entrepreneurship audience who overlaps with Amazon interest
  - Budget: $25/day
  - Creative: The "How I use AI to find 50 profitable products per week" reel (hook appeals directly to this audience)

**Rule:** Let ads run for 72 hours minimum before judging performance. Do not touch them in the first 72 hours.

**Scaling trigger (Nik Setting's ABO → CBO method):**
- After 72 hours: if CPL (cost per profile visit) is under $1.50, increase budget 20%
- After 7 days: if any ad set is generating deal alert opt-ins at under $20/opt-in, move to CBO (Campaign Budget Optimization)

#### Day 9 — Monday, March 9: Setter Job Post + Screening

**Post setter job description on:**
- Twitter/X (post publicly: "Hiring a DM setter. Remote. Paid + commission. DM me.")
- Instagram story (show your audience you're growing — this also generates credibility content)
- Upwork (post for "DM Setter" or "Social Media Appointment Setter")
- Private network referrals

**Setter Job Description (use this):**

> I'm hiring 1–2 DM setters for my Amazon FBA coaching business.
>
> Your job: send 150 DMs/day (50 to new followers, 50 to warm followers, 50 follow-ups). Qualify leads using a script I provide. Book sales calls with people who want to learn Amazon FBA.
>
> Requirements:
> - Good English, professional tone
> - Available 4–6 hours/day, flexible schedule
> - Experience with Instagram DM outreach preferred (not required)
> - Genuine interest in learning — the more you understand Amazon FBA, the better you'll qualify leads
>
> Pay: $10–$15/hour base + $75–$150 commission per booked call that shows
>
> Apply: DM me "SETTER" with one paragraph on why you'd be great at this.

**Note: The commission is slightly higher here than the original agency version because coaching closes faster and at lower ticket — the setter will book more calls and earn commissions more frequently. This makes it a better hire for someone commission-hungry.**

**Screening criteria:** Response speed (did they follow instructions?), tone (professional but not robotic), comprehension (did they read and understand the role?), coachability.

**Target: 5–10 applicants by end of week. Interview top 2–3 by Friday March 13.**

---

#### Day 10 — Tuesday, March 10: DM Playbook Creation

Write the full DM Qualification Playbook for the setter (this is what they train on before they touch your inbox).

**The playbook must cover:**

**Section 1: The Opener Philosophy [root: Nik Setting]**
The opener's only job is to get a response. Not to explain the offer. Not to build trust. Just: first reply.

Use binary questions. Never open-ended questions.

- Amazon coaching audience opener (primary): "Quick question — are you currently selling on Amazon, or are you looking to start your first FBA business?"
- AI/automation audience opener: "Curious — have you looked into using AI tools for Amazon sourcing, or are you still in research mode on how FBA works?"
- General entrepreneur audience opener (for people who followed from non-Amazon content): "Hey — quick question, are you more focused on building income online right now, or are you working on scaling something you already have going?"

**Section 2: The Full Qualification Script (Amazon FBA Coaching — PRIMARY)**

Step 1 — Opener → get first response (use Amazon opener above)
Step 2 — "Got it. What's the main goal — income replacement, a side business alongside your job, or building it into a real asset you could sell someday?"
Step 3 — "Makes sense. And right now, do you have capital set aside that you could put into inventory? Even a rough number helps — I want to make sure the timing makes sense."
Step 4 — "Honest question — if you had a system that consistently found profitable products and a coach walking you through each step, is that something you'd want to move on in the next 30 days, or is the timing off right now?"
Step 5 — [If timing is right + capital is $5K+]: "Perfect. The next step is a quick call with Sabbo — he shows you exactly what the system does and how the coaching works. It's 30 minutes and completely no pressure. Here's the link: [coaching call booking link]. Grab a time that works and let me know when you've booked."
Step 5b — [If capital is $3K–$5K]: "Got it. There are options for people starting at that range — let me grab Sabbo to look at your specific situation. Here's the booking link."
Step 5c — [If capital under $3K]: "Appreciate the honesty. The coaching requires a capital floor to make sense — at under $3K you can't build the inventory needed to see real results. Let me send you the free deal alert trial for now — it'll show you exactly what the system finds, and you can come back when the timing's right." → Send free trial opt-in link.

**Section 3: The Full Qualification Script (Agency — BACK-POCKET ONLY)**
Use sparingly. Only if someone is clearly a business owner/founder asking about marketing/growth systems — not the primary audience for March. If they come up: "Quick question — are you currently running paid ads to grow your business, or are you relying more on referrals and organic right now?" → If they are a 7-figure founder with acquisition problems, escalate to Sabbo directly with "this one might be an agency lead."

**Section 4: Red flags (conversations to exit gracefully)**
- Under $3K available capital for Amazon with no near-term plan to change that (send them the free trial, exit the active qualification)
- "I just want passive income" with no mention of doing any work (not the coaching avatar — they want a course, not a coach)
- Pure information-seekers (asks 10 questions, never answers yours — extract what value you can and move on)
- Someone who is clearly already an advanced seller ($100K+/month) — different conversation, flag to Sabbo
- Anyone hostile, rude, or trying to sell Sabbo something

**Section 5: Bookings protocol**
- Never send the booking link before completing qualification (wastes call slots on unqualified leads)
- After qualification, always end with: "Here's the link. All I ask is that you choose a time you'll be 100% available for and distraction-free. Drop me a confirmation when you book."
- Follow up 24 hours later if no booking: "Hey, just checking — did you get a chance to grab a spot on the calendar?"
- Follow up 48 hours after that if still nothing: "No worries if the timing's off. I'll send you the 7-day deal alert trial in the meantime so you can see what the system actually finds." → Send opt-in. This converts the cold lead into a warm email subscriber.

---

#### Day 11 — Wednesday, March 11: Email Sequence Launch

**Welcome + Nurture Sequence (for 7-Day Deal Alert Trial leads — Amazon coaching):**

Email 1 (immediately after opt-in):
- Subject: "Your first deal alert lands tomorrow — here's what to do with it"
- Body: 3 sentences explaining the format (what they'll receive each day) + one result preview ("Yesterday the pipeline found a product with 42% ROI at Target — you'll see something like this tomorrow") + link to YouTube Video 1 as a preview of the full system
- P.S.: "If you're already sure you want to go deeper — here's how to book a 30-min call with me directly: [coaching call link]"

Email 2 (Day 2 — deal alert delivery):
- Subject: "Deal Alert #2: [Product Name] — [X]% ROI at [Retailer]"
- Body: Full deal format (product, ASIN, source, prices, ROI, net profit, direct buy link) + 2 sentences of context ("Here's why this made the cut: BSR has been consistent for 90 days and there are 3 active FBA sellers — that tells me the demand is real and the competition isn't about to crater the price")

Emails 3–7: Same format as Email 2 — one deal per day, with a brief contextual note on why it passed the filter.

Email 8 (Day after trial ends):
- Subject: "Your 7-day trial is over — here's what most people do next"
- Body: "You've seen 7 real deals. Now you know the system is real. The question is whether you want access to this every week — and whether you want a coach walking you through how to act on what you're seeing."
- CTA: "If you're ready to actually start — here's the link to book a call. No sales pressure. If it's a fit, we'll figure out a plan. If not, I'll tell you honestly." → booking link

Email 9 (3 days after trial ends — if no booking):
- Subject: "The one thing that separates Amazon sellers who win from the ones who give up"
- Body: mini coaching essay — the story of a student who almost didn't start, what changed for them, the outcome. CTA to booking.

Email 10 (7 days after trial ends — if still no booking):
- Subject: "Last one — I won't keep nudging"
- Body: Hormozi Fast Cash style. Short. Direct. No new information. "If you want to talk, the link is here. If not, I'll leave you alone — but I'll keep sending free deal alerts when I run a new trial series." → CTA to booking, or "reply 'ALERTS' if you want to stay on the list for the next free trial."

**Nurture sequence (for booked coaching leads — pre-call warming):**
Using Jeremy Haynes' Hammer Them framework [root: Part 3.2]:
- Retargeting audience in Meta: anyone who completed the coaching call booking form (pixel fires on booking confirmation page)
- Ad content: 3–5 of your best Amazon/AI reels running as traffic/engagement ads at $20/day to this small audience
- Goal: booked prospects see your content 3–5 times per day between booking and the call
- This compresses 5 months of organic content consumption into 2–3 days [root: Jeremy Haynes, Concentrated Messaging]

#### Day 15 — Sunday, March 15: Setter Onboarding Day 1

**Onboarding protocol (SooWei Goh — 48-hour training + quiz gate [root: Part 3.3]):**

Hour 1: Read the DM Playbook (Section 1–5 created in Week 2) — focus on the Amazon coaching qualification script
Hour 2: Watch Sabbo's Amazon content (the two YouTube videos, 3–5 reels) — understand the product viscerally before representing it
Hour 3: Role-play 10 conversations with Sabbo playing the prospect:
- Play: the complete beginner ("I've never sold anything online"), the skeptic ("doesn't Amazon OA not work anymore?"), the ghost, the "how much does it cost" jumper, the already-seller who's plateaued, the person with $5K ready to go, the person with $2K who wants to start
Hour 4: Setter writes their own opener variations for each scenario
Hour 5: Sabbo reviews and approves opener variations. Reject anything that sounds robotic or goes straight to pitch.
Quiz gate: Setter must pass a written quiz on: (1) Amazon coaching ICP definition, (2) capital qualifier thresholds, (3) what the 7-day deal alert trial is and when to send it, (4) how to respond to "is this legit?" and "is this a pyramid scheme?" (real objections Amazon coaching setters face)

**Training content to send setter:**
- The DM Playbook (written in Day 10)
- Amazon FBA coaching ICP: $5K–$20K capital, wants income replacement or side income, motivated, coachable
- Red flags list (under $3K capital, passive income seekers who don't want to do the work, people trying to sell Sabbo something)
- Links to both YouTube videos (setter should be fluent in what the system does before representing it)
- The 7-Day Deal Alert Trial opt-in link (this is the "soft landing" for not-quite-ready leads — setter should offer this proactively)

**Content — repurposing system (this week's focus):**

The repurposing waterfall (Nik Setting's undocumented content principle [root: Part 2.1.2]):
- YouTube Video 1 (Keepa walkthrough) → clip 3 best moments → 3 reels (the moment you find a deal, the FBA calculator reveal, the "this is why that product failed" moment)
- YouTube Video 2 (AI pipeline) → clip 3 best moments → 3 reels (the pipeline architecture diagram, the "I asked Claude to do this" moment, the final deal output)
- Story sequence #1's best slide → carousel post (turn the 6-slide educational sequence into a Canva carousel — "The System Behind My Amazon Sourcing Pipeline")

This week, produce 6+ reels using only content already filmed. Zero new filming required for reels. All filming energy goes to YouTube Video 3.

#### Day 17 — Tuesday, March 17: Setter Day 2 + Ad Optimization Pass 1

**Ad optimization:**

After 7 days of data:
- Check: Which ad set has the lower CPM and higher profile visit rate? (Amazon interest targeting vs. AI/entrepreneurship targeting)
- Action: Pause the worse-performing ad set. Duplicate the winning ad set with a new creative (try the AI sourcing hook reel vs. the Keepa walkthrough reel — the hook matters more than almost anything else in ad creative)
- Scaling threshold check [root: Nik Setting's ABO → CBO method]:
  - If any ad set is generating deal alert opt-ins at under $20/opt-in: increase budget 50%
  - If under $10/opt-in: move to CBO immediately, 3x budget

**New retargeting campaign (activate if pixel has 200+ events):**

Hammer Them campaign [root: Jeremy Haynes, Part 3.2]:
- Audience: Instagram profile visitors last 14 days (exclude existing followers)
- Budget: $20/day
- Creative rotation: 5 different reels — mix of Keepa walkthrough, AI pipeline, student result content, coaching overview, personal story

**Challenge event planning (afternoon):**

For Week 4, the March 22–31 window. The event: **3-Day Free Live Challenge** [root: Ben Bader's Challenge Funnel model].

Challenge design decisions:
- **Name:** "The Amazon FBA Fast Start Challenge: Find Your First Profitable Product in 3 Days Using AI"
- **Format:** 3 consecutive days, 60–90 min live each day (via Zoom + streamed to Instagram Live)
- **Cost:** Free (maximize registrations — this is a wide-top funnel event)
- **Pitch mechanism:** Day 2 soft pitch, Day 3 hard pitch with coaching enrollment link
- **Goal:** 50–100 registrations → 25–50 attendees per day → 10–20 coaching call bookings from the event

**Day structure (Ben Bader's Three Sales framework [root: Ben Bader brain]):**
- Day 1: Break beliefs about the vehicle — "Why 99% of Amazon FBA Advice Is Wrong (And What Actually Works)"
  - Sell: The Vehicle (why AI-powered OA sourcing is the right model — vs. private label, dropshipping, manual OA)
  - Core content: The 3 myths that kill beginner Amazon sellers before they start (myth: you need a unique product, myth: OA is dead, myth: you need $50K to start)
- Day 2: Deep value training + soft pitch — "The 5-Step System I Use to Find Profitable Amazon Products Every Week"
  - Sell: The Authority (why Sabbo specifically — built the pipeline, runs it live, coaches students through it, shows real results)
  - Core content: Walk through the actual system (Keepa → retail price check → FBA calculator → profit threshold → buy or skip). This is the best free content Sabbo has ever delivered.
  - Soft pitch: "Tomorrow I'm going to show you how to get access to this system and a coach who walks you through every step. If you already know you want that, here's how to book a call before then."
- Day 3: Live sourcing demo + hard pitch + enrollment push
  - Sell: The Belief System (people just like them winning — bring on a student result, or demonstrate a live sourcing session that ends with a real profitable find)
  - Live sourcing: "Watch me find a profitable product right now — live — using Keepa and the AI pipeline."
  - Pitch: "Here's what it looks like to work with me — [coaching tiers, pricing range, what's included, the 90-day promise]"
  - CTA: "If you're a motivated person with $5K+ to invest in inventory and you're ready to build a real Amazon business — DM me 'FBA' right now or click the link in the chat."
  - Close with urgency: "I take on a limited number of coaching students per cohort. If you want in on the March cohort — tonight is the decision point."

**Registration setup:**
- Typeform or GoHighLevel registration page (first name, email, one qualifying question: "What's your #1 goal with Amazon FBA — income replacement, side income, or building an asset?")
- ManyChat: comment "CHALLENGE" on the announcement post → automated registration link
- Create registration confirmation email sequence (Hammer Them pre-event: send 3 pieces of your best Amazon content to registrants in the 5 days before the challenge — YouTube Video 1, YouTube Video 2, and a deal alert preview)

#### Day 22 — Sunday, March 22: Challenge Prep + Registration Push

**Registration push (48 hours before launch):**
- Post daily story sequences for 2 days straight: registration reminder, challenge preview ("here's what Day 1 covers"), social proof ("people are already registered from 12 countries"), countdown timer
- DM every warm lead in the setter's conversation list: "Hey, I'm running a free 3-day Amazon challenge starting Tuesday. You mentioned wanting to get started with FBA — this is the exact right thing to join. Here's the link: [link]."

- Hammer Them campaign for registrants: $20/day retargeting showing Amazon/AI content to everyone who registered (Jeremy Haynes pre-event warm-up — make them feel like Sabbo is everywhere before the event starts)

**Challenge content prep (build all three day scripts today):**

**Day 1 Script — "Why 99% of Amazon FBA Advice Is Wrong":**
- Hook: "I've spoken to hundreds of people who tried Amazon FBA and failed. They all had something in common — and it wasn't picking bad products."
- Core teaching: The 3 myths that kill Amazon sellers before they start:
  - Myth 1: "You need a unique product or private label" → OA proof that branded retail arbitrage works
  - Myth 2: "OA is dead / too competitive" → Keepa data showing consistent BSR on OA products, market size reality check
  - Myth 3: "You need $50,000 to start" → Real math on starting with $5K–$10K capital
- Audience participation: "If you've avoided Amazon FBA because of one of these beliefs, type the myth number in the chat."
- Social proof: One result showing someone who overcame one of these myths (student result, or Sabbo's own early result)
- Soft CTA: "Tomorrow I'm going to walk you through the actual system live. If you want to get a head start, DM me 'FBA' and I'll send you a deal alert today."

**Day 2 Script — "The 5-Step System: Live Walkthrough":**
- Hook: "Everything I'm about to show you is the exact system I use every week. No theory — I'm going to walk you through a real product analysis."
- Core teaching: The 5 steps (open Keepa → read BSR trend → check retail price → run FBA calculator → pass/fail decision) — walk through a REAL product live on screen
- Run at least 3 products: one that fails (show why), one that marginally passes, one that clearly passes
- Micro-commitments throughout: "Comment 'FOUND ONE' when you find a product that passes all 5 steps during the walkthrough."
- Show the AI layer: "Now watch what happens when I feed this into the pipeline..." — brief Claude demo
- Pitch (soft): "Tomorrow I'm showing you the live sourcing session. And at the end, I'm opening up spots in my coaching program for people who want me walking them through this in their business. If you know you want that — the link is in the chat. You can book a call before we even get to Day 3."

**Day 3 Script — Live Sourcing Demo + Pitch:**
- Open with: Results wall — pull up 2–3 student wins or your own sourcing wins. Real numbers on screen.
- Live sourcing: "I have Keepa open right now. I'm going to find a profitable product in real time — starting from scratch, with you watching." Run a real session. Find a real deal. Show the final numbers.
- Pitch: "Here's what it looks like to work with me in the coaching program."
  - Tier A (beginner, first FBA business): $3K–$5K — 90-day program, weekly calls, deal alerts included, sourcing system access
  - Tier B (existing seller, plateaued): $5K–$10K — focused on scaling, ads, inventory management, advanced sourcing
  - The promise: Profitable, running Amazon FBA business in 90 days — or keep working until you do
- CTA: "If you're a motivated person with $5K+ available for inventory and you're ready to actually build this — DM me 'FBA' right now or click the enrollment link in the chat."
- Urgency: "I take on a limited cohort each month. March slots are the current cohort. If you're in — decide today. April cohort opens in 30 days."

#### Day 25 — Wednesday, March 25: CHALLENGE DAY 2 + Sales Calls

**Morning:** Coaching sales calls (any calls booked from Week 3 outreach or from Deal Alert Trial email follow-up)
**Afternoon:** Challenge Day 2 live session — the 5-step sourcing system walkthrough
**Evening:** Post-event follow-up (clip + email to non-shows: "Day 2 was the system walkthrough — here's the replay. Day 3 is the live sourcing session.")

**Sales call framework (for coaching enrollment calls):**
Following Hormozi's closing framework [root: Part 4]:
- Do not pitch in the first 10 minutes. Diagnose first.
- "Walk me through what's going on with Amazon right now — are you pre-launch, or have you tried before?"
- "What would it actually mean for you if this was generating $5K–$10K per month? What does that change?"
- Let them tell you the story. Reflect it back: "So what I'm hearing is you're at [current state], and the gap is [X — sourcing knowledge, product selection, capital deployment, or all three]."
- Present the coaching tier as the solution to the specific gap they named:
  - "Based on what you've told me, you're a Tier A candidate. Here's what that program looks like..."
  - "You're already selling — you're a Tier B. Here's where we focus..."
- Price anchor: "The program is $[X] — most people make that back on their first sourcing run once the system is set up. The question isn't the price, it's whether you trust the process. Let me show you why the process works."
- Trial close: "If the numbers make sense and this feels right, is there any reason today wouldn't be the day to move forward?"

**Post-challenge push (same evening):**

Email sequence to all registrants (send over 3 days — March 26, 27, 28):

Email 1 (Thursday evening): "The replay + next steps"
- Replay link for all 3 days
- "If you watched all 3 days and you're ready to stop thinking about Amazon and actually start — here's how to enroll: [enrollment link or coaching call link]"
- "If you're not sure yet, that's okay. Here's the one question that usually clarifies it: 'Do I have $5K+ I could put into inventory right now, and am I willing to learn the system?' If yes to both — that's your answer."

Email 2 (Friday): "I received [X] applications. Here's who I'm moving forward with."
- Create urgency around limited cohort spots
- Restate the transformation: "The person who came to Day 3 and watched the live sourcing session knows what's possible. The only variable now is whether you're willing to do the work."
- Testimonial or result: if a student has a win this week, use it here. "One of my students sourced her first profitable product yesterday — $[X] net profit, $[Y] ROI. She started the coaching program 6 weeks ago."
- CTA: "If you're on the fence, I'm doing one more open coaching call this week. Here's the link."

Email 3 (Saturday): Hormozi Fast Cash close — "Last call"
- Short. Direct. No new information.
- "March cohort enrollment closes at midnight Sunday. If you want in — here's the link. If not, April cohort opens in 30 days and you can join the waitlist."
- One line: "The deal alerts are real. The system is real. The only question is whether you're ready."

---

#### Day 27 — Friday, March 27: Setter Week 3 Review + Reel Sprint

**Setter metrics review:**
- Week 3 KPIs: Has setter hit 50/50/50 daily DMs yet?
- Booking rate: Coaching call bookings / total qualified conversations
- Deal alert opt-in rate: Leads who weren't ready for a call but accepted the trial
- If under 10% booking rate from qualified conversations: identify at which step leads are dropping. Usually the capital question — if leads are ghosting there, the opener is attracting the wrong audience (people without capital following Amazon content). Adjust ad targeting.
- If over 20% booking rate: increase conversation volume immediately. Ramp setter to 75/75/75.

**Content sprint (repurpose challenge content):**
- Post Reel 12: Best clip from Challenge Day 1 (the myth-busting moment — "If you missed Day 1 of the Amazon challenge, here's the moment that got the most reactions.")
- Post Reel 13: Best clip from Challenge Day 2 (the live Keepa analysis finding a real deal — the tension of watching live sourcing in real time is high-engagement content)
- Post Reel 14: Best clip from Challenge Day 3 (the live product find or the pitch moment — "Watch me find a profitable product in 7 minutes, live, with 50 people watching.")

---

#### Day 28 — Saturday, March 28: Sales Call Sprint

**Block this entire day for coaching enrollment calls.** This is close week.

Target: 5–8 coaching calls today (from challenge attendees, from setter bookings, from deal alert trial post-email outreach).

Call structure:
- Diagnose (10 min)
- Present coaching tier (10 min)
- Handle objections (10 min)
- Trial close → BAMFAM (Book A Meeting From A Meeting) if not closing today [root: Part 3.2, Hormozi BAMFAM]

**Common objections + responses (coaching-specific):**

*"I need to think about it."*
Response: "Totally. What specifically do you need to think through? I want to make sure I've answered the right questions before you make a decision. Is it the money, the timing, or whether this actually works?"

*"Is this like a course? I've bought courses before."*
Response: "No — and this is important. A course gives you information. I give you results. I'm on a call with you every week. You can ask me about your specific product. I look at your actual Keepa charts. And I don't stop until you have a profitable business running — that's the commitment on my end."

*"I don't have the capital right now."*
Response: "What's the timeline? Because if it's 30–60 days, we can plan around that. The program starts when you're ready to source. What I don't want is for you to get the capital and then not have the system to deploy it correctly — that's when people lose money."

*"I've tried Amazon before and it didn't work."*
Response: "What happened specifically?" → Listen fully. → "That's exactly what the system is designed to prevent. [Address the specific thing that went wrong.] Here's how the process would have looked different..."

*"It's more than I expected to spend."*
Response: "I understand. Here's the way I think about it — if the coaching gets you to one profitable sourcing run at 30% ROI on $5K inventory, that's $1,500 profit on your first order. Most students are cash-flow positive on coaching within 60–90 days. The program isn't a cost — it's an investment with a measurable return."

---

#### Days 29–31 — March 29–31: Month Close + Review

**Sunday March 29:**
- Final push email to all challenge leads who didn't enroll (Hormozi fast-close style — one line, one CTA, no new pitch)
- Setter: sweep all conversation threads that stalled in March — re-engage with: "Hey — just wanted to check in. The Amazon challenge wrapped up. Did you catch any of it? Here's the replay if not: [link]"
- Post Reel 15: **"What my students are doing differently in their first 30 days — vs. what I see most people doing."** (Coaching hook #16) — talking head, 60 sec. The content machine never stops during close week.
- Story sequence: "March cohort is closing. Here's what the last 30 days actually looked like — building the pipeline, running the challenge, coaching students through their first sourcing runs." Behind-the-scenes authenticity content.

**Monday March 30:**
- Sales calls (any remaining close opportunities from March)
- Begin month review data collection — pull setter KPIs, ad spend, opt-ins, calls booked, calls showed, closes, revenue
- Post one agency content piece (the ONLY agency content of the month — use it now as a breadcrumb for any agency ICP who found Sabbo through Amazon content): **"If you're a 7-figure founder burning ad spend without a growth system — this is what's actually broken."** (Agency hook #21) — brief, 60 sec talking head. Not prominently featured. Just exists.

**Tuesday March 31 — Month-End Review:**

Pull all March KPIs and compare against targets:

|---|---|---|---|
| Content pieces posted | 30+ | — | — |
| New followers | 500+ | — | — |

| Deal Alert Trial opt-ins | 100+ | — | — |

| Coaching calls booked | 25–35 | — | — |
| Coaching calls showed | 18–25 | — | — |

**March → April carry-forward decisions:**
- Which 3 pieces of content drove the most profile visits, deal alert opt-ins, or coaching call bookings? Double down in April — more of those topics, more of that format.
- Which reel performed best organically? Run it as a paid ad in April with the Post ID.
- Which opener generated the highest reply rate for the setter? Lock it in as the default. Remove underperformers from the playbook.
- Which ad creative had the lowest cost-per-opt-in? Expand budget on that creative in April.
- What was the most common reason coaching calls didn't close? That's the April sales training focus — script update, objection handling, or ICP qualification tightening.
- How many agency leads came in organically from Amazon content? If more than 5 — there's a crossover audience. April can add one agency content piece per week without compromising primary focus.

## Daily Operating Rhythm

This is the non-negotiable daily structure. Every day in March follows this rhythm. Deviation destroys compounding.

### Weekday (Monday–Friday)

| Time | Block | Activity |
|---|---|---|
| 7:00–8:00 AM | Morning brain | Review yesterday's metrics. Check setter's DM conversations for 10 min — flag escalations. Check ad performance (CPM, opt-ins, profile visit cost — 5 min). Set one priority for the day. |
| 8:00–10:00 AM | Content creation | Film reel(s), write story sequence, plan or script YouTube video. This block is sacred — no calls, no DMs, no email. Especially no social scrolling. Create, don't consume. |
| 10:00 AM–12:00 PM | Setter management + DM review | Review setter's conversations. Handle escalations. Approve or coach any off-script responses. Look specifically for: conversations that stalled right at the capital question, conversations where the prospect went cold mid-script, any leads the setter flagged as potential agency ICPs. |
| 12:00–2:00 PM | Sales calls | All coaching calls scheduled in this block. 30-minute intro calls for new leads. 60-minute close calls for warm leads who attended the challenge or have been in the email sequence. |
| 2:00–3:00 PM | Lunch + reset | Genuine break. No phone. Context switch is necessary for afternoon performance. |
| 3:00–5:00 PM | Content repurposing + ad review | Edit yesterday's footage. Export best moments for reels. Check whether any organic post is performing above baseline (threshold: 100+ saves OR 50+ DMs OR profile-visit spike 2x average). If yes: run it as a paid ad using Post ID. |
| 5:00–6:00 PM | Admin + email | Respond to email. Review day's setter KPIs. Update coaching call tracker (who showed, who didn't, outcome, follow-up needed). Handle any deal alert trial delivery issues. |
| Evening (flexible) | Story sequence post | Post daily story sequence if not posted in the morning. Consistency matters more than optimal timing. |

### Weekend (Saturday–Sunday)

| Time | Block | Activity |
|---|---|---|
| Morning (2–3 hrs) | Content sprint | Film the week's YouTube video or batch-film 3–5 reels in one session. This is the content inventory the week runs on. |
| Afternoon (1–2 hrs) | Week review + week planning | Pull KPIs (setter report, ad dashboard, opt-in count, calls booked, revenue). Identify the week's best content. Update content calendar for next week. Update setter playbook with any learnings. Run fast_grocery_scan.py to generate next week's deal alerts. |
| Evening | Rest | Non-negotiable. Compounding requires recovery. |

## Ad Campaign Architecture (Full Month)

### Week 1–2: ABO Testing Phase

**Campaign 1 — Profile Visit Traffic (Amazon/AI Audience)**
- Objective: Instagram profile visits
- Budget: $50/day ($25 per ad set)
- Ad sets: 2
  - Ad Set 1: Amazon FBA interests (Amazon seller, FBA, online arbitrage, e-commerce, passive income)
  - Ad Set 2: AI/automation interests (ChatGPT, artificial intelligence, automation, side hustle, entrepreneurship)
- Creatives: Top 2 organic reels from Week 1 (use Post IDs) — Keepa walkthrough reel + AI sourcing hook reel

**Campaign 2 — Hammer Them: Booked-Call Audience (Activate Week 2)**
- Objective: Engagement / reach
- Audience: Anyone who completed the coaching call booking form (Pixel Lead event on booking confirmation page — capital qualified leads only)
- Budget: $20/day
- Creatives: 5 reels rotated — best Amazon/AI content + student result content
- Purpose: Improve show rate by saturating booked leads with proof before the call

### Week 3: ABO → CBO Transition

**If winner identified in Week 2 (lower CPM + more opt-ins):**
- Create new CBO campaign
- Duplicate the winning ad set 3–4 times with slight audience variations
- Starting CBO budget: $75/day
- Let Meta allocate across ad sets

**Campaign 3 — Challenge Registrations (activate March 21)**
- Objective: Lead (registration form completions for Amazon FBA Fast Start Challenge)
- Audience: Lookalike of deal alert opt-in completions (if pixel has 100+ Lead events) + Amazon/FBA interest stack
- Budget: $50/day for 7 days (March 21–28)
- Creative: Challenge announcement reel ("Free 3-day Amazon FBA challenge — I'll find a profitable product live on Day 3")

### Week 4: Full Campaign Stack

| Campaign | Daily Budget | Objective | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| Profile Visit Traffic (CBO) | $75 | Profile visits | Active |
| Hammer Them — Booked-call audience | $20 | Reach/engagement | Active |
| Hammer Them — Challenge registered | $20 | Reach/engagement | Active (pre-event saturation) |
| Challenge Registration | $50 | Leads | Active through March 28 |
| **Total** | **$165/day** | — | — |

**Week 4 total ad spend:** $165/day × 10 days = ~$1,650
**Full March total:** ~$350 (Week 2) + $525 (Week 3) + $1,650 (Week 4) = ~$2,525

This is within the $1,500–$3,000 budget target.

**Nik Setting's scaling thresholds [root: Part 2.1]:**
- ROAS 10x+: Increase spend 3x
- ROAS 4–10x: Increase spend 2x
- ROAS 3–4x: Fix conversion first (profile funnel, offer, messaging) before scaling
- ROAS below 3x: Do not scale until conversion is fixed

**Deal Alert opt-in cost benchmarks:**
- Under $10/opt-in: Excellent. Scale aggressively.
- $10–$20/opt-in: Good. Maintain and test new creatives.
- $20–$40/opt-in: Acceptable early-stage. Optimize creative before scaling.
- Above $40/opt-in: Pause and fix. Either wrong audience or wrong creative.

**Jeremy Haynes Pixel Conditioning — enforced throughout [root: Part 3.2]:**
- Deal alert opt-in page is wide-top-of-funnel — pixel the confirmation for Lead events (no capital gating needed here — free trial)
- Coaching call booking confirmation page IS gated by capital qualifier — only $5K+ answers fire the Purchase-intent pixel event
- State coaching price range in any future VSL within first 60 seconds: "The coaching program is $3K–$10K depending on your tier"
- Drop-sell page (if created for smaller-ticket offer like a course or toolbox) runs on a separate pixel — never fires events to the main coaching-intent pixel
