## Risk Flags and Contingencies

**Risk 1: Setter hire doesn't work out in Week 2**
- Contingency: Do not wait. Post for a second candidate immediately. Meanwhile, Sabbo personally handles DMs for 1 hour per day (capped at that — do not let it bleed into content time).
- Critical note: the deal alert trial opt-in creates a warm email list that partially replaces setter DM volume during the gap. Anyone who opted in and didn't book can be re-engaged via email. This is the backup system.
- The waterfall math still requires 150 DMs/day at full scale. Setter is not optional — it's a matter of timing.

**Risk 2: Deal alert trial opt-ins are high but coaching calls aren't booking**
- Diagnosis: The email sequence Day 8 CTA isn't converting, or the capital qualifier is revealing a mismatch (lots of people opting in who don't have $5K+).
- Fix sequence: (1) Add a softer call to action in Day 5 email (before Day 8): "If you want to go deeper — here's a quick question for me to answer: [Typeform or DM link]." (2) On the opt-in form, add a second qualifying question: "Do you have $5K+ available for inventory in the next 90 days?" — anyone who says "No" gets a different email branch that keeps them on deal alerts but doesn't push coaching calls.

**Risk 3: Amazon FBA audience doesn't convert — low follower growth after 2 weeks of content**
- Fix: This is a hook problem. If Amazon/Keepa content isn't growing the account, run the AI hook content more aggressively. "How I use AI to find 50 profitable Amazon products per week" has a broader appeal than Keepa-specific content (AI audience is larger than dedicated Amazon seller audience).
- Secondary fix: Lean into the coaching journey and personal story content. Nik Setting's most viral content is not niche-specific — it's about the person, the journey, the proof. If the Amazon content isn't growing reach, the storytelling reels will.

**Risk 4: Challenge registers 15 but only 4 show up on Day 1**
- Fix: Pre-event Hammer Them campaign (activated Day 22) — this is specifically designed to improve show rates [root: Jeremy Haynes].
- Setter sends personal DMs to every registrant 1 hour before each session.
- Email cadence: 5 emails in 5 days before Challenge Day 1 (registration confirmation, Day 1 preview: "What you'll learn tomorrow", Day 2 preview, "Don't miss this" urgency email, same-day "we go live in 3 hours" email)
- Day 2 and Day 3 show rates will be higher than Day 1 if you execute the post-Day-1 clip + email correctly. Day 1 non-shows who receive the replay often show up on Day 2 or 3.

**Risk 5: Close rate on coaching calls under 20%**
- Per Hormozi [root: Part 6.3]: Below 30% close rate means avatar or sales process problem, not price problem. Do not lower price.
- Fix sequence: (1) Are the people booking calls actually qualified (capital $5K+, genuine desire to sell)? If not, tighten the setter qualification before booking. (2) Record 3 calls. Identify the exact moment prospects disengage — usually when price is revealed, or when they say "I need to think about it." Address that specific moment in the script.
- Common fix for coaching calls: the prospect doesn't believe the result is achievable FOR THEM specifically. Solution: more social proof before the close. Student result + "here's someone who started in exactly your situation."

**Risk 6: Content volume drops under 3 reels/week due to challenge prep pressure**
- Rule: Content creation block (8–10am) is sacred. Challenge prep happens in the afternoon block.
- Repurposing system (YouTube clip → 3 reels) means one filming session creates 4+ pieces. Challenge Day 1–3 clips create 3 more reels immediately after the event. Missing one original filming session is recoverable. Missing the repurposing system is not.

**Risk 7: Agency leads come in but Sabbo has no capacity for them in March**
- This is a good problem. Do not ignore them.
- Protocol: Setter flags any agency ICP (7-figure founder asking about growth systems, acquisition, paid ads). Sabbo personally responds. Book a call. If it's a fit, take it — but communicate clearly that primary focus is coaching in March and April intake is limited.
- Never let an agency lead go cold just because the month's primary offer is coaching. The two offers are not in conflict — they serve different ICPs and can both be served.

---

## The March Success Definition

March is successful if, on April 1st:

1. **The content machine is running on Amazon/AI/coaching** — 3+ reels per week is default, every reel either teaches Amazon sourcing, demonstrates AI tools, or shows coaching proof
2. **The 7-Day Deal Alert Trial is live and delivering** — at least 100 opt-ins on the list, deals being sent daily via automated sequence
3. **At least 1 setter is live and hitting 50/50/50 DMs daily** — primarily qualifying Amazon coaching leads, capturing not-ready leads into the deal alert trial
4. **Meta ads are live, optimized, and generating deal alert opt-ins at under $20/opt-in** — or profile visits at under $1.50 each if opt-in tracking isn't fully set up yet
5. **At least 4 coaching enrollments closed** ($15K+ in March cash collected — $20K+ if average ticket is $5K)
6. **The email list has 100+ subscribers** (primarily deal alert trial opt-ins + challenge registrants)
7. **The challenge ran** and generated at least 10 coaching call bookings
8. **Agency content exists but did not dominate** — maximum 2–3 pieces posted, none replacing primary Amazon/AI weekly content
9. **The AI sourcing pipeline is documented on camera** — at least 2 pieces of content where the actual pipeline running is visible. Not described. Shown.
10. **The brain update is done** — every learning from March is documented in brain.md, setter playbook is updated, content calendar learnings are logged

April's job is to double the inputs. March's job is to build the machine that April runs on — and that machine runs on Amazon FBA coaching, AI sourcing tools, and the proof that the system produces real results.

The agency will have its moment. When it does, it will benefit from the audience trust, the content library, and the proof-of-competence that March's coaching content built. The right offer at the wrong time fails. The right offer at the right time compounds.

Amazon FBA coaching, powered by AI, documented in public — that is March.

> "Business is a game of attrition. If you stay in the game through the point where it's really difficult, it starts to get easier." — Ben Bader
